DEVELOPMENTAL PSYCHOLOGY
EXAM 1
1. Developmental psychology is best defined as the scientific study of:
  A. abnormal behavior from childhood to adolescence
  B. change and stability across the life span
  C. hereditary transmission of traits

 D. psychological testing in school settings
       Answer: B. change and stability across the life span
  Rationale: Developmental psychology examines patterns of growth, decline, and continuity
across the entire lifespan, not just isolated stages or functions.

2. Which statement best reflects the life-span perspective?
  A. Development ends when biological maturity is reached
  B. Early childhood determines all later outcomes
  C. Development involves gains and losses throughout life

 D. Only childhood and adolescence are true developmental periods
       Answer: C. Development involves gains and losses throughout life
  Rationale: The life-span perspective emphasizes that development is lifelong, multidirectional,
and includes both growth and decline.

3. Which of the following is the best example of a normative age-graded influence?
  A. Entering puberty
  B. Experiencing a volcanic eruption
  C. Sudden loss of a parent

 D. Winning a national lottery
       Answer: A. Entering puberty
  Rationale: Normative age-graded influences are biological and environmental events that
occur at predictable ages, such as puberty.

4. A developmentalist who examines how family, school, culture, and historical context shape
behavior is most closely aligned with which perspective?

  A. Psychoanalytic
  B. Contextual
  C. Behavioral genetics

 D. Trait theory
       Answer: B. Contextual
  Rationale: Contextual perspectives emphasize the interaction of individuals with multiple
environmental systems across time.

5. Which research design is most vulnerable to cohort effects?
  A. Longitudinal
  B. Cross-sectional
  C. Sequential

 D. Experimental
       Answer: B. Cross-sectional
  Rationale: Cross-sectional designs compare different age groups at one time, making results
susceptible to cohort differences rather than true developmental change.

6. A researcher wants to determine whether sleep deprivation causes poorer memory
performance in adolescents. Which method is most appropriate?

  A. Naturalistic observation
  B. Correlational design
  C. Experiment

 D. Case study
       Answer: C. Experiment
  Rationale: Experimental methods allow manipulation of variables and control of confounds,
enabling causal conclusions.

7. Piaget viewed children as:
  A. passive recipients of reinforcement
  B. active constructors of knowledge
  C. driven mainly by unconscious conflicts

 D. shaped entirely by language
       Answer: B. active constructors of knowledge
  Rationale: Piaget emphasized that children actively construct knowledge through interaction
with their environment.

8. Vygotsky emphasized that cognitive growth occurs primarily through:
  A. maturation of reflexes
  B. reinforcement contingencies
  C. social interaction and guided participation

 D. psychosexual conflict resolution
       Answer: C. social interaction and guided participation
  Rationale: Vygotsky highlighted the importance of social interaction and cultural tools in
cognitive development.

9. The stage of prenatal development during which major organs begin to form is the:
  A. germinal stage
  B. embryonic stage
  C. fetal stage

 D. neonatal stage
       Answer: B. embryonic stage
  Rationale: Organogenesis occurs during the embryonic period, making it a critical stage of
development.

10. A fertilized ovum that has not yet implanted in the uterine wall is called a:
   A. fetus
   B. embryo
   C. zygote
 D. blastocyst
       Answer: C. zygote
   Rationale: The zygote is the earliest stage immediately following fertilization before
implantation.

11. Which statement about sex determination is correct?
   A. The mother's ovum determines whether the child will be male or female
   B. The father's sperm determines chromosomal sex
   C. Sex is determined only after implantation

 D. Hormones alone determine chromosomal sex
       Answer: B. The father's sperm determines chromosomal sex
   Rationale: The sperm carries either an X or Y chromosome, determining biological sex at
fertilization.

12. A trait controlled by multiple genes is said to follow:
   A. recessive inheritance
   B. sex-linked inheritance
   C. polygenic inheritance

 D. incomplete dominance only
       Answer: C. polygenic inheritance
   Rationale: Polygenic traits result from the combined effects of multiple genes.

13. Down syndrome is most commonly associated with:
   A. mutation in a single dominant gene
   B. trisomy involving chromosome 21
   C. missing sex chromosome

 D. X-linked recessive inheritance
       Answer: B. trisomy involving chromosome 21
   Rationale: Down syndrome results from an extra copy of chromosome 21.

14. Which maternal condition poses the greatest risk for fetal alcohol spectrum disorders?
   A. Moderate caffeine intake
   B. Prenatal exercise
   C. Heavy alcohol use during pregnancy

 D. Increased folic acid intake
       Answer: C. Heavy alcohol use during pregnancy
   Rationale: Alcohol is a teratogen that disrupts fetal brain and physical development.

15. A teratogen is:
   A. a hereditary disorder with no environmental basis
   B. an environmental agent that can interfere with prenatal development
   C. a postnatal infection acquired during labor

 D. a reflex that promotes newborn survival
       Answer: B. an environmental agent that can interfere with prenatal development
   Rationale: Teratogens are harmful external agents affecting prenatal growth.

16. The principle that development proceeds from the head downward is called:
   A. proximodistal development
   B. cephalocaudal development
   C. epigenetic progression

 D. hierarchical integration
       Answer: B. cephalocaudal development
   Rationale: Cephalocaudal pattern describes head-to-tail growth.

17. Low birth weight is defined as birth weight below:
   A. 4.5 kilograms
   B. 3.5 kilograms
   C. 2.5 kilograms

 D. 1.5 kilograms
       Answer: C. 2.5 kilograms
   Rationale: The standard cutoff for low birth weight is 2,500 grams.

18. Which newborn assessment commonly uses measures such as heart rate, muscle tone, and
reflex irritability?

   A. Stanford-Binet
   B. Apgar scale
   C. Bayley Scales

 D. Denver II
       Answer: B. Apgar scale
   Rationale: The Apgar scale evaluates newborn physical condition immediately after birth.

19. The disappearance of a response after repeated presentation of the same stimulus is called:
   A. conditioning
   B. accommodation
   C. habituation

 D. generalization
       Answer: C. habituation
   Rationale: Habituation reflects decreased responsiveness to repeated stimuli.

20. In Piaget's sensorimotor stage, object permanence refers to understanding that:
   A. objects are named by language
   B. hidden objects continue to exist
   C. all objects can be used symbolically

 D. objects remain unchanged in size
       Answer: B. hidden objects continue to exist
   Rationale: Object permanence is recognizing that objects still exist even when out of sight.
21. A baby who shakes a rattle because the sound is interesting is showing:

A. primary circular reaction
B. secondary circular reaction
C. deferred imitation

D. social referencing
    Answer: B. secondary circular reaction
Rationale: Repeating actions to produce interesting external effects defines secondary circular
reactions.

22. The psychologist most associated with the sensorimotor stage is:

A. Skinner
B. Erikson
C. Piaget

D. Kohlberg
    Answer: C. Piaget
Rationale: Piaget developed the sensorimotor stage theory.

23. Chomsky proposed that children are biologically prepared for language through a:

A. behavior chain
B. language acquisition device
C. moral grammar

D. reinforcement schedule
    Answer: B. language acquisition device
Rationale: Chomsky proposed an innate mechanism for language learning.

24. "Overextension" in early speech refers to:

A. failure to use gestures
B. using one word too narrowly
C. using one word too broadly

D. repeating adult speech exactly
    Answer: C. using one word too broadly
Rationale: Overextension involves applying a word to too many objects.

25. A toddler sees a dog, looks at the parent's fearful face, and then withdraws. This is an
example of:

A. deferred imitation
B. social referencing
C. mutual regulation
D. separation protest
 Answer: B. social referencing

Rationale: Children look to caregivers' emotional cues to guide behavior.

26. According to Erikson, the central psychosocial task of infancy is:

A. autonomy versus shame and doubt
B. initiative versus guilt
C. trust versus mistrust

D. identity versus role confusion
    Answer: C. trust versus mistrust
Rationale: Infants develop trust when caregivers are consistent and responsive.

27. The attachment pattern characterized by distress at separation and ambivalent behavior at
reunion is:

A. secure
B. avoidant
C. resistant/ambivalent

D. disorganized only in adolescence
    Answer: C. resistant/ambivalent
Rationale: This attachment involves distress and inconsistent caregiver responses.

28. Temperament refers to:

A. learned social roles
B. biologically based emotional style
C. unconscious wishes

D. parental discipline strategy
    Answer: B. biologically based emotional style
Rationale: Temperament reflects innate emotional reactivity and regulation.

29. Preschool children's difficulty understanding that others may hold beliefs different from their
own is most closely related to limitations in:

A. object permanence
B. theory of mind
C. conservation

D. autobiographical memory
    Answer: B. theory of mind
Rationale: Understanding others' perspectives develops during early childhood.

30. Piaget described early childhood as the stage of:

A. concrete operations
B. formal operations
C. preoperational thought

D. sensorimotor intelligence
    Answer: C. preoperational thought
Rationale: This stage includes symbolic thinking but limited logic.

31. A child says that a taller glass contains more water even after equal amounts are poured
from identical containers. This error shows lack of:

   A. reversibility
   B. symbolic function
   C. seriation

 D. hypothetico-deductive reasoning
       Answer: A. reversibility
   Rationale: The child cannot mentally reverse the transformation, which is required to
understand conservation.

32. Vygotsky's zone of proximal development refers to tasks that:
   A. are impossible for the child to learn
   B. the child can do alone without difficulty
   C. the child can master with guidance

 D. depend only on maturation
       Answer: C. the child can master with guidance
   Rationale: The zone of proximal development includes tasks achievable with assistance from
more skilled individuals.

33. Private speech in early childhood is best understood as:
   A. evidence of egocentrism only
   B. immature language that should be discouraged
   C. self-guiding speech that supports problem solving

 D. a sign of language delay
       Answer: C. self-guiding speech that supports problem solving
   Rationale: Private speech helps children regulate their behavior and thinking during tasks.

34. Which parenting style is generally associated with the most favorable developmental
outcomes?

   A. Authoritarian
   B. Permissive
   C. Authoritative

 D. Neglectful
       Answer: C. Authoritative
   Rationale: Authoritative parenting combines warmth and control, promoting competence and
independence.

35. According to Erikson, the major psychosocial crisis in early childhood is:
   A. trust versus mistrust
   B. initiative versus guilt
   C. industry versus inferiority

 D. autonomy versus shame and doubt
       Answer: B. initiative versus guilt
   Rationale: Children develop initiative by engaging in purposeful activities during early
childhood.

36. Play that involves make-believe and role enactment is called:
   A. functional play
   B. rough-and-tumble play
   C. dramatic or pretend play

 D. parallel play
       Answer: C. dramatic or pretend play
   Rationale: Pretend play involves symbolic role-taking and imagination.

37. Which is the best example of induction in discipline?
   A. Hitting a child immediately after misbehavior
   B. Removing all privileges indefinitely
   C. Explaining how the child's behavior affected another person

 D. Ignoring the child until compliance occurs
       Answer: C. Explaining how the child's behavior affected another person
   Rationale: Induction teaches children empathy by highlighting consequences of their actions.

38. A child who can identify the self using stable traits such as "I am helpful" or "I am good at
drawing" is showing growth in:

   A. self-concept
   B. object permanence
   C. delayed imitation

 D. gender constancy
       Answer: A. self-concept
   Rationale: Self-concept develops as children begin describing themselves using stable
characteristics.

39. Piaget's concrete operational child is most likely able to:
   A. think only in reflexive patterns
   B. solve abstract propositions with ease
   C. conserve quantity and classify hierarchically

 D. reason well about hypothetical worlds
       Answer: C. conserve quantity and classify hierarchically
   Rationale: Concrete operational thinking allows logical reasoning about tangible objects and
conservation tasks.

40. The ability to arrange items in order along a dimension, such as shortest to tallest, is called:
   A. centration
   B. seriation
   C. transduction

 D. animism
       Answer: B. seriation
   Rationale: Seriation involves ordering objects along a quantitative dimension.

41. Metamemory refers to:
   A. memory loss in middle childhood
   B. memory for motor acts
   C. knowledge about how memory works

 D. unconscious memory storage
       Answer: C. knowledge about how memory works
   Rationale: Metamemory is awareness and understanding of memory processes.

42. Sternberg's triarchic theory includes analytic, creative, and:
   A. fluid intelligence
   B. crystallized intelligence
   C. practical intelligence

 D. moral intelligence
       Answer: C. practical intelligence
   Rationale: Practical intelligence refers to real-world problem-solving ability.

43. A child who uses rehearsal or organization to remember information is demonstrating:
   A. executive dysfunction
   B. mnemonic strategy use
   C. egocentric speech

 D. sensory memory only
       Answer: B. mnemonic strategy use
   Rationale: Strategies like rehearsal improve memory performance.

44. According to Erikson, the key psychosocial issue in middle childhood is:
   A. industry versus inferiority
   B. initiative versus guilt
   C. autonomy versus shame and doubt

 D. intimacy versus isolation
       Answer: A. industry versus inferiority
   Rationale: Children develop competence through productive activities.

45. Repeated peer aggression involving a power imbalance is called:
   A. assertiveness
   B. sociometric rejection
   C. bullying
   D. co-regulation
  Answer: C. bullying

   Rationale: Bullying involves repeated aggression and unequal power.

46. A child who is well-liked by many peers and disliked by few would most likely be classified
as:

   A. neglected
   B. controversial
   C. popular

 D. rejected
       Answer: C. popular
   Rationale: Popular children receive high positive and low negative peer nominations.

47. Resilience is best described as:
   A. absence of stress exposure
   B. automatic recovery without support
   C. positive adaptation despite adversity

 D. genetic immunity to psychopathology
       Answer: C. positive adaptation despite adversity
   Rationale: Resilience refers to successful adaptation despite challenges.

48. Which family factor is most consistently linked to better child adjustment after divorce?
   A. High interparental conflict
   B. Consistent warmth and effective parenting
   C. Frequent triangulation

 D. Parentification of the child
       Answer: B. Consistent warmth and effective parenting
   Rationale: Supportive parenting buffers children from stress after divorce.

49. Puberty refers to:
   A. attainment of legal adulthood
   B. period of rapid hormonal and physical sexual maturation
   C. end of brain development

 D. achievement of identity
       Answer: B. period of rapid hormonal and physical sexual maturation
   Rationale: Puberty involves biological changes leading to sexual maturity.

50. Menarche is:
   A. first ejaculation
   B. first ovulation
   C. first menstrual period

 D. onset of breast development
       Answer: C. first menstrual period
   Rationale: Menarche marks the beginning of menstruation.
51. One hallmark of adolescent egocentrism is the:
   A. conservation error
   B. imaginary audience
   C. stranger anxiety

 D. deferred imitation
       Answer: B. imaginary audience
   Rationale: Adolescents believe others are constantly observing them.

52. Piaget held that adolescents enter the stage of:
   A. preconventional morality
   B. formal operations
   C. concrete operations

 D. postformal thought
       Answer: B. formal operations
   Rationale: Adolescents develop abstract and hypothetical thinking.

53. The ability to generate hypotheses and test them systematically is:
   A. transductive reasoning
   B. social referencing
   C. hypothetical-deductive reasoning

 D. practical intelligence
       Answer: C. hypothetical-deductive reasoning
   Rationale: This is a key feature of formal operational thinking.

54. According to Kohlberg, reasoning based on social approval and law-and-order concerns is
characteristic of:

   A. preconventional morality
   B. conventional morality
   C. postconventional morality

 D. autonomous morality only
       Answer: B. conventional morality
   Rationale: Conventional morality focuses on maintaining social order and gaining approval.

55. Gilligan argued that traditional theories of moral development underemphasized:
   A. logic
   B. justice
   C. care and responsibility in relationships

 D. reinforcement history
       Answer: C. care and responsibility in relationships
   Rationale: Gilligan emphasized an ethic of care.

56. Marcia described identity development using the dimensions of:
   A. attachment and trust
   B. crisis/exploration and commitment
   C. autonomy and intimacy

 D. initiative and guilt
       Answer: B. crisis/exploration and commitment
   Rationale: Identity status depends on exploration and commitment.

57. An adolescent who has explored alternatives and made definite choices about beliefs and
goals is in identity:

   A. diffusion
   B. foreclosure
   C. moratorium

 D. achievement
       Answer: D. achievement
   Rationale: Identity achievement reflects both exploration and commitment.

58. Which parenting pattern is generally associated with the most favorable adolescent
outcomes?

   A. Authoritative
   B. Rejecting
   C. Coercive

 D. Inconsistent permissiveness
       Answer: A. Authoritative
   Rationale: Balanced parenting promotes autonomy and competence.

59. Which adolescent is at greatest risk for delinquent behavior?
   A. One with strong school bonding and prosocial peers
   B. One with effective parental monitoring and supportive adults
   C. One with deviant peers and weak family supervision

 D. One with high academic engagement and sports involvement
       Answer: C. One with deviant peers and weak family supervision
   Rationale: Risk increases with negative peer influence and poor supervision.

60. The term "sexting" refers to:
   A. early sexual maturation
   B. digital transmission of sexual messages or images
   C. sex education in schools

 D. online identity diffusion only
       Answer: B. digital transmission of sexual messages or images
   Rationale: Sexting involves sharing sexual content electronically.

61. Arnett used the term "emerging adulthood" to refer roughly to:
   A. ages 10 to 14
   B. ages 15 to 18
   C. late teens through twenties in many industrialized societies
   D. ages 30 to 40
  Answer: C. late teens through twenties in many industrialized societies

   Rationale: Emerging adulthood is a distinct developmental period characterized by
exploration in identity, work, and relationships.

62. Which characteristic is most typical of emerging adulthood?
   A. Immediate assumption of stable adult roles in all cultures
   B. Exploration of identity, work, and relationships
   C. Complete psychosocial maturity by age 18

 D. Total independence from parents in all settings
       Answer: B. Exploration of identity, work, and relationships
   Rationale: This period is marked by instability and exploration before settling into adult roles.

63. Sternberg's triangular theory of love includes intimacy, passion, and:
   A. attachment
   B. fidelity
   C. commitment

 D. sacrifice
       Answer: C. commitment
   Rationale: Commitment completes the three components of love in Sternberg's theory.

64. A couple living together without being legally married are:
   A. separated
   B. remarried
   C. cohabiting

 D. disengaged
       Answer: C. cohabiting
   Rationale: Cohabitation refers to partners living together without legal marriage.

65. Which factor is commonly associated with better adjustment to marriage and parenthood?
   A. Unrealistic expectations and low communication
   B. Chronic role conflict with no support
   C. Flexibility, communication, and shared responsibility

 D. Financial secrecy and rigid gender expectations
       Answer: C. Flexibility, communication, and shared responsibility
   Rationale: Healthy relationships rely on communication and shared roles.

66. Emotional intelligence refers primarily to the ability to:
   A. raise IQ through training
   B. understand and regulate emotions
   C. memorize emotional words

 D. suppress all negative affect
       Answer: B. understand and regulate emotions
   Rationale: Emotional intelligence involves recognizing and managing emotions effectively.
67. Fluid intelligence refers to:
   A. accumulated knowledge
   B. school grades only
   C. ability to solve novel problems

 D. motor coordination
       Answer: C. ability to solve novel problems
   Rationale: Fluid intelligence involves reasoning and problem-solving in new situations.

68. Crystallized intelligence refers to:
   A. genetic endowment alone
   B. stored knowledge and verbal skill
   C. rapid processing only

 D. nonverbal reasoning in infants
       Answer: B. stored knowledge and verbal skill
   Rationale: Crystallized intelligence reflects accumulated knowledge over time.

69. Which is the best example of postformal or mature adult thought?
   A. Insisting every issue has one correct answer
   B. Rejecting contradiction as impossible
   C. Integrating logic with experience and context

 D. Thinking only in concrete terms
       Answer: C. Integrating logic with experience and context
   Rationale: Mature thinking considers multiple perspectives and contextual factors.

70. In many societies, transition to adult work and family roles is influenced strongly by:
   A. reflex development
   B. historical and cultural context
   C. fixed universal age deadlines only

 D. test scores alone
       Answer: B. historical and cultural context
   Rationale: Developmental timing is shaped by sociocultural conditions.

71. Menopause refers to:
   A. first menstrual period
   B. cessation of ovulation and menstruation
   C. decline in testosterone only

 D. end of sexuality
       Answer: B. cessation of ovulation and menstruation
   Rationale: Menopause marks the end of reproductive capability in women.

72. Which statement about middle adulthood is most accurate?
   A. All adults experience a severe midlife crisis
   B. Midlife is uniformly a period of decline
   C. Midlife can involve both loss and growth
 D. Personality becomes completely unstable
       Answer: C. Midlife can involve both loss and growth
   Rationale: Midlife includes both challenges and opportunities for development.

73. According to Horn and Cattell, which ability tends to be better maintained with age and
experience?

   A. Fluid intelligence
   B. Crystallized intelligence
   C. Sensory memory

 D. Processing speed
       Answer: B. Crystallized intelligence
   Rationale: Knowledge-based abilities are maintained or even improve with age.

74. Expertise in middle adulthood often compensates for slower processing by:
   A. eliminating the need for memory
   B. relying on deep domain-specific knowledge
   C. preventing any cognitive decline

 D. reducing the influence of practice
       Answer: B. relying on deep domain-specific knowledge
   Rationale: Experts use experience and organized knowledge to maintain performance.

75. Erikson described the central psychosocial task of middle adulthood as:
   A. ego integrity versus despair
   B. intimacy versus isolation
   C. generativity versus stagnation

 D. industry versus inferiority
       Answer: C. generativity versus stagnation
   Rationale: Adults seek to contribute to the next generation.

76. Generativity is best expressed in which behavior?
   A. Withdrawing from society
   B. Investing in guiding the next generation
   C. Avoiding responsibility

 D. Rejecting work and family roles
       Answer: B. Investing in guiding the next generation
   Rationale: Generativity involves mentoring, parenting, and societal contribution.

77. The "empty nest" generally refers to:
   A. infertility in middle adulthood
   B. loss of occupational role
   C. children leaving the parental home

 D. widowhood
       Answer: C. children leaving the parental home
   Rationale: The empty nest occurs when children move out.
78. Caring simultaneously for adolescent or adult children and aging parents is often described
as:

   A. identity foreclosure
   B. sandwich generation experience
   C. disengagement

 D. selective optimization
       Answer: B. sandwich generation experience
   Rationale: This describes adults caring for two generations at once.

79. Which factor is most strongly linked to well-being in long-term midlife relationships?
   A. Constant idealization without conflict
   B. Marital quality rather than marital status alone
   C. Economic dependence only

 D. Absence of all role strain
       Answer: B. Marital quality rather than marital status alone
   Rationale: Relationship satisfaction predicts well-being more than status alone.

80. Identity process in midlife is best characterized by:
   A. absolute stability with no revision
   B. continuing adaptation and reinterpretation of the self
   C. elimination of all earlier commitments

 D. complete dependence on biology
       Answer: B. continuing adaptation and reinterpretation of the self
   Rationale: Identity continues evolving through life experiences.

81. Presbyopia refers to:
   A. age-related hearing loss
   B. clouding of the lens
   C. difficulty focusing on near objects

 D. irreversible optic nerve damage
       Answer: C. difficulty focusing on near objects
   Rationale: Presbyopia affects near vision due to lens stiffness.

82. Which theory proposes that aging results partly from accumulated damage from wear,
toxins, or cellular error?

   A. Variable-rate theory
   B. Psychoanalytic theory
   C. Attachment theory

 D. Social learning theory
       Answer: A. Variable-rate theory
   Rationale: Biological aging is partly due to accumulated damage over time.

83. Selective optimization with compensation refers to:
   A. denying age-related change
   B. maximizing all activities equally
   C. focusing on priorities and compensating for losses

 D. avoiding social participation
       Answer: C. focusing on priorities and compensating for losses
   Rationale: Older adults adapt by prioritizing strengths and compensating for declines.

84. Wisdom in late adulthood is best understood as:
   A. perfect memory for facts
   B. superior sensorimotor speed
   C. expert knowledge in the pragmatics of life

 D. immunity from emotional distress
       Answer: C. expert knowledge in the pragmatics of life
   Rationale: Wisdom involves practical judgment and life insight.

85. Erikson's final psychosocial crisis is:
   A. intimacy versus isolation
   B. ego integrity versus despair
   C. initiative versus guilt

 D. autonomy versus shame and doubt
       Answer: B. ego integrity versus despair
   Rationale: Older adults evaluate their life with acceptance or regret.

86. Which situation best reflects ageism?
   A. Providing accessible services to older adults
   B. Assuming all older adults are frail, forgetful, and resistant to change
   C. Encouraging active aging

 D. Adapting communication to sensory needs
       Answer: B. Assuming all older adults are frail, forgetful, and resistant to change
   Rationale: Ageism involves stereotyping and discrimination based on age.

87. Disengagement theory proposes that:
   A. older adults thrive by maximizing social roles
   B. aging involves mutual withdrawal between person and society
   C. social support becomes irrelevant in old age

 D. loneliness is biologically predetermined
       Answer: B. aging involves mutual withdrawal between person and society
   Rationale: The theory suggests reduced interaction between older adults and society.

88. Activity theory would predict greater satisfaction in late adulthood when older adults:
   A. remain socially and psychologically engaged
   B. sever most social ties
   C. avoid meaningful roles
   D. depend entirely on institutions
  Answer: A. remain socially and psychologically engaged

   Rationale: Active engagement supports well-being in old age.

89. Which loss is often associated with the greatest long-term adjustment challenge in late
adulthood?

   A. Loss of a favorite television program
   B. Loss of a spouse
   C. Loss of a recreational hobby

 D. Loss of an outdated work title
       Answer: B. Loss of a spouse
   Rationale: Spousal loss has profound emotional and adjustment impact.

90. Kubler-Ross's framework is most commonly associated with:
   A. attachment categories
   B. stages of grief and reactions to dying
   C. moral development

 D. intelligence testing
       Answer: B. stages of grief and reactions to dying
   Rationale: Kubler-Ross described emotional responses to death and dying.

91. A psychometrician is asked to conduct psychotherapy for an adolescent with depression in a
routine outpatient setting. The best response is to:

   A. provide therapy independently if the family insists
   B. provide therapy only if no psychologist is available anywhere
   C. decline the therapy role and refer appropriately, unless it is an emergency situation

 D. proceed as long as the client signs consent
       Answer: C. decline the therapy role and refer appropriately, unless it is an emergency
situation
   Rationale: Scope of practice limits psychometricians from independently providing
psychotherapy.

92. A psychometrician administers a psychological test without required supervision and
interprets results independently. The main ethical issue is:

   A. overemphasis on confidentiality
   B. practice beyond professional boundaries
   C. excessive use of informed consent

 D. failure to use a projective test
       Answer: B. practice beyond professional boundaries
   Rationale: Practicing beyond defined roles violates ethical and legal standards.

93. A school requests raw test data from a psychometrician. The best action is to:
   A. release all materials immediately
   B. release only summaries to anyone
   C. protect test data and release only to authorized individuals
 D. post results publicly
       Answer: C. protect test data and release only to authorized individuals
   Rationale: Confidentiality and test security must be maintained.

94. During teleassessment, disruptions affect test performance. The ethical response is to:
   A. ignore the issue
   B. continue without noting it
   C. document limitations and consider effects on validity

 D. adjust scores arbitrarily
       Answer: C. document limitations and consider effects on validity
   Rationale: Test validity must be preserved and limitations reported.

95. Sharing identifiable client information in class violates:
   A. beneficence only
   B. test standardization
   C. confidentiality and privacy

 D. informed assent
       Answer: C. confidentiality and privacy
   Rationale: Client identity must be protected.

96. A practitioner notices unethical test use by a colleague. The best response is to:
   A. ignore it
   B. consider appropriate action and resolve if possible
   C. publicly shame the colleague

 D. immediately report without basis
       Answer: B. consider appropriate action and resolve if possible
   Rationale: Ethical practice requires appropriate and proportional response.

97. Delegating testing to an untrained assistant is unethical because:
   A. delegation is never allowed
   B. tasks must only be delegated to competent individuals
   C. assistants can only schedule

 D. two psychologists are always required
       Answer: B. tasks must only be delegated to competent individuals
   Rationale: Delegation requires proper training and supervision.

98. A client chooses to terminate therapy early. The ethical response is to:
   A. threaten consequences
   B. deny termination
   C. respect the client's right while discussing implications

 D. disclose information to family
       Answer: C. respect the client's right while discussing implications
   Rationale: Clients have autonomy to terminate services.
99. Leaving test protocols unsecured violates:
   A. social desirability
   B. confidentiality and test security
   C. interpretation norms

 D. informed refusal
       Answer: B. confidentiality and test security
   Rationale: Secure handling of materials is required.

100. Before conducting a court-ordered assessment, the practitioner should:
    A. assume full confidentiality
    B. clarify role, purpose, and limits of confidentiality
    C. promise secrecy

 D. skip explanation
        Answer: B. clarify role, purpose, and limits of confidentiality
    Rationale: Third-party assessments require clear informed consent and role clarification.
DEVELOPMENTAL PSYCHOLOGY
EXAM 2
DEVELOPMENTAL PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 2

1. Which statement best reflects the life-span perspective in development?
  A. Development ends once biological maturity is reached.
  B. Development is limited to childhood because growth is most visible then.
  C. Development involves lifelong patterns of change and stability.

 D. Development is determined almost entirely by heredity.
       Answer: C. Development involves lifelong patterns of change and stability.
  Rationale: Development is viewed as a continuous process from conception to death,
involving both gains and losses across all stages.

2. A developmental psychologist studying how poverty, parenting, and school quality interact in
shaping cognition is most directly examining:

  A. a single maturation timetable
  B. interrelated contextual influences
  C. only hereditary transmission

 D. reflexive behavior
       Answer: B. interrelated contextual influences
  Rationale: Development is influenced by multiple interacting environmental systems rather
than a single isolated factor.

3. Which is the best example of a normative age-graded influence?
  A. Experiencing a major earthquake
  B. Beginning menopause in midlife
  C. Being born during a pandemic

 D. Losing a parent at age 8
       Answer: B. Beginning menopause in midlife
  Rationale: Normative age-graded influences are biological or environmental events that occur
at a typical time in life.

4. Which statement best captures the difference between a critical period and a sensitive
period?

  A. A critical period is longer than a sensitive period.
  B. A critical period requires social learning; a sensitive period does not.
  C. A critical period is a narrowly defined time when an event must occur, whereas a sensitive
period is a time of heightened responsiveness.

 D. A critical period applies only to language and a sensitive period applies only to attachment.
       Answer: C. A critical period is a narrowly defined time when an event must occur, whereas
a sensitive period is a time of heightened responsiveness.
  Rationale: Critical periods require specific experiences at a precise time, while sensitive
periods allow more flexibility but optimal learning occurs within them.

5. A theorist who emphasizes unconscious motivation and early experience would most likely
belong to which perspective?
  A. Psychoanalytic
  B. Information-processing
  C. Behaviorist

 D. Contextual
       Answer: A. Psychoanalytic
  Rationale: Psychoanalytic theory focuses on unconscious processes and early childhood
experiences as determinants of behavior.

6. The concept of the zone of proximal development is most closely associated with:
  A. Piaget
  B. Erikson
  C. Vygotsky

 D. Bandura
       Answer: C. Vygotsky
  Rationale: Vygotsky proposed that learning occurs through guided support within a child's
zone of proximal development.

7. In developmental research, a major advantage of longitudinal designs is that they:
  A. avoid attrition completely
  B. can directly show individual patterns of change over time
  C. are always faster than cross-sectional studies

 D. eliminate cohort effects entirely
       Answer: B. can directly show individual patterns of change over time
  Rationale: Longitudinal studies track the same individuals, allowing observation of
developmental changes within the same participants.

8. A researcher compares 8-year-olds, 18-year-olds, and 68-year-olds at one point in time. This
is a:

  A. longitudinal design
  B. sequential design
  C. cross-sectional design

 D. microgenetic design
       Answer: C. cross-sectional design
  Rationale: Cross-sectional research compares different age groups at a single point in time.

9. Which research method is most appropriate when the goal is to understand how participants
make sense of bereavement in their own words?

  A. Qualitative interview
  B. Randomized controlled trial
  C. Twin study

 D. Standardized intelligence test
       Answer: A. Qualitative interview
  Rationale: Qualitative interviews capture subjective meanings and personal experiences such
as grief.
10. Which ethical principle is most central when a researcher ensures that participants fully
understand risks before joining a study?

   A. Debriefing
   B. Standardization
   C. Informed consent

 D. Random assignment
       Answer: C. Informed consent
   Rationale: Informed consent ensures participants understand procedures, risks, and their
rights before participation.

(Continuing in same format...)

11. Which pair correctly distinguishes genotype from phenotype?
   A. Genotype is observable traits; phenotype is genetic makeup.
   B. Genotype is inherited potential; phenotype is its observable expression.
   C. Genotype is environmental influence; phenotype is biological inheritance.

 D. Genotype is dominant traits only; phenotype is recessive traits only.
       Answer: B. Genotype is inherited potential; phenotype is its observable expression.
   Rationale: Genotype refers to genetic makeup, while phenotype is the observable result
influenced by environment.

12. When both parents are carriers for an autosomal recessive disorder, the child will express
the disorder only if the child:

   A. inherits one recessive allele
   B. inherits two dominant alleles
   C. inherits two recessive alleles

 D. is male
       Answer: C. inherits two recessive alleles
   Rationale: Autosomal recessive conditions require two copies of the recessive gene to be
expressed.

13. Down syndrome is most commonly associated with:
   A. trisomy 21
   B. a recessive sex-linked gene
   C. a dominant autosomal mutation

 D. genomic imprinting only
       Answer: A. trisomy 21
   Rationale: Down syndrome results from an extra chromosome 21.

14. Which statement best illustrates canalization?
   A. A trait is unaffected by genes.
   B. Development follows a strongly programmed path unless environmental forces are

extreme.
   C. Children inherit all emotional tendencies directly from one parent.

 D. Prenatal growth proceeds randomly.
       Answer: B. Development follows a strongly programmed path unless environmental forces
are extreme.
   Rationale: Canalization refers to traits that develop predictably unless disrupted by strong
environmental factors.

15. A fetus is most vulnerable to teratogens during the embryonic period because this is when:
   A. organ systems are forming rapidly
   B. reflexes are already well established
   C. fetal learning has reached maturity

 D. language begins to emerge
       Answer: A. organ systems are forming rapidly
   Rationale: Organogenesis occurs during the embryonic stage, making it highly sensitive to
teratogens.

16. Which maternal factor poses a significant prenatal risk because it can directly reduce
oxygen available to the fetus?

   A. Moderate exercise
   B. Smoking
   C. Morning sickness

 D. Reading aloud
       Answer: B. Smoking
   Rationale: Smoking reduces oxygen supply to the fetus, increasing risk for low birth weight
and developmental complications.

17. Which paternal factor has been linked to developmental risk in offspring?
   A. Paternal eye color
   B. Paternal age
   C. Paternal birth order

 D. Paternal handedness only
       Answer: B. Paternal age
   Rationale: Advanced paternal age is associated with increased risk of genetic mutations
affecting development.

18. The zygote, embryo, and fetus represent:
   A. psychosocial stages
   B. three phases of prenatal development
   C. three types of twinship

 D. three patterns of temperament
       Answer: B. three phases of prenatal development
   Rationale: Prenatal development progresses through germinal (zygote), embryonic, and fetal
stages.
19. A baby born weighing below 2,500 grams is classified as:
   A. postmature
   B. low birth weight
   C. small-headed

 D. preoperational
       Answer: B. low birth weight
   Rationale: Low birth weight is defined as less than 2,500 grams at birth.

20. Which newborn assessment primarily evaluates reflexes, muscle tone, color, respiration,
and heart rate shortly after birth?

   A. Stanford-Binet
   B. Denver II
   C. Apgar scale

 D. Bayley scale
       Answer: C. Apgar scale
   Rationale: The Apgar scale assesses newborn physical condition immediately after birth.

21. Cephalocaudal development refers to growth that proceeds:
   A. from the center outward
   B. from head to toe
   C. from toe to head

 D. from the outside inward
       Answer: B. from head to toe
   Rationale: Cephalocaudal development describes progression from head downward.

22. The disappearance of many unused neural connections in early development is called:
   A. habituation
   B. assimilation
   C. synaptic pruning

 D. scaffolding
       Answer: C. synaptic pruning
   Rationale: Synaptic pruning eliminates unused neural pathways, improving efficiency.

23. According to dynamic systems theory, motor development results from:
   A. maturation alone
   B. reinforcement alone
   C. interaction among neural, muscular, perceptual, and environmental systems

 D. reflex suppression only
       Answer: C. interaction among neural, muscular, perceptual, and environmental systems
   Rationale: Motor skills emerge from coordinated interaction of multiple systems.

24. Piaget's sensorimotor stage is characterized primarily by:
   A. hypothetical reasoning
   B. symbolic algebra
   C. learning through sensory and motor activity

 D. formal moral thinking
       Answer: C. learning through sensory and motor activity
   Rationale: Infants learn through direct interaction with their environment via senses and
actions.

25. Object permanence refers to understanding that:
   A. moving objects are dangerous
   B. objects continue to exist even when out of sight
   C. all objects have names

 D. symbols and objects are identical
       Answer: B. objects continue to exist even when out of sight
   Rationale: Object permanence is a key cognitive milestone in infancy.

26. Habituation is best defined as:
   A. increased response to a repeated stimulus
   B. decreased response to a familiar repeated stimulus
   C. forming an emotional bond with a caregiver

 D. generalizing from one problem to another
       Answer: B. decreased response to a familiar repeated stimulus
   Rationale: Habituation reflects learning by reduced attention to repeated stimuli.

27. A child calls all four-legged animals "dog." This is an example of:
   A. overextension
   B. underextension
   C. telegraphic speech

 D. fast mapping
       Answer: A. overextension
   Rationale: Overextension occurs when a word is applied too broadly.

28. Noam Chomsky is best known for proposing that:
   A. language is learned only through imitation
   B. language development depends on a biologically based capacity
   C. moral development proceeds in stages

 D. attachment develops through reinforcement
       Answer: B. language development depends on a biologically based capacity
   Rationale: Chomsky proposed an innate language acquisition mechanism.

29. Which finding best supports a social-contextual view of language development?
   A. Language emerges without any social input.
   B. Caregiver-child interaction helps shape language growth.
   C. Vocabulary growth depends only on maturation.

 D. Syntax appears suddenly and independently of experience.
       Answer: B. Caregiver-child interaction helps shape language growth.
   Rationale: Social interaction plays a critical role in language acquisition.

30. In classical conditioning, learning occurs when:
   A. a behavior is strengthened by its consequences
   B. two stimuli become associated
   C. an infant mentally represents an object

 D. a child imitates a model for reward
       Answer: B. two stimuli become associated
   Rationale: Classical conditioning involves forming associations between stimuli.

31. Erikson described the central psychosocial task of infancy as:
   A. autonomy versus shame and doubt
   B. trust versus mistrust
   C. initiative versus guilt

 D. identity versus role confusion
       Answer: B. trust versus mistrust
   Rationale: Infants develop trust when caregivers are reliable and responsive.

32. Ainsworth's "securely attached" infant is most likely to:
   A. ignore the caregiver upon reunion
   B. show little distress at separation and avoid contact on reunion
   C. seek contact with the caregiver and be comforted at reunion

 D. display disorganized and contradictory behavior only
       Answer: C. seek contact with the caregiver and be comforted at reunion
   Rationale: Secure attachment is characterized by comfort and trust in the caregiver.

33. Temperament refers to:
   A. learned moral standards
   B. biologically based individual differences in emotional reactivity and self-regulation
   C. stable intelligence across the life span

 D. attachment to siblings
       Answer: B. biologically based individual differences in emotional reactivity and
self-regulation
   Rationale: Temperament reflects innate differences in emotional style.

34. Social referencing occurs when an infant:
   A. names familiar objects
   B. uses another person's emotional reaction to guide behavior
   C. shows object permanence

 D. imitates sounds without meaning
       Answer: B. uses another person's emotional reaction to guide behavior
   Rationale: Infants look to caregivers' cues to interpret unfamiliar situations.

35. The emergence of autonomy in toddlerhood is most closely linked to:
   A. shame over fantasy play
   B. efforts at self-control and independent action
   C. mastery of formal logic

 D. pubertal timing
       Answer: B. efforts at self-control and independent action
   Rationale: Toddlers strive for independence and self-regulation.

36. Nonorganic failure to thrive is most strongly associated with:
   A. inherited endocrine disease only
   B. severe neglect and disturbed caregiving
   C. early symbolic play

 D. excessive peer contact
       Answer: B. severe neglect and disturbed caregiving
   Rationale: It often results from emotional and environmental deprivation.

37. In Piaget's theory, preoperational children are especially likely to show:
   A. reversible thinking
   B. egocentrism and centration
   C. formal operational logic

 D. abstract propositional reasoning
       Answer: B. egocentrism and centration
   Rationale: Preoperational thought is limited by inability to consider multiple perspectives.

38. Conservation tasks assess whether children understand that:
   A. all people think the same way
   B. quantity remains the same despite changes in appearance
   C. rules should never be broken

 D. memory is permanent
       Answer: B. quantity remains the same despite changes in appearance
   Rationale: Conservation reflects logical reasoning about physical properties.

39. Theory of mind refers to understanding that:
   A. the brain stops developing in early childhood
   B. people have mental states that may differ from reality and from one another
   C. children cannot deceive before adolescence

 D. language causes intelligence
       Answer: B. people have mental states that may differ from reality and from one another
   Rationale: Theory of mind involves understanding beliefs, intentions, and perspectives.

40. Vygotsky would most likely emphasize that cognitive growth is promoted by:
   A. solitary discovery without adult guidance
   B. guided participation and scaffolding
   C. maturation independent of culture
   D. fixed IQ potential
  Answer: B. guided participation and scaffolding

   Rationale: Learning occurs through social interaction and support.

41. Private speech in early childhood is best understood as:
   A. evidence of pathology
   B. immature babbling without function
   C. a self-guiding tool for thought and behavior

 D. refusal to socialize
       Answer: C. a self-guiding tool for thought and behavior
   Rationale: Private speech helps children regulate their thinking and guide their actions during
problem-solving.

42. Which parenting style is generally linked with the most favorable developmental outcomes?
   A. Authoritarian
   B. Neglectful
   C. Permissive

 D. Authoritative
       Answer: D. Authoritative
   Rationale: Authoritative parenting combines warmth and firm control, promoting competence
and self-regulation.

43. Erikson's central conflict of early childhood is:
   A. trust versus mistrust
   B. autonomy versus shame and doubt
   C. initiative versus guilt

 D. industry versus inferiority
       Answer: C. initiative versus guilt
   Rationale: Children begin to assert control and take initiative in activities during early
childhood.

44. According to cognitive developmental views of gender, children actively:
   A. construct an understanding of gender categories
   B. inherit all gender-role preferences directly
   C. ignore social information about gender

 D. stop play once gender constancy develops
       Answer: A. construct an understanding of gender categories
   Rationale: Children actively organize and interpret gender-related information through
cognitive processes.

45. Parten's category of cooperative play involves:
   A. solitary manipulation of objects
   B. parallel activity without interaction
   C. organized play with shared goals
   D. watching others without joining
  Answer: C. organized play with shared goals

   Rationale: Cooperative play involves interaction and coordination with peers toward a
common objective.

46. In middle childhood, concrete operational thought allows children to:
   A. reason abstractly about hypothetical propositions
   B. think only in symbolic images
   C. perform mental operations on concrete objects and events

 D. abandon classification skills
       Answer: C. perform mental operations on concrete objects and events
   Rationale: Children develop logical thinking tied to real-world objects and situations.

47. Executive functioning includes:
   A. puberty and hormonal regulation
   B. planning, inhibitory control, and working memory
   C. sensory thresholds only

 D. attachment security alone
       Answer: B. planning, inhibitory control, and working memory
   Rationale: Executive functions are higher-order cognitive processes involved in
self-regulation.

48. Metamemory is:
   A. memory loss caused by stress
   B. memory for motor skills
   C. knowledge about how memory works

 D. unconscious recall of infancy
       Answer: C. knowledge about how memory works
   Rationale: Metamemory involves awareness and understanding of memory processes.

49. Sternberg's triarchic theory highlights:
   A. id, ego, and superego
   B. practical, analytical, and creative aspects of intelligence
   C. crystallized intelligence only

 D. reinforcement schedules
       Answer: B. practical, analytical, and creative aspects of intelligence
   Rationale: Sternberg proposed three types of intelligence: analytical, creative, and practical.

50. Children with learning disabilities typically:
   A. have uniformly low intelligence across all areas
   B. show specific difficulties in academic processing despite otherwise adequate opportunity to

learn
   C. cannot benefit from intervention
   D. always have sensory impairment
  Answer: B. show specific difficulties in academic processing despite otherwise adequate

opportunity to learn
   Rationale: Learning disabilities involve specific deficits, not global intellectual impairment.

51. Erikson's central issue in middle childhood is:
   A. identity versus role confusion
   B. industry versus inferiority
   C. generativity versus stagnation

 D. ego integrity versus despair
       Answer: B. industry versus inferiority
   Rationale: Children strive to develop competence and skills valued by society.

52. Co-regulation in middle childhood refers to:
   A. complete parental control
   B. shared regulation in which children gain autonomy while parents continue guidance
   C. peer enforcement of classroom rules

 D. emotional dependence on siblings only
       Answer: B. shared regulation in which children gain autonomy while parents continue
guidance
   Rationale: Co-regulation reflects gradual transfer of responsibility from parent to child.

53. Which child is at greatest risk for peer rejection?
   A. A cooperative child who shares
   B. A child who displays hostile attribution bias and aggressive behavior
   C. A child who enjoys reading alone at times

 D. A child with average athletic skill
       Answer: B. A child who displays hostile attribution bias and aggressive behavior
   Rationale: Aggressive behavior and misinterpreting others' intentions increase rejection risk.

54. Bullying is best distinguished from ordinary conflict by the presence of:
   A. accidental harm only
   B. imbalance of power and repeated aggression
   C. verbal disagreement

 D. sibling rivalry
       Answer: B. imbalance of power and repeated aggression
   Rationale: Bullying involves repeated harm and a power imbalance.

55. Puberty begins with:
   A. mastery of conservation
   B. activation of hormonal processes leading to sexual maturation
   C. onset of formal operations

 D. completion of brain myelination
       Answer: B. activation of hormonal processes leading to sexual maturation
   Rationale: Puberty is triggered by hormonal changes that lead to physical maturation.
56. Which adolescent is most likely to experience stress related to pubertal timing?
   A. A boy maturing somewhat earlier than peers, with supportive peers
   B. A girl maturing much earlier than peers in a sexualized peer environment
   C. A boy with average pubertal timing

 D. A girl whose puberty begins within the typical range and with strong support
       Answer: B. A girl maturing much earlier than peers in a sexualized peer environment
   Rationale: Early maturation in girls is linked to higher psychosocial risks.

57. Piaget's formal operational stage is marked by the capacity for:
   A. object permanence
   B. abstract and hypothetical reasoning
   C. stranger anxiety

 D. conservation of liquid only
       Answer: B. abstract and hypothetical reasoning
   Rationale: Adolescents develop the ability to think abstractly and logically.

58. Adolescent egocentrism may be expressed in the:
   A. zone of proximal development
   B. imaginary audience and personal fable
   C. secure base phenomenon

 D. social clock
       Answer: B. imaginary audience and personal fable
   Rationale: Adolescents may believe others are constantly watching them and that their
experiences are unique.

59. Kohlberg's theory focuses on development of:
   A. attachment
   B. moral reasoning
   C. psychosexual identity

 D. motor coordination
       Answer: B. moral reasoning
   Rationale: Kohlberg studied how individuals reason about moral dilemmas.

60. Gilligan argued that some moral reasoning is better understood through an emphasis on:
   A. operant conditioning
   B. care and relationships
   C. object permanence

 D. fluid intelligence
       Answer: B. care and relationships
   Rationale: Gilligan emphasized an ethic of care rather than justice alone.

61. Marcia's identity status characterized by exploration without commitment is:
   A. foreclosure
   B. achievement
   C. moratorium

 D. diffusion
       Answer: C. moratorium
   Rationale: Moratorium involves active exploration of identity options without firm commitment.

62. An adolescent who adopts parental values without personal exploration is in:
   A. foreclosure
   B. moratorium
   C. achievement

 D. diffusion
       Answer: A. foreclosure
   Rationale: Foreclosure reflects commitment made without prior exploration.

63. Which statement about adolescent-parent relations is most accurate?
   A. Severe rebellion is universal and inevitable.
   B. Most adolescent-parent conflict centers on everyday issues rather than core values.
   C. Adolescents function best without parental monitoring.

 D. Identity formation requires total emotional separation from family.
       Answer: B. Most adolescent-parent conflict centers on everyday issues rather than core
values.
   Rationale: Research shows that conflict is typically mild and related to daily matters.

64. Juvenile delinquency is best understood as:
   A. purely genetic in origin
   B. the product of interacting biological, family, peer, and community influences
   C. caused only by low intelligence

 D. an unavoidable feature of adolescence
       Answer: B. the product of interacting biological, family, peer, and community influences
   Rationale: Delinquency results from multiple interacting risk factors.

65. Emerging adulthood is often characterized by:
   A. immediate assumption of stable adult roles by all individuals
   B. identity exploration and instability in love, work, and worldview
   C. complete dependence on parents without change

 D. decline in cognitive capacity
       Answer: B. identity exploration and instability in love, work, and worldview
   Rationale: Emerging adulthood involves exploration before stable commitments.

66. Postformal thought is often described as:
   A. rigid and absolutist
   B. reflective, practical, and able to tolerate ambiguity
   C. limited to adolescence
 D. equivalent to sensorimotor thought
       Answer: B. reflective, practical, and able to tolerate ambiguity
   Rationale: Postformal thinking integrates logic with real-world complexity.

67. Schaie proposed that adult cognitive development includes a shift toward using intellect for:
   A. sensorimotor adaptation
   B. practical goals and life demands
   C. stranger wariness

 D. conservation tasks
       Answer: B. practical goals and life demands
   Rationale: Adults use cognition to meet real-life responsibilities and challenges.

68. Sternberg's view of successful intelligence particularly values:
   A. memorization alone
   B. adaptation to, shaping of, and selection of environments
   C. repression of emotion

 D. unconscious conflict resolution
       Answer: B. adaptation to, shaping of, and selection of environments
   Rationale: Successful intelligence involves adapting to and influencing one's environment.

69. In emerging adulthood, intimacy is most likely to develop successfully after progress in:
   A. basic reflexes
   B. object permanence
   C. identity formation

 D. menopause
       Answer: C. identity formation
   Rationale: A stable identity supports the development of close relationships.

70. Which statement about marriage and cohabitation is most accurate?
   A. All cohabiting relationships are unstable and identical.
   B. Relationship outcomes vary according to commitment, context, and life circumstances.
   C. Marriage guarantees psychological well-being.

 D. Cohabitation eliminates all risk for breakup.
       Answer: B. Relationship outcomes vary according to commitment, context, and life
circumstances.
   Rationale: Relationship success depends on various personal and contextual factors.

71. Generativity in midlife refers primarily to:
   A. regret over lost youth
   B. concern for guiding the next generation and contributing to society
   C. withdrawal from all social roles

 D. fear of death
       Answer: B. concern for guiding the next generation and contributing to society
   Rationale: Generativity involves productivity and concern for future generations.
72. Which statement best reflects current views of the midlife crisis?
   A. It is universal and biologically inevitable.
   B. It is a myth with no basis in experience.
   C. It may occur for some individuals, but it is not a normative experience for all.

 D. It occurs only in men.
       Answer: C. It may occur for some individuals, but it is not a normative experience for all.
   Rationale: Midlife crisis is not universal but may occur depending on circumstances.

73. Fluid intelligence generally:
   A. increases steadily across all of adulthood
   B. involves accumulated knowledge and often remains more stable than speeded problem

solving
   C. is identical to crystallized intelligence

 D. disappears by late adulthood
       Answer: B. involves accumulated knowledge and often remains more stable than speeded
problem solving
   Rationale: While fluid intelligence declines, knowledge-based abilities tend to remain stable.

74. Crystallized intelligence is best described as:
   A. speed of novel information processing
   B. acquired knowledge and verbal skill
   C. infant reflex functioning

 D. hormonal adaptation to stress
       Answer: B. acquired knowledge and verbal skill
   Rationale: Crystallized intelligence reflects accumulated knowledge and experience.

75. The "empty nest" is most accurately viewed as:
   A. uniformly devastating for all parents
   B. often stressful but also potentially associated with renewed flexibility and satisfaction
   C. evidence of failed attachment

 D. irrelevant to marital relationships
       Answer: B. often stressful but also potentially associated with renewed flexibility and
satisfaction
   Rationale: Parents may experience both loss and new opportunities.

76. Which midlife adult best exemplifies filial maturity?
   A. A son who expects his aging parent to remain fully dependent
   B. A daughter who recognizes her aging parent as a separate adult with strengths and

limitations
   C. A parent who refuses all contact with siblings

 D. An adult child who infantilizes an older parent
       Answer: B. A daughter who recognizes her aging parent as a separate adult with
strengths and limitations
   Rationale: Filial maturity involves understanding parents as independent individuals.

77. Age-related declines in late adulthood are:
   A. identical across all individuals
   B. uniform across all abilities
   C. variable and influenced by health, education, lifestyle, and context

 D. unrelated to environment
       Answer: C. variable and influenced by health, education, lifestyle, and context
   Rationale: Aging varies widely among individuals.

78. Which is most characteristic of dementia?
   A. Normal age-related slowing only
   B. Severe progressive impairment in cognitive functioning that interferes with daily life
   C. Temporary adolescent confusion

 D. Stable personality style
       Answer: B. Severe progressive impairment in cognitive functioning that interferes with
daily life
   Rationale: Dementia significantly impairs daily functioning.

79. Selective optimization with compensation means older adults:
   A. avoid all goals to reduce frustration
   B. focus on valued goals, maximize strengths, and compensate for losses
   C. inevitably disengage from society

 D. rely only on family for functioning
       Answer: B. focus on valued goals, maximize strengths, and compensate for losses
   Rationale: Older adults adapt by optimizing strengths and compensating for decline.

80. Erikson's final psychosocial conflict is:
   A. initiative versus guilt
   B. intimacy versus isolation
   C. generativity versus stagnation

 D. ego integrity versus despair
       Answer: D. ego integrity versus despair
   Rationale: Older adults evaluate life with acceptance or regret.

81. Which statement best reflects continuity theory in aging?
   A. Older adults function best when all past roles are abandoned.
   B. Adaptation is promoted by maintaining patterns of behavior, values, and relationships that

are meaningful.
   C. Retirement inevitably leads to despair.

 D. Aging is determined only by genetic programming.
       Answer: B. Adaptation is promoted by maintaining patterns of behavior, values, and
relationships that are meaningful.
   Rationale: Continuity theory emphasizes consistency in behavior and identity.
82. Widowhood in late adulthood is best understood as:
   A. a brief and uniform process of grief
   B. a major life transition shaped by relationship quality, health, support, gender, and culture
   C. always more difficult than losing a child

 D. unrelated to identity
       Answer: B. a major life transition shaped by relationship quality, health, support, gender,
and culture
   Rationale: Widowhood varies depending on multiple personal and contextual factors.

83. Which statement about bereavement is most accurate?
   A. All mourners pass through identical stages in fixed order.
   B. Grief responses vary considerably across persons and cultures.
   C. Healthy grief lasts no more than two weeks.

 D. Continuing bonds always indicate pathology.
       Answer: B. Grief responses vary considerably across persons and cultures.
   Rationale: Grief is individualized and culturally influenced.

84. Ambiguous loss is especially difficult because:
   A. it is always associated with criminal behavior
   B. the loss lacks clarity or closure
   C. it applies only to children

 D. it is resolved through standard testing
       Answer: B. the loss lacks clarity or closure
   Rationale: Ambiguous loss creates uncertainty and complicates grieving.

85. Which adult loss is often underestimated socially despite its psychological significance?
   A. Losing a pen
   B. Mourning a miscarriage
   C. Missing one class

 D. Relocating for work
       Answer: B. Mourning a miscarriage
   Rationale: Miscarriage grief is often unrecognized but deeply impactful.

86. A life review in late adulthood may promote:
   A. sensorimotor adaptation
   B. ego integrity and meaning-making
   C. role confusion

 D. stranger anxiety
       Answer: B. ego integrity and meaning-making
   Rationale: Reflecting on life helps older adults achieve acceptance and coherence.

87. In a right-to-die case, the most ethically sound first step for a psychologist asked for an
opinion on decisional capacity is to:
   A. give an immediate opinion based on family report alone
   B. refuse automatically because death-related cases are always unethical
   C. conduct or recommend adequate assessment within one's competence and clarify the
limits of one's role

 D. rely solely on personal beliefs about euthanasia
       Answer: C. conduct or recommend adequate assessment within one's competence and
clarify the limits of one's role
   Rationale: Ethical practice requires competence, proper assessment, and role clarification.

88. Under the PAP Code of Ethics, only licensed and registered psychologists and
psychometricians are legally allowed to practice their profession, and practice must remain:

   A. within media popularity
   B. within boundaries prescribed by law and competence
   C. limited to hospital settings

 D. free from documentation requirements
       Answer: B. within boundaries prescribed by law and competence
   Rationale: Practice must comply with legal scope and professional competence under RA
10029.

89. A psychometrician is asked by a school to provide psychotherapy to a depressed student.
The most appropriate response is to:

   A. begin therapy immediately to avoid delay
   B. provide therapy only if the student consents
   C. decline the therapy role and facilitate referral, since psychometricians are prohibited from
the practice of therapy except in emergencies

 D. offer therapy if supervised by a teacher
       Answer: C. decline the therapy role and facilitate referral, since psychometricians are
prohibited from the practice of therapy except in emergencies
   Rationale: RA 10029 limits psychometricians' scope; therapy is not within their independent
practice.

90. Which situation best reflects proper delegation of work?
   A. Delegating test interpretation to an untrained clerk because the office is busy
   B. Delegating tasks only to persons competent to perform them, with appropriate supervision
   C. Letting a parent administer a psychological test at home for convenience

 D. Allowing any staff member to score projective tests without training
       Answer: B. Delegating tasks only to persons competent to perform them, with appropriate
supervision
   Rationale: Ethical delegation requires competence and supervision.

91. A practitioner becomes aware that personal stress is seriously impairing professional
judgment. The most ethical action is to:

   A. continue working to avoid disappointing clients
   B. hide the difficulty and make no changes
   C. seek consultation or assistance and consider limiting, suspending, or terminating affected
duties

 D. transfer all confidential files to a friend
       Answer: C. seek consultation or assistance and consider limiting, suspending, or
terminating affected duties
   Rationale: Ethical standards require addressing impairment to prevent harm.

92. Which action best protects confidentiality in telepsychology?
   A. Using open public Wi-Fi without safeguards
   B. Discussing cases loudly in shared public spaces
   C. Using secure systems and informing clients of privacy risks in electronic transmission

 D. Recording all sessions without consent
       Answer: C. Using secure systems and informing clients of privacy risks in electronic
transmission
   Rationale: Confidentiality must be protected through secure communication and informed
consent.

93. A psychologist receives a third-party request from an employer to assess an employee. At
the outset, the psychologist should clarify:

   A. that confidentiality is unlimited in all circumstances
   B. only the fee arrangement
   C. the role, who the client is, probable uses of the information, and limits of confidentiality

 D. that the employer automatically owns all raw data
       Answer: C. the role, who the client is, probable uses of the information, and limits of
confidentiality
   Rationale: Ethical practice requires clear role definition and disclosure of limits.

94. Under the ethics code, test data such as raw scores and notes should:
   A. always be posted to the client's family group chat
   B. be released freely upon verbal request
   C. not be released to unauthorized persons; raw data are generally not released except when

regulated by the court

 D. be shared with teachers without restriction
       Answer: C. not be released to unauthorized persons; raw data are generally not released
except when regulated by the court
   Rationale: Confidentiality and test security must be maintained.

95. Which practice is most consistent with ethical assessment?
   A. Using obsolete tests if they are familiar
   B. Administering photocopied test materials to save money
   C. Selecting valid, reliable, appropriate instruments relevant to the referral question

 D. Interpreting scores without considering cultural and situational factors
       Answer: C. Selecting valid, reliable, appropriate instruments relevant to the referral
question
   Rationale: Ethical testing requires valid tools and proper application.

96. A psychometrician is asked to administer assessment tools independently in a setting where
supervision by a registered psychologist is applicable. The most ethical course is to:

   A. proceed independently because administration is always unrestricted
   B. proceed only within RA 10029 boundaries and under required supervision
   C. refuse all assessment work permanently

 D. release test protocols to prove transparency
       Answer: B. proceed only within RA 10029 boundaries and under required supervision
   Rationale: Psychometricians must follow supervision requirements under RA 10029.

97. A client refuses further therapy after three sessions. Ethically, the therapist should:
   A. insist that termination is not the client's choice
   B. respect the client's right to withdraw and discuss appropriate next steps
   C. threaten disclosure to family

 D. continue billing for unfinished treatment automatically
       Answer: B. respect the client's right to withdraw and discuss appropriate next steps
   Rationale: Clients have the right to terminate services at any time.

98. Which statement best reflects the ethics code on multiple relationships?
   A. They are always harmless if both parties agree.
   B. They should be avoided when they may impair objectivity, competence, or effectiveness, or

risk exploitation or harm.
   C. They are prohibited only in schools.

 D. They are acceptable whenever therapy is brief.
       Answer: B. They should be avoided when they may impair objectivity, competence, or
effectiveness, or risk exploitation or harm.
   Rationale: Dual relationships are discouraged when they pose risks to professionalism and
client welfare.

99. During a timed teleassessment, the internet connection repeatedly fails. The most ethical
response is to:

   A. ignore the disruption and interpret results as fully equivalent
   B. continue while blaming the client
   C. consider the impact of connectivity on performance and address limitations in
interpretation or reschedule as needed

 D. report only percentile ranks without comment
       Answer: C. consider the impact of connectivity on performance and address limitations in
interpretation or reschedule as needed
   Rationale: Assessment validity must be protected by addressing technical limitations.

100. A colleague appears to have committed an ethical violation that may substantially harm a
client. According to the code, the psychologist should:

    A. ignore it to preserve collegiality
    B. gossip about it informally
    C. take appropriate action, which may include reporting to proper authorities if substantial
harm is likely

 D. post concerns publicly on social media first
        Answer: C. take appropriate action, which may include reporting to proper authorities if
substantial harm is likely
    Rationale: Ethical responsibility includes addressing violations that may harm clients.
DEVELOPMENTAL PSYCHOLOGY
EXAM 3
DEVELOPMENTAL PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 3

1. Which statement best reflects the life-span perspective in developmental psychology?
  A. Development ends when biological maturity is reached.
  B. Development consists only of age-related gains.
  C. Development is lifelong, multidimensional, multidirectional, and plastic.

 D. Development is determined almost entirely by heredity.
       Answer: C. Development is lifelong, multidimensional, multidirectional, and plastic.
  Rationale: The life-span perspective holds that development continues throughout the entire
life course and involves multiple dimensions, directions of change, and capacity for modification.

2. A developmental psychologist studies how poverty, schooling, and family relationships
interact with brain maturation in shaping children's school performance. This approach is best
described as:

  A. reductionistic
  B. interdisciplinary
  C. psychodynamic

 D. nativistic
       Answer: B. interdisciplinary
  Rationale: This approach integrates biological, cognitive, and contextual influences, which is
the hallmark of interdisciplinary developmental study.

3. Which is the best example of a normative history-graded influence?
  A. A child's temperament
  B. Puberty at age 12
  C. Exposure to a major pandemic during adolescence

 D. Losing a parent in middle childhood
       Answer: C. Exposure to a major pandemic during adolescence
  Rationale: A normative history-graded influence is an event shared by many people in a
generation because of a particular historical period.

4. Which research design is most appropriate if a psychologist wants to compare age
differences in memory among 20-, 40-, and 60-year-olds at one point in time?

  A. longitudinal
  B. cross-sectional
  C. sequential-cohort

 D. ethnographic
       Answer: B. cross-sectional
  Rationale: Cross-sectional research compares different age groups at the same point in time.

5. A researcher finds that children who attend high-quality preschool later perform better in
reading. Before concluding that preschool caused the better reading outcomes, the researcher
must most directly address:

  A. attrition
  B. cohort effects
  C. confounding variables

 D. observer bias only
       Answer: C. confounding variables
  Rationale: To infer causation, the researcher must rule out alternative influences such as
family background, parental involvement, or prior ability.

6. In Piaget's theory, development is advanced when children modify existing cognitive schemes
to fit new information. This process is called:

  A. assimilation
  B. accommodation
  C. equilibration

 D. habituation
       Answer: B. accommodation
  Rationale: Accommodation occurs when a person changes an existing mental structure to
incorporate new experience.

7. A fertilized ovum divides repeatedly and travels down the fallopian tube before implantation.
This period is the:

  A. fetal period
  B. embryonic period
  C. germinal period

 D. neonatal period
       Answer: C. germinal period
  Rationale: The germinal period begins at fertilization and includes early cell division and
implantation.

8. A genetic counselor explains that a disorder appears only when a child inherits two recessive
alleles, one from each parent. This pattern is:

  A. sex-linked dominant
  B. autosomal recessive
  C. multifactorial

 D. chromosomal nondisjunction
       Answer: B. autosomal recessive
  Rationale: Autosomal recessive disorders are expressed only when both alleles for the trait
are recessive.

9. Which maternal condition poses the greatest risk for fetal alcohol spectrum disorders?
  A. mild morning sickness
  B. iron supplementation
  C. persistent alcohol use during pregnancy

 D. moderate prenatal exercise
       Answer: C. persistent alcohol use during pregnancy
  Rationale: Alcohol is a teratogen that can disrupt fetal development and produce fetal alcohol
spectrum disorders.
