10. Which statement best reflects the modern view of heredity and environment?
   A. Heredity fixes development and environment has little effect.
   B. Environment determines development unless a severe mutation is present.
   C. Heredity and environment interact continuously across development.

 D. Heredity influences only physical traits, not behavior.
       Answer: C. Heredity and environment interact continuously across development.
   Rationale: Contemporary developmental psychology emphasizes ongoing interaction
between genetic predispositions and environmental conditions.

11. A newborn's score on the Apgar scale is used primarily to:
   A. diagnose intellectual disability
   B. assess immediate adaptation to extrauterine life
   C. measure attachment security

 D. predict long-term personality
       Answer: B. assess immediate adaptation to extrauterine life
   Rationale: The Apgar scale evaluates newborn condition immediately after birth, including
respiration, heart rate, reflexes, tone, and color.

12. The tendency for development to proceed from the head downward is called:
   A. proximodistal development
   B. cephalocaudal development
   C. epigenesis

 D. differentiation
       Answer: B. cephalocaudal development
   Rationale: Cephalocaudal development describes the principle that growth and motor control
proceed from head to lower body.

13. An infant repeatedly drops a spoon from a high chair and watches a parent retrieve it. In
Piaget's sensorimotor framework, this behavior most clearly reflects:

   A. object permanence
   B. deferred imitation
   C. tertiary circular reactions

 D. social referencing
       Answer: C. tertiary circular reactions
   Rationale: Tertiary circular reactions involve deliberate experimentation with actions to
observe new outcomes.

14. If an infant becomes less responsive to a repeated stimulus and then shows renewed
attention when a new stimulus is presented, the infant has demonstrated:

   A. conservation
   B. habituation and dishabituation
   C. imprinting

 D. overregularization
       Answer: B. habituation and dishabituation
   Rationale: Habituation is decreased response to repeated stimulation, while dishabituation is
renewed attention to a novel stimulus.

15. Which theorist most strongly emphasized the role of social interaction and guided
participation in cognitive development?

   A. Piaget
   B. Vygotsky
   C. Freud

 D. Gesell
       Answer: B. Vygotsky
   Rationale: Vygotsky stressed the importance of social interaction, guided participation, and
cultural tools in cognitive growth.

16. A toddler calls all four-legged animals "dog." This error is best described as:
   A. fast mapping
   B. underextension
   C. overextension

 D. telegraphic speech
       Answer: C. overextension
   Rationale: Overextension occurs when a child applies a word too broadly to objects beyond
its correct category.

17. According to Erikson, the central psychosocial task of infancy is:
   A. autonomy versus shame and doubt
   B. trust versus mistrust
   C. initiative versus guilt

 D. industry versus inferiority
       Answer: B. trust versus mistrust
   Rationale: Erikson proposed that infancy centers on developing basic trust through consistent
and responsive care.

18. In Ainsworth's Strange Situation, a securely attached infant is most likely to:
   A. ignore the caregiver completely upon reunion
   B. show distress at separation and seek comfort at reunion
   C. resist contact and simultaneously seek it in a confused way

 D. remain equally friendly to the stranger and caregiver
       Answer: B. show distress at separation and seek comfort at reunion
   Rationale: Securely attached infants use the caregiver as a safe base, become distressed by
separation, and are comforted upon reunion.

19. Social referencing refers to:
   A. learning by imitation without understanding
   B. using another person's emotional reaction to guide one's own behavior
   C. confusing self with others in early infancy

 D. showing stranger anxiety in unfamiliar settings
       Answer: B. using another person's emotional reaction to guide one's own behavior
   Rationale: Social referencing occurs when children look to another person's emotional cues
to decide how to respond in uncertain situations.

20. A toddler who insists on saying "Me do it!" is showing the developmental push toward:
   A. initiative
   B. intimacy
   C. autonomy

 D. generativity
       Answer: C. autonomy
   Rationale: This behavior reflects the toddler's growing need for self-control and independent
action.

21. Preoperational thought is characterized by:
   A. abstract hypothetico-deductive reasoning
   B. mental operations involving reversibility and conservation
   C. symbolic thinking but limited logical operations

 D. formal scientific problem solving
       Answer: C. symbolic thinking but limited logical operations
   Rationale: Preoperational children use symbols and language but still lack mature logical
operations such as conservation.

22. A child sees a taller, narrower glass as having more liquid than a shorter, wider one, despite
seeing the same liquid poured between them. This illustrates lack of:

   A. object permanence
   B. class inclusion
   C. conservation

 D. seriation
       Answer: C. conservation
   Rationale: Conservation is the understanding that quantity remains the same despite
changes in shape or appearance.

23. The ability to understand that others can hold beliefs different from one's own is called:
   A. private speech
   B. theory of mind
   C. social learning

 D. reciprocal determinism
       Answer: B. theory of mind
   Rationale: Theory of mind is the capacity to understand that other people have separate
beliefs, intentions, and perspectives.
24. According to Vygotsky, the range between what a child can do alone and what the child can
do with help is the:

   A. accommodation zone
   B. latent learning field
   C. zone of proximal development

 D. scaffold interval
       Answer: C. zone of proximal development
   Rationale: The zone of proximal development refers to the gap between independent
performance and performance possible with guidance.

25. Which parenting style is generally associated with the most favorable developmental
outcomes in early childhood?

   A. authoritarian
   B. authoritative
   C. permissive

 D. neglectful
       Answer: B. authoritative
   Rationale: Authoritative parenting combines warmth and firm control, which tends to promote
competence, self-regulation, and social adjustment.

26. In Erikson's theory, a preschool child's major psychosocial challenge is:
   A. trust versus mistrust
   B. autonomy versus shame and doubt
   C. initiative versus guilt

 D. identity versus role confusion
       Answer: C. initiative versus guilt
   Rationale: Preschool children develop initiative as they begin purposeful activity and role
exploration.

27. Parten's category of play in which children play near one another with similar materials but
without true interaction is:

   A. cooperative play
   B. associative play
   C. parallel play

 D. onlooker play
       Answer: C. parallel play
   Rationale: Parallel play involves playing alongside other children without organized
interaction.

28. A parent explains to a child, "How would you feel if someone grabbed your toy?" This
discipline approach primarily promotes:

   A. external compliance through fear
   B. inductive discipline and empathy
   C. learned helplessness

 D. permissiveness
       Answer: B. inductive discipline and empathy
   Rationale: Inductive discipline encourages children to understand the effects of their actions
on others, which fosters empathy and internalization.

29. Compared with early childhood, children in middle childhood are more likely to:
   A. rely entirely on perception
   B. understand conservation and classification
   C. show no improvement in selective attention

 D. lose all egocentric tendencies immediately
       Answer: B. understand conservation and classification
   Rationale: Middle childhood is associated with concrete operational thought, including
conservation and classification skills.

30. A school-age child organizes colored blocks first by shape and then by size. This best
demonstrates:

   A. centration
   B. seriation
   C. transduction

 D. animism
       Answer: B. seriation
   Rationale: Seriation is the ability to arrange objects in a logical order according to a
dimension such as size.

31. Knowledge about memory processes and strategies is called:
   A. metamemory
   B. eidetic memory
   C. implicit memory

 D. rehearsal deficit
       Answer: A. metamemory
   Rationale: Metamemory refers to awareness and understanding of how memory works and
how it can be improved.

32. A child who remembers a spelling list by using the first letters to make a phrase is using:
   A. accommodation
   B. a mnemonic strategy
   C. social referencing

 D. symbolic function
       Answer: B. a mnemonic strategy
   Rationale: A mnemonic strategy is a deliberate memory aid that helps organize and retrieve
information.

33. Sternberg's triarchic theory suggests that traditional school tasks emphasize mainly:
   A. practical intelligence only
   B. analytical intelligence
   C. emotional intelligence

 D. kinesthetic intelligence
       Answer: B. analytical intelligence
   Rationale: Traditional academic tasks usually reward analytical skills such as evaluating,
comparing, and solving structured problems.

34. A child's belief that "I am good at math but not very good at drawing" illustrates:
   A. global self-esteem only
   B. differentiated self-concept
   C. identity foreclosure

 D. personal fable
       Answer: B. differentiated self-concept
   Rationale: In middle childhood, children begin describing themselves in specific domains
rather than only in global terms.

35. According to Erikson, the major psychosocial issue of middle childhood is:
   A. industry versus inferiority
   B. initiative versus guilt
   C. integrity versus despair

 D. intimacy versus isolation
       Answer: A. industry versus inferiority
   Rationale: School-age children focus on mastering valued skills and developing a sense of
competence.

36. A child rejected by peers because the child often interprets ambiguous acts as hostile is
showing:

   A. social facilitation
   B. hostile attribution bias
   C. moral realism

 D. selective optimization
       Answer: B. hostile attribution bias
   Rationale: Hostile attribution bias is the tendency to assume that unclear social actions are
intended to be harmful.

37. Which statement about puberty is most accurate?
   A. It begins at the same chronological age for all adolescents.
   B. It consists only of visible physical changes.
   C. It involves hormonal changes that trigger sexual maturation.

 D. It marks the end of brain development.
       Answer: C. It involves hormonal changes that trigger sexual maturation.
   Rationale: Puberty is driven by hormonal processes that initiate physical and reproductive
maturation.
38. Imaginary audience and personal fable are commonly associated with:
   A. sensorimotor thought
   B. concrete operational thought
   C. adolescent egocentrism

 D. postformal thought
       Answer: C. adolescent egocentrism
   Rationale: These patterns reflect adolescents' heightened self-consciousness and belief in
their uniqueness.

39. Piaget's formal operational stage is characterized by the ability to:
   A. understand object permanence
   B. reason hypothetically and systematically
   C. conserve quantity through direct manipulation only

 D. engage only in trial-and-error problem solving
       Answer: B. reason hypothetically and systematically
   Rationale: Formal operational thinking includes abstract reasoning and systematic hypothesis
testing.

40. According to Kohlberg, moral reasoning at the conventional level is based primarily on:
   A. avoidance of punishment only
   B. self-interest only
   C. conformity to social expectations and rules

 D. universal ethical principles
       Answer: C. conformity to social expectations and rules
   Rationale: Conventional morality centers on gaining approval, maintaining relationships, and
obeying laws and social order.

41. Gilligan argued that Kohlberg's theory underemphasized:
   A. justice
   B. care and responsibility in moral reasoning
   C. cognitive development

 D. reinforcement history
       Answer: B. care and responsibility in moral reasoning
   Rationale: Gilligan proposed that moral reasoning also includes an ethic of care, not only
justice-based principles.

42. Which adolescent is most likely to be in identity moratorium?
   A. one who has made commitments without exploring alternatives
   B. one who is exploring options but has not yet committed
   C. one who shows neither exploration nor commitment

 D. one who has committed after active exploration
       Answer: B. one who is exploring options but has not yet committed
   Rationale: Moratorium is defined by active exploration without firm commitment.
43. According to Erikson, successful resolution of the adolescent identity crisis leads to the
virtue of:

   A. hope
   B. will
   C. fidelity

 D. wisdom
       Answer: C. fidelity
   Rationale: Fidelity is the virtue that emerges when adolescents form a stable and coherent
sense of identity.

44. Marcia's identity status characterized by commitment without prior exploration is:
   A. diffusion
   B. foreclosure
   C. moratorium

 D. achievement
       Answer: B. foreclosure
   Rationale: Foreclosure occurs when a person commits to roles or beliefs without seriously
exploring alternatives.

45. Which family pattern is most consistently associated with healthier adolescent adjustment?
   A. no parental monitoring at all
   B. rigid control with no warmth
   C. warm relationships with appropriate monitoring

 D. complete peer-guided autonomy
       Answer: C. warm relationships with appropriate monitoring
   Rationale: Adolescents tend to function best when parents combine emotional support with
appropriate supervision.

46. Juvenile delinquency is best understood as:
   A. caused entirely by biology
   B. caused entirely by parenting
   C. influenced by interacting biological, family, peer, and community factors

 D. a normal and necessary phase of adolescence
       Answer: C. influenced by interacting biological, family, peer, and community factors
   Rationale: Delinquency is a multidetermined outcome shaped by the interaction of several
personal and environmental influences.

47. The term emerging adulthood refers to:
   A. the transition from infancy to toddlerhood
   B. a distinct period marked by exploration and instability between adolescence and settled

adult roles
   C. the onset of menopause
   D. the final stage of Erikson's theory
  Answer: B. a distinct period marked by exploration and instability between adolescence

and settled adult roles
   Rationale: Emerging adulthood is characterized by identity exploration, instability, and

delayed assumption of enduring adult roles.

48. One hallmark of adult cognition beyond adolescence is the growing ability to:
   A. eliminate all contradictions from thought
   B. think only in absolute terms
   C. integrate logic with experience and emotion

 D. reject relativistic thinking completely
       Answer: C. integrate logic with experience and emotion
   Rationale: Adult cognition often becomes more flexible and realistic by combining logic,
experience, and emotional understanding.

49. Sternberg used the term tacit knowledge to refer to:
   A. genetic knowledge present at birth
   B. information not formally taught but useful for getting ahead
   C. explicit memory for school subjects

 D. unconscious conflict material
       Answer: B. information not formally taught but useful for getting ahead
   Rationale: Tacit knowledge refers to practical know-how gained informally through
experience.

50. Emotional intelligence refers to the capacity to:
   A. solve abstract equations rapidly
   B. memorize large amounts of information
   C. understand and regulate emotions effectively

 D. ignore emotions in decision making
       Answer: C. understand and regulate emotions effectively
   Rationale: Emotional intelligence involves perceiving, understanding, and managing emotions
in oneself and others.

51. In emerging adulthood, intimate relationships are generally healthiest when they are based
on:

   A. identity diffusion and dependence
   B. mutuality, communication, and commitment
   C. avoidance of self-disclosure

 D. role confusion
       Answer: B. mutuality, communication, and commitment
   Rationale: Healthy intimate relationships are grounded in reciprocity, openness, trust, and
stable commitment.

52. According to Erikson, failure to establish close reciprocal relationships in young adulthood
risks:
   A. stagnation
   B. despair
   C. isolation

 D. inferiority
       Answer: C. isolation
   Rationale: In Erikson's theory, the unresolved outcome of the intimacy versus isolation stage
is social and emotional isolation.

53. Which statement best reflects current views of marriage in emerging adulthood?
   A. Marriage universally occurs at the same age.
   B. Entry into marriage varies with culture, economics, and personal goals.
   C. Marriage is no longer relevant to development.

 D. Marriage always decreases stress regardless of relationship quality.
       Answer: B. Entry into marriage varies with culture, economics, and personal goals.
   Rationale: Marriage patterns differ widely depending on social context, values, resources, and
life planning.

54. Parenthood is best understood as:
   A. purely a biological event with no psychological meaning
   B. uniformly beneficial for all couples at all times
   C. a developmental experience shaped by readiness, support, and context

 D. unrelated to identity or role change
       Answer: C. a developmental experience shaped by readiness, support, and context
   Rationale: Parenthood affects roles, identity, relationships, and adjustment, and its meaning
varies across life circumstances.

55. In middle adulthood, fluid intelligence generally:
   A. rises sharply into late life
   B. remains completely unchanged
   C. tends to decline more than crystallized intelligence

 D. becomes the same as tacit knowledge
       Answer: C. tends to decline more than crystallized intelligence
   Rationale: Fluid intelligence, especially speed and novel problem-solving ability, tends to
decrease earlier than accumulated knowledge.

56. Crystallized intelligence refers primarily to:
   A. speed of processing novel information
   B. accumulated knowledge and verbal skills
   C. sensory acuity

 D. motor coordination
       Answer: B. accumulated knowledge and verbal skills
   Rationale: Crystallized intelligence reflects learning, vocabulary, and experience-based
knowledge.
57. Expertise in middle adulthood often compensates for declines in:
   A. moral reasoning
   B. all forms of memory
   C. processing speed in specific domains

 D. personality stability
       Answer: C. processing speed in specific domains
   Rationale: Expertise allows adults to perform effectively despite slower basic processing
through experience and efficient strategies.

58. Which statement is most consistent with current evidence on the "midlife crisis"?
   A. It is universal and biologically inevitable.
   B. It is a myth with no basis in any individual experience.
   C. It may occur for some individuals but is not a normative universal crisis.

 D. It occurs in all adults exactly between ages 40 and 45.
       Answer: C. It may occur for some individuals but is not a normative universal crisis.
   Rationale: Research does not support the idea that all adults experience a standard midlife
crisis, although some individuals do.

59. Erikson described the major psychosocial task of middle adulthood as:
   A. intimacy versus isolation
   B. generativity versus stagnation
   C. industry versus inferiority

 D. identity versus confusion
       Answer: B. generativity versus stagnation
   Rationale: Middle adulthood emphasizes productivity, care, and contribution to the next
generation and society.

60. Generativity is best defined as:
   A. withdrawal from social responsibility
   B. concern for guiding the next generation and contributing to society
   C. exclusive focus on personal achievement

 D. fear of death and loss
       Answer: B. concern for guiding the next generation and contributing to society
   Rationale: Generativity includes mentoring, parenting, teaching, and contributing to the
broader community.

61. The "empty nest" is best viewed as:
   A. always a severe psychological crisis
   B. a transition whose effects vary by relationship quality, culture, and personal meaning
   C. proof of failed parenting

 D. irrelevant to middle adulthood
       Answer: B. a transition whose effects vary by relationship quality, culture, and personal
meaning
   Rationale: The empty nest is a developmental transition with varied outcomes depending on
context and interpretation.

62. Caring simultaneously for one's children and aging parents is commonly termed:
   A. kin selection
   B. social convoy
   C. sandwich generation

 D. filial diffusion
       Answer: C. sandwich generation
   Rationale: The sandwich generation refers to adults who are responsible for both younger
and older family members at the same time.

63. In late adulthood, sensory and psychomotor changes most commonly involve:
   A. dramatic gains in visual acuity
   B. complete loss of learning capacity
   C. gradual decline in vision, hearing, balance, and reaction speed

 D. identical changes in all older adults
       Answer: C. gradual decline in vision, hearing, balance, and reaction speed
   Rationale: These age-related changes are common in late adulthood, though the extent
varies across individuals.

64. Which theory proposes that aging results partly from accumulated cellular damage caused
by unstable oxygen molecules?

   A. programmed senescence theory
   B. free-radical theory
   C. attachment theory

 D. activity theory
       Answer: B. free-radical theory
   Rationale: Free-radical theory explains aging partly in terms of cumulative damage caused by
unstable oxygen molecules.

65. Reserve capacity refers to:
   A. excess money saved for retirement
   B. the body's and brain's built-in ability to endure stress before impairment becomes evident
   C. stored unconscious conflict

 D. a type of crystallized intelligence
       Answer: B. the body's and brain's built-in ability to endure stress before impairment
becomes evident
   Rationale: Reserve capacity refers to functional resilience that allows individuals to cope with
stress and loss before obvious decline appears.

66. Which cognitive ability is most likely to remain relatively strong in healthy older adults?
   A. speed of processing
   B. working memory under heavy load
   C. semantic knowledge

 D. divided attention
       Answer: C. semantic knowledge
   Rationale: Semantic knowledge, including vocabulary and general information, is often well
maintained in healthy aging.

67. Wisdom in late adulthood is best described as:
   A. rote recall of facts
   B. practical insight about life matters with judgment and reflection
   C. simple processing speed

 D. absolute moral certainty
       Answer: B. practical insight about life matters with judgment and reflection
   Rationale: Wisdom involves reflective judgment, deep understanding, and practical insight
into important life issues.

68. Erikson's final psychosocial conflict is:
   A. intimacy versus isolation
   B. generativity versus stagnation
   C. ego integrity versus despair

 D. trust versus mistrust
       Answer: C. ego integrity versus despair
   Rationale: In late adulthood, individuals evaluate their lives and either reach acceptance or
experience regret and despair.

69. Selective optimization with compensation refers to:
   A. choosing random activities after retirement
   B. maximizing performance by focusing on priorities and compensating for losses
   C. withdrawing from society to preserve energy

 D. depending exclusively on others for functioning
       Answer: B. maximizing performance by focusing on priorities and compensating for losses
   Rationale: This model explains how older adults adapt by selecting goals, optimizing
strengths, and compensating for decline.

70. Which statement best reflects continuity theory in aging?
   A. Older adults function best when they radically abandon past habits.
   B. Adjustment is aided by maintaining patterns of behavior and identity over time.
   C. Aging is best understood as inevitable disengagement.

 D. Social support becomes unimportant in old age.
       Answer: B. Adjustment is aided by maintaining patterns of behavior and identity over time.
   Rationale: Continuity theory proposes that adaptation in old age is enhanced by preserving
consistent habits, values, and roles.

71. Widowhood in late adulthood is best understood as:
   A. a uniform experience with identical outcomes
   B. a transition shaped by health, finances, social support, and prior relationship quality
   C. easier for everyone than divorce

 D. unrelated to mental health risk
       Answer: B. a transition shaped by health, finances, social support, and prior relationship
quality
   Rationale: Adjustment to widowhood varies widely depending on personal, social, and
economic circumstances.

72. Elder abuse includes:
   A. only physical violence
   B. only financial exploitation
   C. physical, emotional, sexual, neglectful, and financial mistreatment

 D. only abuse committed by strangers
       Answer: C. physical, emotional, sexual, neglectful, and financial mistreatment
   Rationale: Elder abuse encompasses multiple forms of harm and exploitation, not just one
type.

73. Contemporary views of grief are most consistent with the idea that:
   A. all bereaved persons progress through identical fixed stages
   B. grief shows multiple patterns and is shaped by relationship, context, and culture
   C. healthy grieving requires immediate detachment from the deceased

 D. absence of crying always indicates pathology
       Answer: B. grief shows multiple patterns and is shaped by relationship, context, and
culture
   Rationale: Current grief models emphasize variability rather than one universal sequence of
responses.

74. A person whose spouse has dementia and is psychologically absent but physically present
may experience:

   A. resilience
   B. ambiguous loss
   C. anticipatory socialization

 D. selective compensation
       Answer: B. ambiguous loss
   Rationale: Ambiguous loss occurs when a loved one is physically present but psychologically
altered or unavailable.

75. Compared with younger children, adolescents' understanding of death is generally:
   A. less abstract and less emotionally nuanced
   B. more likely to include abstract and existential concerns
   C. limited to magical thinking only

 D. unrelated to identity issues
       Answer: B. more likely to include abstract and existential concerns
   Rationale: Adolescents' more advanced cognition allows them to think about death in
abstract, existential, and personal terms.

76. A life review in late adulthood often serves the developmental function of:
   A. increasing egocentrism
   B. supporting ego integrity and meaning-making
   C. eliminating all regret

 D. reversing cognitive decline
       Answer: B. supporting ego integrity and meaning-making
   Rationale: Life review helps older adults integrate their experiences and find coherence and
meaning in their lives.

77. Which is the clearest example of passive euthanasia?
   A. administering a lethal injection
   B. prescribing medication specifically to cause death
   C. withholding or withdrawing extraordinary life-sustaining treatment

 D. falsifying a death certificate
       Answer: C. withholding or withdrawing extraordinary life-sustaining treatment
   Rationale: Passive euthanasia involves allowing death to occur by not starting or continuing
extraordinary life-prolonging measures.

78. A developmental psychologist working with bereaved parents should remember that:
   A. there is a single normal timetable for recovery
   B. parental grief is usually brief
   C. the death of a child often carries profound, long-lasting meaning consequences

 D. parents should avoid talking about the deceased child
       Answer: C. the death of a child often carries profound, long-lasting meaning
consequences
   Rationale: The loss of a child is often one of the most devastating forms of bereavement and
may have enduring psychological effects.

79. A psychometrician is asked by a school principal to interpret a child's test protocol
independently and recommend psychotherapy. Under RA 10029-linked ethical limits, the best
action is to:

   A. comply because school authorities requested it
   B. interpret the test and begin therapy if the parents agree
   C. work within psychometrician boundaries and refer/supervise through a registered
psychologist

 D. refuse all further involvement in the case
       Answer: C. work within psychometrician boundaries and refer/supervise through a
registered psychologist
   Rationale: RA 10029 limits psychometricians to their lawful scope, so independent
interpretation beyond role and psychotherapy require referral or supervision by a licensed
psychologist.
80. Which ethical principle most directly requires psychology practitioners to obtain free and
informed consent and protect confidentiality?

   A. respect for the dignity of persons and peoples
   B. industry versus inferiority
   C. disengagement theory

 D. psychometric standardization
       Answer: A. respect for the dignity of persons and peoples
   Rationale: This ethical principle includes respect for autonomy, privacy, informed consent,
and protection of confidential information.

81. A client discloses information during telepsychology. Ethically, the practitioner should:
   A. assume online sessions are exempt from ordinary ethical rules
   B. apply the same ethical principles as face-to-face work and discuss privacy risks
   C. record the session automatically without discussion

 D. email confidential files without safeguards if the client seems comfortable
       Answer: B. apply the same ethical principles as face-to-face work and discuss privacy
risks
   Rationale: Telepsychology is governed by the same ethical standards as in-person work, with
additional attention to privacy and security risks.

82. When providing services to a minor who cannot legally give full informed consent, the
practitioner should:

   A. ignore the child's preferences because only the guardian matters
   B. obtain assent when appropriate, consider the child's welfare, and obtain permission from a
legally authorized person
   C. proceed without explanation if the service is beneficial

 D. rely only on school consent
       Answer: B. obtain assent when appropriate, consider the child's welfare, and obtain
permission from a legally authorized person
   Rationale: Ethical practice requires protecting the rights and welfare of vulnerable persons
through assent, proper explanation, and lawful substitute consent.

83. Which action best reflects the ethical standard on boundaries of competence?
   A. Accepting any case to gain experience
   B. Providing services only within one's education, training, supervised experience, and

competence
   C. Using unfamiliar tests without studying them if time is limited

 D. Avoiding referrals so clients stay within one facility
       Answer: B. Providing services only within one's education, training, supervised
experience, and competence
   Rationale: Ethical competence requires practitioners to work only within areas for which they
are adequately prepared.
84. A psychometrician in training is delegated test administration by a supervisor. Ethical
delegation requires that:

   A. any staff member may interpret results if they observed testing
   B. delegated tasks match the trainee's competence and level of supervision
   C. the client need not be informed that tasks are delegated

 D. supervision is optional if the trainee has a manual
       Answer: B. delegated tasks match the trainee's competence and level of supervision
   Rationale: Delegation is ethical only when responsibilities are appropriate to training and
supported by sufficient supervision.

85. A psychology practitioner becomes aware that personal distress is impairing professional
judgment. The most ethical response is to:

   A. continue services to avoid disappointing clients
   B. conceal the problem from everyone
   C. obtain consultation or assistance and determine whether duties should be limited,
suspended, or terminated

 D. rely on experience alone and ignore self-care
       Answer: C. obtain consultation or assistance and determine whether duties should be
limited, suspended, or terminated
   Rationale: Ethical practice requires self-monitoring and corrective action when personal
problems interfere with competent service.

86. A practitioner is asked by an employer to evaluate an employee referred by management. At
the outset, the practitioner should clarify:

   A. only the employee's diagnosis
   B. who the client is, the evaluator's role, probable uses of the information, and limits of
confidentiality
   C. only the employer's expectations

 D. only the fee schedule
       Answer: B. who the client is, the evaluator's role, probable uses of the information, and
limits of confidentiality
   Rationale: Third-party service requests require clear role definition and transparency about
information use and confidentiality limits.

87. Which situation is the clearest example of a harmful multiple relationship?
   A. Conducting one scheduled assessment session with a referred client
   B. Becoming a business partner of a current therapy client
   C. Consulting another professional about a case with appropriate safeguards

 D. Providing crisis referral information in an emergency
       Answer: B. Becoming a business partner of a current therapy client
   Rationale: A business relationship with a current client risks impaired objectivity, exploitation,
and harm.

88. Which action best protects confidentiality in reports or consultations?
   A. Sharing all background details to make the case interesting
   B. Limiting disclosure to information relevant to the professional purpose
   C. Posting anonymized-looking details on social media without consent

 D. Discussing cases freely with friends who are curious
       Answer: B. Limiting disclosure to information relevant to the professional purpose
   Rationale: Confidentiality is best protected by disclosing only the minimum information
necessary for the legitimate professional purpose.

89. A psychometrician is asked to conduct psychotherapy for a distressed test-taker because
the psychologist is unavailable. The most ethical response is:

   A. provide therapy because prior test contact is sufficient
   B. provide therapy only if the client insists
   C. recognize that psychometricians are prohibited from practicing therapy except in
emergencies, and then only within emergency limits with proper referral

 D. accept the role if no written complaint is expected
       Answer: C. recognize that psychometricians are prohibited from practicing therapy except
in emergencies, and then only within emergency limits with proper referral
   Rationale: Psychometricians must remain within legal and ethical scope, and therapy is
outside ordinary practice except within narrow emergency conditions.

90. Which statement is most consistent with the ethical standard on assessment by unqualified
persons?

   A. Test materials may be shared widely if the purpose is educational.
   B. Assessment tools may be promoted for routine use by unqualified persons.
   C. Test protocols and interpretations must be secured from unqualified persons.

 D. Anyone may interpret a protocol if the raw score is available.
       Answer: C. Test protocols and interpretations must be secured from unqualified persons.
   Rationale: Ethical standards require restricting test materials and interpretations to qualified
professionals to prevent misuse and harm.

91. A researcher becomes aware that another practitioner may have violated the code but
believes an informal discussion could correct the problem without breaching confidentiality. The
most ethical first step is to:

   A. post the concern publicly online
   B. attempt informal resolution when appropriate
   C. file a complaint without evidence

 D. ignore the issue because only committees may act
       Answer: B. attempt informal resolution when appropriate
   Rationale: When suitable and confidentiality is not violated, informal resolution is the proper
initial response to a possible ethical concern.

92. Which response best reflects ethics when law and the code appear to conflict?
   A. Ignore both the law and the code.
   B. First try to resolve the conflict while remaining committed to the code; if unresolved, adhere
to law or governing authority.

   C. Always follow the code regardless of legal consequences.

 D. Always follow organizational preference regardless of law.
       Answer: B. First try to resolve the conflict while remaining committed to the code; if
unresolved, adhere to law or governing authority.
   Rationale: Ethical practice requires attempting to reconcile law and ethics first, but if
unresolved, practitioners follow the law or governing authority.

93. A practitioner wants to record a counseling session for supervision. Ethically, the practitioner
should first:

   A. record first and obtain consent later
   B. obtain consent and explain anticipated uses of the recording
   C. ask only the supervisor's permission

 D. record secretly if identifying information will be removed
       Answer: B. obtain consent and explain anticipated uses of the recording
   Rationale: Recording client voices or images requires prior consent and clear explanation of
how the recording will be used.

94. A practitioner asked to release a client's assessment results to a third party should primarily
consider:

   A. whether the third party is curious
   B. whether disclosure is authorized, necessary, and limited to what is needed
   C. whether the practitioner will receive praise

 D. whether the client is unlikely to object
       Answer: B. whether disclosure is authorized, necessary, and limited to what is needed
   Rationale: Ethical disclosure requires valid authorization, legitimate purpose, and minimal
necessary release of information.

95. Which is the best example of exploitative conduct?
   A. Referring a client to another qualified professional when needed
   B. Using one's authority over a supervisee for personal gain
   C. Explaining limits of confidentiality

 D. Seeking consultation on a difficult case
       Answer: B. Using one's authority over a supervisee for personal gain
   Rationale: Exploitation occurs when a practitioner misuses power over another person for
personal benefit.

96. Which practice best reflects integrity in public statements?
   A. Exaggerating success rates to attract clients
   B. Using vague credentials that could be misinterpreted
   C. Making accurate, nondeceptive statements about training, services, and qualifications
   D. Claiming competence in all areas of psychology
  Answer: C. Making accurate, nondeceptive statements about training, services, and

qualifications
   Rationale: Integrity requires truthful and accurate communication about one's background,

services, and competence.

97. In an emergency where no other mental health service is available, a practitioner may:
   A. provide no help unless fully specialized
   B. provide cautious, limited emergency assistance and discontinue when the emergency

ends, ensuring competent follow-up is available
   C. take over long-term treatment indefinitely outside competence

 D. ignore referral needs after the crisis
       Answer: B. provide cautious, limited emergency assistance and discontinue when the
emergency ends, ensuring competent follow-up is available
   Rationale: Ethical emergency practice allows limited assistance to prevent harm, provided the
practitioner acts cautiously and ensures proper referral afterward.

98. Which action best reflects ethical cooperation with other professionals?
   A. Refusing all collaboration to protect professional identity
   B. Collaborating when necessary and professionally appropriate to serve the client effectively
   C. Sharing confidential material without limits

 D. Letting nonqualified personnel make final clinical decisions
       Answer: B. Collaborating when necessary and professionally appropriate to serve the
client effectively
   Rationale: Ethical cooperation with other professionals is appropriate when it improves
service delivery and benefits the client.

99. A psychometrician administering tests in a clinic is most ethically justified in doing which of
the following?

   A. Independently diagnosing complex psychopathology without supervision
   B. Keeping raw protocols secure and operating within boundaries prescribed by RA 10029
   C. Conducting marriage therapy after office hours

 D. Delegating interpretation to clerical staff
       Answer: B. Keeping raw protocols secure and operating within boundaries prescribed by
RA 10029
   Rationale: Ethical psychometric practice requires protecting assessment materials and
remaining within the lawful scope of professional duties.

100. A developmental psychology review that integrates scientific knowledge with ethical
practice in the Philippines is most valid when it:

    A. focuses only on memorizing names and ignores application
    B. isolates developmental theory from legal-ethical realities
    C. combines life-span concepts, applied reasoning, and professional boundaries in practice
    D. avoids scenario-based questions because they are too difficult
  Answer: C. combines life-span concepts, applied reasoning, and professional boundaries

in practice
    Rationale: A strong professional review integrates theory, application, and ethical-legal

boundaries relevant to actual practice.
DEVELOPMENTAL PSYCHOLOGY
EXAM 4
DEVELOPMENTAL PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 4

1. Which statement best reflects the life-span perspective in developmental psychology?
  A. Development ends when biological maturity is reached.
  B. Development consists only of gains during childhood and losses during old age.
  C. Development is lifelong, multidimensional, and shaped by interacting influences.

 D. Development is determined mainly by heredity and is minimally affected by context.
       Answer: C. Development is lifelong, multidimensional, and shaped by interacting
influences.
  Rationale: This reflects the life-span perspective because development continues from
conception to death and is shaped by interacting biological, psychological, social, and
contextual influences.

2. A developmental psychologist wants to study how poverty, culture, and family structure jointly
influence learning outcomes. Which perspective is most directly emphasized?

  A. Contextual perspective
  B. Psychoanalytic perspective
  C. Strict behaviorist perspective

 D. Trait perspective
       Answer: A. Contextual perspective
  Rationale: The contextual perspective emphasizes that development must be understood
within social, cultural, family, and environmental systems that interact to shape outcomes.

3. Which of the following is the best example of a normative history-graded influence?
  A. A child develops asthma because of a genetic vulnerability
  B. A teenager experiences parental divorce
  C. A cohort's schooling is disrupted by a pandemic

 D. A woman enters menopause at midlife
       Answer: C. A cohort's schooling is disrupted by a pandemic
  Rationale: A normative history-graded influence affects many people in a generation at the
same historical time, such as a pandemic disrupting schooling.

4. In developmental research, a study that follows the same individuals from age 5 to age 25
uses which design?

  A. Cross-sectional
  B. Longitudinal
  C. Correlational

 D. Experimental simulation
       Answer: B. Longitudinal
  Rationale: A longitudinal design follows the same participants over an extended period to
examine developmental change over time.

5. A major strength of experimental research is that it:
  A. guarantees generalizability to all settings
  B. allows causal inference when properly controlled
  C. eliminates all ethical concerns

 D. avoids participant attrition
       Answer: B. allows causal inference when properly controlled
  Rationale: Experimental research permits stronger conclusions about cause and effect
because variables can be systematically manipulated and controlled.

6. Which pairing is correctly matched?
  A. Piaget -- psychosocial stages
  B. Erikson -- psychosexual stages
  C. Vygotsky -- sociocultural learning

 D. Bandura -- operant conditioning only
       Answer: C. Vygotsky -- sociocultural learning
  Rationale: Vygotsky is correctly matched with sociocultural learning because he emphasized
cognitive development through social interaction and guided participation.

7. A child can solve a problem only when a teacher provides hints, prompts, and step-by-step
support. Vygotsky would describe this as learning within the:

  A. latent trait structure
  B. zone of proximal development
  C. concrete operations lag

 D. reciprocal inhibition zone
       Answer: B. zone of proximal development
  Rationale: The zone of proximal development refers to tasks a learner cannot yet do
independently but can accomplish with guidance and support.

8. Which concept is most closely associated with Bronfenbrenner?
  A. Object permanence
  B. Bioecological systems
  C. Classical conditioning

 D. Identity foreclosure
       Answer: B. Bioecological systems
  Rationale: Bronfenbrenner is associated with the bioecological systems view, which explains
development through interacting environmental systems.

9. A researcher argues that development proceeds through a series of qualitatively distinct
stages. This position addresses which basic issue?

  A. Nature versus nurture
  B. Continuity versus discontinuity
  C. Reliability versus validity

 D. Sex versus gender
       Answer: B. Continuity versus discontinuity
  Rationale: A stage-based view assumes discontinuity because development is seen as
occurring through distinct qualitative shifts.
10. Which statement about heredity and environment is most accurate?
   A. Heredity determines genotype, whereas environment determines phenotype with no

overlap.
   B. Heredity and environment usually operate independently.
   C. Development reflects ongoing interaction between biological endowment and experience.

 D. Environment matters only when heredity is weak.
       Answer: C. Development reflects ongoing interaction between biological endowment and
experience.
   Rationale: Development is best understood as the product of continual interaction between
inherited potential and environmental experience.

11. During prenatal development, the period of most rapid differentiation of major organs occurs
in the:

   A. germinal stage
   B. embryonic stage
   C. fetal stage

 D. neonatal stage
       Answer: B. embryonic stage
   Rationale: The embryonic stage is the period of organ formation and the time when major
body structures rapidly differentiate.

12. Which maternal factor is most strongly associated with fetal alcohol spectrum disorder?
   A. High caffeine intake
   B. Exposure to loud sounds
   C. Alcohol use during pregnancy

 D. Mild maternal exercise
       Answer: C. Alcohol use during pregnancy
   Rationale: Fetal alcohol spectrum disorder results from prenatal exposure to alcohol during
pregnancy.

13. A baby is born weighing far below expected standards and is at elevated risk for
developmental complications. This infant is best described as:

   A. postmature
   B. low birth weight
   C. cephalocaudal delayed

 D. proximodistal immature
       Answer: B. low birth weight
   Rationale: Low birth weight infants face increased risk for medical and developmental
complications.

14. Which principle of physical growth states that development proceeds from the head
downward?

   A. Proximodistal
   B. Cephalocaudal
   C. Epigenetic

 D. Hierarchical
       Answer: B. Cephalocaudal
   Rationale: Cephalocaudal development refers to growth and control progressing from the
head downward toward the lower parts of the body.

15. The rooting, sucking, and Moro responses in newborns are best classified as:
   A. conditioned habits
   B. learned motor schemes
   C. reflexes

 D. temperament styles
       Answer: C. reflexes
   Rationale: These are innate, automatic responses present at birth that help survival and
indicate neurological functioning.

16. Piaget's sensorimotor stage is primarily characterized by the development of:
   A. abstract deductive logic
   B. symbolic moral reasoning
   C. knowledge through sensory and motor interaction

 D. formal hypothetical thinking
       Answer: C. knowledge through sensory and motor interaction
   Rationale: In the sensorimotor stage, infants learn about the world primarily through direct
sensory experience and physical action.

17. The understanding that objects continue to exist even when out of sight is called:
   A. conservation
   B. irreversibility
   C. object permanence

 D. centration
       Answer: C. object permanence
   Rationale: Object permanence is the understanding that objects still exist even when they are
no longer visible.

18. Habituation in infancy refers to:
   A. fear of unfamiliar stimuli
   B. decreasing response to repeated stimulation
   C. imitation of caregiver behavior

 D. distress from sensory overload
       Answer: B. decreasing response to repeated stimulation
   Rationale: Habituation occurs when an infant's response declines after repeated exposure to
the same stimulus, indicating recognition or learning.
19. Which finding most strongly challenges Piaget's original claim that infancy is cognitively very
limited?

   A. Infants show no preference for faces
   B. Infants may show earlier-than-expected object knowledge
   C. Toddlers cannot yet speak in sentences

 D. Preschoolers are egocentric
       Answer: B. Infants may show earlier-than-expected object knowledge
   Rationale: Research suggests infants demonstrate some understanding of object properties
earlier than Piaget originally proposed.

20. The classic debate on language acquisition is best summarized as:
   A. maturation versus attachment
   B. heredity versus nutrition
   C. nature versus nurture

 D. cognition versus emotion
       Answer: C. nature versus nurture
   Rationale: The major debate in language acquisition concerns the relative contribution of
innate biological readiness and environmental learning.

21. Noam Chomsky is most associated with the view that language development is supported
by:

   A. reinforcement histories alone
   B. an inborn capacity for language
   C. imitation without cognition

 D. peer modeling in adolescence
       Answer: B. an inborn capacity for language
   Rationale: Chomsky argued that humans possess an innate biological capacity that supports
language acquisition.

22. An infant forms a close emotional bond with a consistent caregiver and uses that person as
a secure base for exploration. This illustrates:

   A. autonomy
   B. attachment
   C. conservation

 D. deferred imitation
       Answer: B. attachment
   Rationale: Attachment is an enduring emotional bond that allows the caregiver to function as
a secure base for exploration.

23. According to Erikson, the central psychosocial task of infancy is:
   A. initiative versus guilt
   B. industry versus inferiority
   C. trust versus mistrust
   D. identity versus role confusion
  Answer: C. trust versus mistrust

   Rationale: Erikson identified trust versus mistrust as the central infant task, based on whether
caregiving is dependable and responsive.

24. A toddler insists, "Me do it!" when trying to put on shoes. This behavior most directly reflects:
   A. basic trust
   B. autonomy
   C. generativity

 D. intimacy
       Answer: B. autonomy
   Rationale: The behavior reflects the toddler's drive for independence, which is central to
autonomy versus shame and doubt.

25. Social referencing occurs when an infant:
   A. copies a sibling's homework behavior
   B. looks to a caregiver's emotional cues to guide behavior
   C. prefers social rewards over food rewards

 D. uses language to label people in the environment
       Answer: B. looks to a caregiver's emotional cues to guide behavior
   Rationale: Social referencing occurs when infants use another person's emotional reaction to
interpret uncertain situations.

26. Which parenting outcome is most strongly associated with warm, responsive, and
appropriately controlling caregiving?

   A. Learned helplessness
   B. Secure attachment and better self-regulation
   C. Persistent egocentrism

 D. Identity diffusion
       Answer: B. Secure attachment and better self-regulation
   Rationale: Warm and responsive caregiving with appropriate control supports secure
attachment and stronger self-regulatory capacities.

27. Failure to thrive in infancy is most likely when:
   A. caloric intake is excessive
   B. attachment and caregiving are severely disrupted
   C. motor development is advanced

 D. object permanence develops late
       Answer: B. attachment and caregiving are severely disrupted
   Rationale: Failure to thrive is often linked to neglect, poor caregiving, or severely disturbed
caregiver-child interaction.

28. In Piaget's preoperational stage, a child focuses on one striking aspect of a situation and
ignores others. This is called:

   A. conservation
   B. centration
   C. reversibility

 D. accommodation
       Answer: B. centration
   Rationale: Centration is the tendency to focus on one dimension of a situation while
neglecting others.

29. A child believes that a taller glass contains more juice even when the amount was merely
poured from a short glass. This error reflects lack of:

   A. object permanence
   B. attachment security
   C. conservation

 D. private speech
       Answer: C. conservation
   Rationale: The child lacks conservation because the child does not understand that quantity
remains the same despite changes in appearance.

30. Vygotsky viewed private speech mainly as:
   A. a sign of pathology
   B. immature echolalia with no function
   C. a tool for self-guidance and regulation

 D. evidence of delayed language development
       Answer: C. a tool for self-guidance and regulation
   Rationale: Vygotsky saw private speech as a helpful means by which children guide their own
thinking and behavior.

31. Which is a hallmark of theory of mind?
   A. Knowing that all rules are fixed
   B. Understanding that others may hold false beliefs
   C. Classifying objects by shape

 D. Recalling a list of digits backward
       Answer: B. Understanding that others may hold false beliefs
   Rationale: Theory of mind involves recognizing that other people can have thoughts, beliefs,
and perspectives different from one's own.

32. According to Erikson, the major psychosocial conflict in early childhood is:
   A. trust versus mistrust
   B. initiative versus guilt
   C. industry versus inferiority

 D. ego integrity versus despair
       Answer: B. initiative versus guilt
   Rationale: Erikson identified initiative versus guilt as the key early childhood task because
children become increasingly purposeful and self-directed.
33. A child spends time pretending to be a doctor while assigning roles to peers. This best
illustrates:

   A. parallel play only
   B. associative neglect
   C. imaginative socio-dramatic play

 D. formal operational reasoning
       Answer: C. imaginative socio-dramatic play
   Rationale: Socio-dramatic play involves pretend roles, shared scenarios, and coordinated
make-believe with others.

34. Which statement about parenting styles is most accurate?
   A. Authoritative parenting combines warmth with firm control.
   B. Authoritarian parenting is always optimal across all cultures.
   C. Permissive parenting emphasizes high control and low warmth.

 D. Neglectful parenting is marked by high responsiveness.
       Answer: A. Authoritative parenting combines warmth with firm control.
   Rationale: Authoritative parenting is defined by high responsiveness together with clear
expectations and appropriate control.

35. In middle childhood, children typically move into Piaget's stage of:
   A. sensorimotor thought
   B. preoperational thought
   C. concrete operational thought

 D. postformal thought
       Answer: C. concrete operational thought
   Rationale: Middle childhood is typically associated with concrete operational thinking,
including logical reasoning about tangible situations.

36. A school-age child understands conservation, seriation, and classification but struggles with
abstract hypotheticals. This profile best fits:

   A. preoperational thought
   B. concrete operational thought
   C. formal operational thought

 D. postformal thought
       Answer: B. concrete operational thought
   Rationale: Concrete operational thinkers can reason logically about concrete information but
still have difficulty with abstract hypothetical problems.

37. Metamemory refers to:
   A. memory loss due to trauma
   B. awareness of how memory works
   C. unconscious repression

 D. reflexive recall in infancy
       Answer: B. awareness of how memory works
   Rationale: Metamemory is knowledge and awareness about memory processes, including
strategies for remembering.

38. Which ability improves markedly in middle childhood and helps children follow multistep
instructions and solve problems?

   A. Executive functioning
   B. Sensorimotor adaptation
   C. Neonatal reflex integration

 D. Ego diffusion
       Answer: A. Executive functioning
   Rationale: Executive functioning improves in middle childhood and supports planning,
attention control, inhibition, and organized problem solving.

39. A child's belief that "I am good at math but weak in drawing" best reflects development of:
   A. object permanence
   B. representational self-concept
   C. ego integrity

 D. social smile
       Answer: B. representational self-concept
   Rationale: This reflects a more differentiated self-concept in which children describe
themselves in specific domains.

40. Erikson identified the key psychosocial task of middle childhood as:
   A. industry versus inferiority
   B. intimacy versus isolation
   C. autonomy versus shame

 D. identity versus confusion
       Answer: A. industry versus inferiority
   Rationale: Industry versus inferiority centers on developing competence and confidence in
school, work, and social tasks.

41. Repeated peer victimization involving power imbalance and intent to harm is called:
   A. scaffolding
   B. bullying
   C. accommodation

 D. social referencing
       Answer: B. bullying
   Rationale: Bullying involves repeated harmful behavior in which there is a power imbalance
between the aggressor and the victim.

42. During puberty, the hormonal process that triggers sexual maturation primarily involves the:
   A. limbic-only circuit
   B. hypothalamic-pituitary-gonadal axis
   C. enteric nervous system
 D. peripheral sensory tract
       Answer: B. hypothalamic-pituitary-gonadal axis
   Rationale: Sexual maturation is triggered by endocrine activity involving the hypothalamus,
pituitary gland, and gonads.

43. Adolescents often feel as though everyone is watching them. Elkind called this:
   A. identity achievement
   B. imaginary audience
   C. self-efficacy

 D. social clock
       Answer: B. imaginary audience
   Rationale: The imaginary audience refers to adolescent egocentrism in which adolescents
believe others are constantly observing and evaluating them.

44. Piaget's formal operational stage is marked by the ability to:
   A. think only in concrete terms
   B. use hypothetical-deductive reasoning
   C. rely exclusively on trial and error

 D. understand only immediate sensory input
       Answer: B. use hypothetical-deductive reasoning
   Rationale: Formal operational thought includes abstract, systematic, and
hypothetical-deductive reasoning.

45. Kohlberg's theory is primarily concerned with development of:
   A. language syntax
   B. moral reasoning
   C. attachment behavior

 D. emotional contagion
       Answer: B. moral reasoning
   Rationale: Kohlberg's theory focuses on how people reason about moral issues and justice.

46. Carol Gilligan is best known for emphasizing:
   A. operant conditioning
   B. an ethic of care in moral development
   C. psychosocial foreclosure

 D. ecological motor development
       Answer: B. an ethic of care in moral development
   Rationale: Gilligan emphasized that moral reasoning may also be grounded in care,
relationships, and responsibility to others.

47. Which adolescent is most likely to be in Marcia's moratorium status?
   A. One who has explored alternatives but has not yet committed
   B. One with strong commitment without prior exploration
   C. One who avoids both exploration and commitment
 D. One whose identity is fully integrated and stable
       Answer: A. One who has explored alternatives but has not yet committed
   Rationale: Moratorium refers to active exploration of alternatives without a firm commitment
yet.

48. According to Erikson, the psychosocial crisis of adolescence is:
   A. initiative versus guilt
   B. identity versus identity confusion
   C. intimacy versus isolation

 D. generativity versus stagnation
       Answer: B. identity versus identity confusion
   Rationale: Erikson described adolescence as the period of forming a coherent identity rather
than experiencing confusion about roles and self.

49. Which statement about adolescent-parent relationships is most accurate?
   A. Serious conflict is universal and necessary for normal development.
   B. Adolescence always leads to emotional detachment from parents.
   C. Most adolescents maintain attachment to parents while seeking autonomy.

 D. Peer influence completely replaces family influence.
       Answer: C. Most adolescents maintain attachment to parents while seeking autonomy.
   Rationale: Most adolescents continue to value parental attachment while also working toward
greater independence.

50. Juvenile delinquency is best understood as:
   A. caused solely by heredity
   B. unrelated to peer and family influences
   C. shaped by interacting biological, family, peer, and community factors

 D. a normal stage all adolescents pass through
       Answer: C. shaped by interacting biological, family, peer, and community factors
   Rationale: Delinquency is best explained by multiple interacting influences rather than a
single cause.

51. The term emerging adulthood is most often used for the period characterized by exploration
and instability between:

   A. ages 10 to 14
   B. ages 15 to 17
   C. late teens through the twenties

 D. ages 40 to 60
       Answer: C. late teens through the twenties
   Rationale: Emerging adulthood refers to the period from the late teens through the twenties
marked by identity exploration and transition.

52. Which ability is most consistent with adult cognition beyond adolescence?
   A. Decreased capacity for reflective thought
   B. Greater ability to handle ambiguity and practical problems
   C. Complete replacement of emotion by logic

 D. Loss of all idealism and moral concern
       Answer: B. Greater ability to handle ambiguity and practical problems
   Rationale: Adult cognition often becomes more reflective, flexible, and practical in dealing
with complex real-life issues.

53. Sternberg's triarchic theory includes:
   A. sensorimotor, preoperational, concrete
   B. classical, operant, observational
   C. analytical, creative, and practical intelligence

 D. trust, autonomy, and initiative
       Answer: C. analytical, creative, and practical intelligence
   Rationale: Sternberg's triarchic theory proposes that intelligence includes analytical, creative,
and practical components.

54. Emotional intelligence refers to the capacity to:
   A. eliminate emotion from reasoning
   B. understand and regulate emotions
   C. memorize emotional words efficiently

 D. avoid all interpersonal conflict
       Answer: B. understand and regulate emotions
   Rationale: Emotional intelligence involves recognizing, understanding, and managing one's
own emotions and those of others.

55. A major developmental task in emerging and young adulthood, according to Erikson, is:
   A. industry
   B. integrity
   C. intimacy

 D. autonomy
       Answer: C. intimacy
   Rationale: Erikson viewed intimacy versus isolation as the major young adult task, involving
formation of close committed relationships.

56. Which factor is most strongly associated with higher relationship stability in young
adulthood?

   A. Impulsivity and poor communication
   B. Mutual commitment and effective conflict management
   C. Avoidance of all disagreements

 D. Dependence on peer approval
       Answer: B. Mutual commitment and effective conflict management
   Rationale: Relationship stability is strongly supported by commitment, communication, and
constructive conflict resolution.
57. Parenthood is best viewed developmentally as:
   A. uniformly stressful and maladaptive
   B. irrelevant to adult identity
   C. a transition that can bring both strain and growth

 D. protective against all marital dissatisfaction
       Answer: C. a transition that can bring both strain and growth
   Rationale: Parenthood is a developmental transition that can increase stress while also
fostering growth, meaning, and identity change.

58. In middle adulthood, fluid intelligence generally:
   A. sharply increases without interruption
   B. remains identical to adolescent levels
   C. tends to decline more than crystallized intelligence

 D. replaces crystallized intelligence
       Answer: C. tends to decline more than crystallized intelligence
   Rationale: Fluid intelligence, which involves solving novel problems, tends to decline earlier
and more than crystallized intelligence.

59. Crystallized intelligence refers to:
   A. rapid novel problem solving
   B. accumulated knowledge and verbal skill
   C. motor speed under pressure

 D. abstract reasoning in infancy
       Answer: B. accumulated knowledge and verbal skill
   Rationale: Crystallized intelligence refers to the accumulation of knowledge, vocabulary, and
learned skills over time.

60. Expertise in midlife often allows adults to:
   A. avoid all age-related cognitive changes
   B. perform efficiently in familiar domains
   C. eliminate the need for deliberate practice

 D. solve all novel tasks better than younger adults
       Answer: B. perform efficiently in familiar domains
   Rationale: Expertise allows adults to use extensive knowledge and experience to perform
efficiently in practiced areas.

61. Erikson described the central psychosocial challenge of middle adulthood as:
   A. trust versus mistrust
   B. intimacy versus isolation
   C. generativity versus stagnation

 D. ego integrity versus despair
       Answer: C. generativity versus stagnation
   Rationale: Generativity versus stagnation involves contributing to society and guiding the next
generation rather than becoming self-absorbed.
62. Generativity is best defined as:
   A. fear of mortality
   B. concern for guiding the next generation
   C. withdrawal from social obligations

 D. resistance to identity change
       Answer: B. concern for guiding the next generation
   Rationale: Generativity involves caring for, guiding, and contributing to the welfare of younger
generations and society.

63. The so-called "midlife crisis" is best characterized as:
   A. universal and biologically inevitable
   B. a myth with no basis in any adult experience
   C. a possible but nonuniversal pattern influenced by context and meaning

 D. identical across cultures and genders
       Answer: C. a possible but nonuniversal pattern influenced by context and meaning
   Rationale: Research shows that a midlife crisis is not universal and depends on individual
circumstances, interpretation, and context.

64. The "empty nest" is most accurately described as:
   A. always producing severe depression in parents
   B. a transition whose effects vary depending on context and prior family relationships
   C. evidence of failed attachment

 D. irrelevant to midlife adjustment
       Answer: B. a transition whose effects vary depending on context and prior family
relationships
   Rationale: The empty nest is a transition that may be experienced positively or negatively
depending on family history, role investment, and context.

65. In late adulthood, which concept refers to adapting by selecting goals, optimizing strengths,
and compensating for losses?

   A. Social referencing
   B. Selective optimization with compensation
   C. Identity foreclosure

 D. Classical conditioning
       Answer: B. Selective optimization with compensation
   Rationale: This concept describes adaptive aging through choosing priorities, maximizing
strengths, and compensating for limitations.

66. Which statement about aging is most accurate?
   A. All older adults show severe cognitive impairment.
   B. Aging is uniform across individuals.
   C. Late adulthood involves both losses and potentials for adaptation.
   D. Personality disappears in old age.
  Answer: C. Late adulthood involves both losses and potentials for adaptation.

   Rationale: Aging involves both decline and resilience, with substantial individual differences
and capacity for adaptation.

67. Which memory ability tends to be relatively preserved longest in normal aging?
   A. Speeded working memory in novel tasks
   B. Procedural memory for well-practiced skills
   C. Immediate recall under divided attention

 D. All forms of episodic recall
       Answer: B. Procedural memory for well-practiced skills
   Rationale: Procedural memory for familiar, well-practiced actions is often relatively preserved
in normal aging.

68. Wisdom in late adulthood is best described as:
   A. photographic memory
   B. rigid adherence to tradition
   C. expert knowledge about life and sound judgment

 D. absence of emotional conflict
       Answer: C. expert knowledge about life and sound judgment
   Rationale: Wisdom involves deep life knowledge, judgment, and insight in handling human
problems and life complexities.

69. Erikson's final psychosocial stage is:
   A. identity versus confusion
   B. intimacy versus isolation
   C. generativity versus stagnation

 D. ego integrity versus despair
       Answer: D. ego integrity versus despair
   Rationale: Erikson's final stage concerns evaluating one's life as meaningful and acceptable
rather than experiencing regret and despair.

70. An older adult who accepts both achievements and regrets and feels life has had meaning is
showing:

   A. despair
   B. ego integrity
   C. stagnation

 D. foreclosure
       Answer: B. ego integrity
   Rationale: Ego integrity is reflected in acceptance of one's life as meaningful despite
imperfections or regrets.

71. Which factor is most protective for psychological well-being in late adulthood?
   A. Complete disengagement from all roles
   B. Absolute independence from others
   C. Supportive social relationships

 D. Avoidance of all reflection on the past
       Answer: C. Supportive social relationships
   Rationale: Strong and supportive social ties are consistently associated with better mental
health and adjustment in late adulthood.

72. Widowhood adjustment is generally easier when:
   A. the person is socially isolated
   B. grief is denied immediately
   C. there are coping resources and social support

 D. all reminders of the spouse are eliminated at once
       Answer: C. there are coping resources and social support
   Rationale: Adjustment to widowhood is generally better when the bereaved person has
emotional, practical, and social resources available.

73. Bereavement refers to:
   A. the biological cessation of life
   B. the social status and experience of having suffered a loss
   C. denial of impending death

 D. physician-assisted dying
       Answer: B. the social status and experience of having suffered a loss
   Rationale: Bereavement refers to the condition or status of having lost someone through
death.

74. Grief is best understood as:
   A. a fixed sequence everyone follows identically
   B. an emotional response to loss that varies across persons and cultures
   C. always pathological if prolonged beyond two weeks

 D. unrelated to attachment
       Answer: B. an emotional response to loss that varies across persons and cultures
   Rationale: Grief is a response to loss that differs in pattern, timing, and expression across
individuals and cultures.

75. Which loss is often socially unrecognized and may therefore complicate mourning?
   A. Retirement
   B. Ambiguous or disenfranchised loss
   C. Graduation

 D. Geographic relocation only
       Answer: B. Ambiguous or disenfranchised loss
   Rationale: Ambiguous or disenfranchised losses may lack clear recognition or closure,
making mourning more difficult.

76. In end-of-life ethics, an advance directive is primarily intended to:
   A. guarantee euthanasia on request
   B. record a person's treatment wishes when future incapacity may occur
   C. transfer all decisions to the state

 D. eliminate all family involvement
       Answer: B. record a person's treatment wishes when future incapacity may occur
   Rationale: An advance directive helps preserve personal autonomy by documenting
treatment preferences before incapacity occurs.

77. Compared with early adulthood, late adulthood is often associated with:
   A. less concern with meaning
   B. more avoidance of life review
   C. greater salience of mortality and legacy

 D. disappearance of spiritual concerns
       Answer: C. greater salience of mortality and legacy
   Rationale: In late adulthood, awareness of mortality often heightens reflection on meaning,
legacy, and life review.

78. Which statement best reflects current developmental understanding of death across the life
span?

   A. Children and adults understand death in exactly the same way.
   B. Understanding of death changes with cognitive development and experience.
   C. Adolescents rarely think about mortality.

 D. Older adults universally fear death more than all younger groups.
       Answer: B. Understanding of death changes with cognitive development and experience.
   Rationale: Concepts of death develop over time and are shaped by age-related cognitive
growth and life experience.

79. Under RA 10029 and the PAP Code, which statement is most accurate?
   A. Any psychology graduate may independently practice as a psychologist.
   B. Only licensed and registered psychologists and psychometricians are legally allowed to

practice their profession.
   C. Licensure is optional if one works online.

 D. Registration is required only for test interpretation.
       Answer: B. Only licensed and registered psychologists and psychometricians are legally
allowed to practice their profession.
   Rationale: RA 10029 and the PAP Code specify that legal practice of psychology and
psychometrics requires proper licensure and registration.

80. A psychometrician is asked to conduct a highly specialized forensic evaluation beyond
current training. The most ethical response is to:

   A. accept the case to gain experience
   B. proceed if the client insists
   C. refuse or refer unless competence is first obtained

 D. administer tests and let the lawyer interpret them
       Answer: C. refuse or refer unless competence is first obtained
   Rationale: Ethical practice requires working only within one's competence and making
appropriate referrals when expertise is lacking.

81. Which principle is violated when a practitioner continues working despite serious personal
problems that impair judgment and service quality?

   A. Beneficence through persistence
   B. Maintaining competence and self-monitoring
   C. Social facilitation

 D. Normative adaptation
       Answer: B. Maintaining competence and self-monitoring
   Rationale: Practitioners must monitor how personal problems affect their functioning and limit
or suspend work when competence is impaired.

82. A practitioner becomes aware that another psychologist may have committed an ethical
violation likely to cause substantial harm. The Code indicates that the practitioner should:

   A. always post the allegation publicly
   B. ignore the matter to preserve collegiality
   C. take further action and report to appropriate authorities when warranted

 D. destroy relevant records
       Answer: C. take further action and report to appropriate authorities when warranted
   Rationale: When likely substantial harm exists, the Code supports taking further appropriate
action and reporting the matter through proper channels.

83. Before beginning assessment or therapy, the practitioner should primarily:
   A. avoid discussing risks to prevent anxiety
   B. obtain informed consent using reasonably understandable language
   C. rely only on implied consent in all cases

 D. postpone all discussion of confidentiality until termination
       Answer: B. obtain informed consent using reasonably understandable language
   Rationale: Ethical practice requires informed consent that is clearly explained in language the
client can reasonably understand.

84. When services are court ordered, the practitioner should:
   A. assume consent is unnecessary and give no explanation
   B. inform the individual about the nature of services and limits of confidentiality
   C. keep all information fully confidential from the court

 D. provide only raw test data directly to all parties
       Answer: B. inform the individual about the nature of services and limits of confidentiality
   Rationale: Even when services are mandated, the person should still be informed about the
nature of services and the limits of confidentiality.

85. Which of the following best illustrates a multiple relationship?
   A. Administering a test to a referred client
   B. Conducting therapy with a current client while also entering a business partnership with
that client

   C. Consulting with a colleague about a case without identifiers

 D. Referring a client to a physician
       Answer: B. Conducting therapy with a current client while also entering a business
partnership with that client
   Rationale: A multiple relationship exists when a practitioner has another significant role with a
person with whom there is already a professional relationship.

86. A practitioner provides services through telepsychology. According to the Code, the
practitioner should:

   A. assume online work is exempt from usual ethical standards
   B. apply the same ethical principles that govern face-to-face services
   C. focus only on convenience, not privacy

 D. avoid documenting consent because sessions are virtual
       Answer: B. apply the same ethical principles that govern face-to-face services
   Rationale: The Code states that telepsychology is governed by the same ethical principles
that apply to in-person psychological services.
