87. Which statement best reflects ethical confidentiality?
   A. Confidentiality has no limits under any circumstance.
   B. Confidentiality may be limited by law, danger, or other valid ethical and legal grounds.
   C. Confidentiality applies only to written records.

 D. Confidentiality belongs solely to the referral source.
       Answer: B. Confidentiality may be limited by law, danger, or other valid ethical and legal
grounds.
   Rationale: Confidentiality is fundamental but not absolute, since legal requirements and
protection from harm can justify limited disclosure.

88. Before recording a client's voice or image, the practitioner must:
   A. record first and explain later
   B. obtain consent and explain anticipated uses
   C. rely on clinic ownership of equipment

 D. ask only a family member
       Answer: B. obtain consent and explain anticipated uses
   Rationale: Ethical recording requires prior consent and clear explanation of how the recording
will be used.

89. Which practice is most ethical regarding assessment tools?
   A. Using photocopied test materials if the client cannot pay
   B. Selecting tests irrelevant to the referral to gather more data
   C. Using standardized, valid, reliable tools appropriate to the client

 D. Administering the same battery to everyone regardless of language
       Answer: C. Using standardized, valid, reliable tools appropriate to the client
   Rationale: Ethical assessment requires the use of psychometrically sound tools that are
relevant and appropriate to the client and referral question.

90. A client requests raw test scores and item responses after assessment. Under the Code, the
best response is:

   A. release all raw data automatically to any requester
   B. refuse all feedback of any kind
   C. explain results appropriately but do not release raw test data except when legally required

 D. post the results to the referral source's portal without consent
       Answer: C. explain results appropriately but do not release raw test data except when
legally required
   Rationale: Ethical practice supports giving understandable feedback while protecting
restricted raw test data unless release is legally mandated.

91. In explaining test findings to parents or teachers, the practitioner should:
   A. use highly technical language to preserve authority
   B. communicate in clear nontechnical language
   C. provide only percentile ranks

 D. avoid discussing limitations of findings
       Answer: B. communicate in clear nontechnical language
   Rationale: Test findings should be explained in language that intended recipients can clearly
understand.

92. A psychometrician is asked to let an unqualified office staff member administer a restricted
psychological test alone. The best response is:

   A. allow it if the staff member promises confidentiality
   B. allow it when the office is busy
   C. decline because assessment by unqualified persons is unethical

 D. allow it if scoring is done later by a psychologist
       Answer: C. decline because assessment by unqualified persons is unethical
   Rationale: Restricted psychological assessment must not be administered by unqualified
persons because doing so violates professional standards.

93. Which action best reflects ethical public statements by psychology practitioners?
   A. Exaggerating success rates to attract clients
   B. Making false claims about credentials on social media
   C. Providing accurate, nondeceptive information about services and qualifications

 D. Advertising guaranteed outcomes for therapy
       Answer: C. Providing accurate, nondeceptive information about services and qualifications
   Rationale: Ethical public statements must be truthful, accurate, and not misleading about
qualifications or services.

94. A client referred by an employer asks whether the practitioner can keep all assessment
findings secret from the company. The best initial response is to:
   A. promise full secrecy immediately
   B. clarify at the outset who the client is, probable uses of information, and limits of
confidentiality
   C. refuse the referral automatically

 D. submit all data directly to coworkers
       Answer: B. clarify at the outset who the client is, probable uses of information, and limits
of confidentiality
   Rationale: In third-party referrals, the practitioner must clarify roles, intended recipients of
information, and confidentiality limits at the outset.

95. Which of the following best reflects the Code's stance on exploitation?
   A. It is acceptable if the client benefits financially
   B. It is prohibited to exploit those under one's authority
   C. It applies only to sexual exploitation

 D. It is allowed in teaching settings
       Answer: B. It is prohibited to exploit those under one's authority
   Rationale: The Code prohibits exploiting clients, students, supervisees, employees, or others
over whom the practitioner has authority.

96. A practitioner delegates part of service delivery to an assistant. Ethical delegation requires
that the practitioner:

   A. delegate any task to reduce workload
   B. assign only tasks the assistant can perform competently with proper supervision
   C. avoid telling the client

 D. delegate only clerical duties and never interpretation
       Answer: B. assign only tasks the assistant can perform competently with proper
supervision
   Rationale: Ethical delegation requires that assigned tasks match the assistant's competence
and that adequate supervision be provided.

97. Which developmental concept is most directly relevant when a psychologist interprets a
child's test result in light of cultural and language background?

   A. Conservation
   B. Contextual influences on development
   C. Imaginary audience

 D. Basic trust
       Answer: B. Contextual influences on development
   Rationale: Interpreting results in light of culture and language reflects the principle that
development and assessment must be understood within context.

98. A board-style item asks which proponent is correctly matched with the theory. Which option
is correct?

   A. Bowlby -- operant conditioning
   B. Ainsworth -- attachment patterns
   C. Marcia -- psychosexual stages

 D. Schaie -- ecological systems theory
       Answer: B. Ainsworth -- attachment patterns
   Rationale: Ainsworth is correctly associated with attachment patterns through her work on the
Strange Situation.

99. Which theorist is most associated with adult cognitive development as involving life-span
stages of use of intellect?

   A. Schaie
   B. Skinner
   C. Watson

 D. Gesell
       Answer: A. Schaie
   Rationale: Schaie is associated with a life-span model describing changing uses of intellect
across adulthood.

100. A psychologist handling an online assessment session notices repeated connectivity
problems during a timed test. The most ethical action is to:

    A. ignore the interruptions because standardization must never be adjusted
    B. continue and interpret scores as fully comparable
    C. document the problem, inform the client of its implications, and qualify interpretation as
needed

 D. delete the session and provide no explanation
        Answer: C. document the problem, inform the client of its implications, and qualify
interpretation as needed
    Rationale: Ethical teleassessment requires documenting disruptions, informing the client,
and interpreting results cautiously when standardization is compromised.
DEVELOPMENTAL PSYCHOLOGY
EXAM 5
DEVELOPMENTAL PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 5

1. Which statement best reflects the life-span perspective in developmental psychology?
  A. Development ends when biological maturity is reached.
  B. Development is shaped only by hereditary factors.
  C. Development involves both gains and losses across the entire life span.

 D. Development follows a fixed universal sequence unaffected by culture.
       Answer: C. Development involves both gains and losses across the entire life span.
  Rationale: The life-span perspective emphasizes that development is lifelong and includes
both growth and decline across different domains.

2. A developmental psychologist studies how retirement affects identity, health behavior, and
family roles. This work best illustrates which principle?

  A. Development is limited to childhood
  B. Development is multidimensional and multidirectional
  C. Development is exclusively cognitive

 D. Development is determined primarily by maturation
       Answer: B. Development is multidimensional and multidirectional
  Rationale: The example involves multiple domains (identity, health, family roles),
demonstrating that development occurs across various dimensions and directions.

3. A child enters school during a nationwide economic crisis that affects nutrition, stress, and
academic opportunity. This is best classified as a:

  A. normative age-graded influence
  B. normative history-graded influence
  C. nonnormative influence

 D. maturational influence
       Answer: B. normative history-graded influence
  Rationale: A widespread event affecting a large group at a particular historical time is a
normative history-graded influence.

4. Which of the following is the best example of a nonnormative influence?
  A. Pubertal onset
  B. Entering Grade 1
  C. Menopause

 D. Surviving a major earthquake that destroyed one's home
       Answer: D. Surviving a major earthquake that destroyed one's home
  Rationale: Nonnormative influences are irregular and uncommon events that affect individuals
in unique ways.

5. In Piaget's theory, cognitive growth occurs partly because children:
  A. are conditioned by reinforcement schedules
  B. resolve unconscious conflicts
  C. actively construct understanding through assimilation and accommodation
 D. imitate adult behavior without restructuring thought
       Answer: C. actively construct understanding through assimilation and accommodation
  Rationale: Piaget emphasized active construction of knowledge through assimilation and
accommodation processes.

6. Vygotsky would most likely emphasize that children learn best when:
  A. they are left to discover everything independently
  B. tasks are slightly beyond their current ability and guided by a more competent other
  C. rewards are withheld until mastery occurs

 D. biological maturation is complete before instruction begins
       Answer: B. tasks are slightly beyond their current ability and guided by a more competent
other
  Rationale: Vygotsky's concept of the zone of proximal development highlights guided learning
with assistance from more knowledgeable individuals.

7. In developmental research, which design is most vulnerable to cohort effects?
  A. Longitudinal
  B. Cross-sectional
  C. Sequential

 D. Experimental
       Answer: B. Cross-sectional
  Rationale: Cross-sectional designs compare different age groups at one time, making them
susceptible to cohort differences.

8. Which statement most accurately distinguishes critical and sensitive periods?
  A. Both terms refer only to prenatal growth.
  B. A critical period is an exact age when learning must occur, whereas a sensitive period is a

time of heightened responsiveness.
  C. Sensitive periods apply only to language.

 D. Critical periods can be extended indefinitely through training.
       Answer: B. A critical period is an exact age when learning must occur, whereas a sensitive
period is a time of heightened responsiveness.
  Rationale: Critical periods are narrow and essential, while sensitive periods are broader
windows of optimal learning.

9. Which perspective would be most likely to explain behavior in terms of unconscious
motivation and early experience?

  A. Psychoanalytic
  B. Information-processing
  C. Behaviorist

 D. Evolutionary
       Answer: A. Psychoanalytic
  Rationale: Psychoanalytic theory focuses on unconscious processes and early developmental
experiences.
10. A fertilized ovum divides repeatedly and forms a blastocyst before implantation. This
process occurs during the:

   A. fetal period
   B. germinal period
   C. embryonic period

 D. neonatal period
       Answer: B. germinal period
   Rationale: The germinal period includes fertilization, cell division, and implantation.

11. Which chromosomal condition results from an extra chromosome 21?
   A. Turner syndrome
   B. Klinefelter syndrome
   C. Down syndrome

 D. Fragile X syndrome
       Answer: C. Down syndrome
   Rationale: Down syndrome is caused by trisomy 21.

12. A trait influenced by multiple genes, such as skin color or height, best illustrates:
   A. dominant inheritance
   B. recessive inheritance
   C. polygenic inheritance

 D. sex-linked inheritance
       Answer: C. polygenic inheritance
   Rationale: Polygenic inheritance involves multiple genes contributing to a single trait.

13. Which maternal factor poses the greatest risk for fetal alcohol spectrum disorders?
   A. Low calcium intake
   B. Alcohol consumption during pregnancy
   C. Moderate maternal exercise

 D. Delayed clamping of the umbilical cord
       Answer: B. Alcohol consumption during pregnancy
   Rationale: Alcohol exposure during pregnancy directly causes fetal alcohol spectrum
disorders.

14. The principle that development proceeds from the head downward is called:
   A. proximodistal
   B. cephalocaudal
   C. hierarchical

 D. maturational lag
       Answer: B. cephalocaudal
   Rationale: Cephalocaudal development describes growth from head to tail.

15. A newborn turns toward a nipple when the cheek is stroked. This is the:
   A. Babinski reflex
   B. Moro reflex
   C. rooting reflex

 D. grasping reflex
       Answer: C. rooting reflex
   Rationale: The rooting reflex helps infants locate food by turning toward touch on the cheek.

16. Which infant is at greatest developmental risk?
   A. A full-term infant weighing 3.2 kilograms
   B. A postmature infant with no complications
   C. A low-birth-weight infant born preterm

 D. A newborn with strong reflexes and average Apgar score
       Answer: C. A low-birth-weight infant born preterm
   Rationale: Preterm low-birth-weight infants have increased risk for developmental
complications.

17. According to dynamic systems theory, motor development:
   A. unfolds solely from genetic programming
   B. is unrelated to perception and motivation
   C. emerges from the interaction of multiple systems

 D. depends only on neuromuscular maturation
       Answer: C. emerges from the interaction of multiple systems
   Rationale: Motor development arises from interactions among physical, cognitive, and
environmental factors.

18. Habituation in infancy refers to:
   A. distress when a caregiver leaves
   B. decreased response after repeated exposure to a stimulus
   C. repeating an adult's exact movements

 D. conditioning through reinforcement
       Answer: B. decreased response after repeated exposure to a stimulus
   Rationale: Habituation is a basic learning process involving reduced response to familiar
stimuli.

19. Object permanence refers to the understanding that:
   A. symbols can stand for real objects
   B. hidden objects continue to exist
   C. objects move only when touched

 D. actions cause predictable outcomes
       Answer: B. hidden objects continue to exist
   Rationale: Object permanence is the awareness that objects exist even when out of sight.

20. A toddler calls all four-legged animals "dog." This is an example of:
   A. underextension
   B. overregularization
   C. overextension

 D. telegraphic speech
       Answer: C. overextension
   Rationale: Overextension occurs when a word is applied too broadly.

21. Chomsky's major contribution to language development was the proposal that:
   A. language is learned only through imitation
   B. language acquisition is supported by an innate predisposition
   C. grammar develops after formal schooling

 D. reinforcement is sufficient to explain syntax
       Answer: B. language acquisition is supported by an innate predisposition
   Rationale: Chomsky proposed an inborn capacity for language acquisition.

22. Which infant behavior best reflects social referencing?
   A. Crying when hungry
   B. Looking to a caregiver's facial expression before approaching an unfamiliar object
   C. Repeating a new word several times

 D. Searching for a hidden toy
       Answer: B. Looking to a caregiver's facial expression before approaching an unfamiliar
object
   Rationale: Social referencing involves using others' emotional cues to guide behavior.

23. In Erikson's first psychosocial crisis, healthy development leads primarily to:
   A. autonomy
   B. initiative
   C. trust

 D. identity
       Answer: C. trust
   Rationale: Consistent caregiving fosters a sense of trust in infancy.

24. Ainsworth's securely attached infant is most likely to:
   A. ignore the caregiver during reunion
   B. be distressed by separation and comforted upon reunion
   C. show no preference between caregiver and stranger

 D. resist contact and remain inconsolable
       Answer: B. be distressed by separation and comforted upon reunion
   Rationale: Secure attachment involves distress upon separation and comfort upon reunion.

25. Temperament refers to:
   A. learned moral standards
   B. stable individual differences in emotional reactivity and self-regulation
   C. attachment classifications
   D. parental discipline strategies
  Answer: B. stable individual differences in emotional reactivity and self-regulation

   Rationale: Temperament describes biologically based emotional and behavioral tendencies.

26. A toddler insists on feeding herself and says "No!" frequently. This behavior is most
consistent with Erikson's stage of:

   A. trust versus mistrust
   B. autonomy versus shame and doubt
   C. initiative versus guilt

 D. industry versus inferiority
       Answer: B. autonomy versus shame and doubt
   Rationale: Toddlerhood is characterized by striving for independence and self-control,
reflecting autonomy.

27. In early childhood, egocentrism means that a child:
   A. is selfish and intentionally rude
   B. cannot take another person's perspective easily
   C. is unable to use symbols

 D. lacks memory for past events
       Answer: B. cannot take another person's perspective easily
   Rationale: Egocentrism refers to difficulty in perspective-taking, not selfish intent.

28. Conservation failure in preschoolers most strongly suggests difficulty with:
   A. reversibility
   B. object permanence
   C. deferred imitation

 D. operant conditioning
       Answer: A. reversibility
   Rationale: Preschoolers struggle to mentally reverse actions, leading to conservation errors.

29. Theory of mind refers to the developing ability to:
   A. memorize abstract rules
   B. understand that others have mental states different from one's own
   C. distinguish fantasy from play

 D. classify objects into hierarchies
       Answer: B. understand that others have mental states different from one's own
   Rationale: Theory of mind involves recognizing others' thoughts, beliefs, and intentions.

30. Which type of play involves children acting out imaginary roles?
   A. Functional play
   B. Constructive play
   C. Dramatic play

 D. Parallel play
       Answer: C. Dramatic play
   Rationale: Dramatic play involves role-playing and imagination.
31. According to Baumrind, which parenting style combines warmth with firm control and
explanation?

   A. Authoritarian
   B. Authoritative
   C. Permissive

 D. Neglectful
       Answer: B. Authoritative
   Rationale: Authoritative parenting balances responsiveness and demandingness.

32. A preschooler avoids touching a hot stove because she has internalized parental standards.
This reflects early:

   A. sensorimotor coordination
   B. social referencing
   C. conscience development

 D. identity achievement
       Answer: C. conscience development
   Rationale: Internalizing rules and standards reflects emerging conscience.

33. Middle childhood is marked by Piaget's stage of:
   A. preoperational thought
   B. formal operations
   C. concrete operations

 D. sensorimotor intelligence
       Answer: C. concrete operations
   Rationale: Children develop logical thinking about concrete objects during this stage.

34. Which skill typically improves markedly in middle childhood?
   A. Object permanence
   B. Hypothetical-deductive reasoning
   C. Conservation and classification

 D. Symbolic function
       Answer: C. Conservation and classification
   Rationale: These logical skills improve during concrete operations.

35. Metamemory refers to:
   A. unconscious memory traces
   B. memory for motor routines
   C. knowledge about one's own memory processes

 D. loss of autobiographical memory
       Answer: C. knowledge about one's own memory processes
   Rationale: Metamemory involves awareness and control of memory strategies.

36. A child remembers the planets by using a rhyme. This is an example of:
   A. habituation
   B. mnemonic strategy
   C. centration

 D. transductive reasoning
       Answer: B. mnemonic strategy
   Rationale: Mnemonics aid memory through structured techniques.

37. Which child is most likely to show industry according to Erikson?
   A. One who avoids all school tasks
   B. One who develops competence through productive work
   C. One who becomes highly dependent on parents

 D. One who rejects rules as meaningless
       Answer: B. One who develops competence through productive work
   Rationale: Industry involves mastering skills and feeling competent.

38. A child who is frequently chosen as a playmate because she is cooperative and helpful is
likely considered:

   A. neglected
   B. rejected-aggressive
   C. popular-prosocial

 D. controversial
       Answer: C. popular-prosocial
   Rationale: Popular-prosocial children are liked due to positive social behavior.

39. Bullying differs from ordinary conflict because bullying involves:
   A. only physical aggression
   B. mutual hostility of equal intensity
   C. repeated aggression with a power imbalance

 D. accidental harm without intent
       Answer: C. repeated aggression with a power imbalance
   Rationale: Bullying includes repetition and imbalance of power.

40. Which factor is most strongly associated with resilience in school-age children?
   A. Complete absence of stress
   B. At least one stable, supportive relationship
   C. High socioeconomic status only

 D. Superior physical strength
       Answer: B. At least one stable, supportive relationship
   Rationale: Supportive relationships are key protective factors for resilience.

41. Puberty is triggered primarily by changes in the:
   A. digestive and respiratory systems
   B. endocrine system
   C. skeletal system alone
 D. immune system
       Answer: B. endocrine system
   Rationale: Hormonal changes regulate the onset of puberty.

42. Early-maturing girls are at elevated risk for which outcome?
   A. Improved emotional adjustment in all cases
   B. Lower peer attention
   C. Internalizing and externalizing problems

 D. Delayed body image concerns
       Answer: C. Internalizing and externalizing problems
   Rationale: Early maturation can increase psychological and behavioral risks.

43. Piaget proposed that adolescents enter formal operational thought, characterized by:
   A. inability to reason beyond direct experience
   B. hypothetical and abstract reasoning
   C. dependence on trial-and-error only

 D. loss of concrete reasoning
       Answer: B. hypothetical and abstract reasoning
   Rationale: Formal operations enable abstract and hypothetical thinking.

44. Adolescent egocentrism includes the personal fable, which refers to:
   A. belief that adults are always wrong
   B. difficulty with conservation tasks
   C. sense of uniqueness and invulnerability

 D. fear of imaginary creatures
       Answer: C. sense of uniqueness and invulnerability
   Rationale: The personal fable involves beliefs of uniqueness and invincibility.

45. Kohlberg's theory of moral development focuses primarily on:
   A. emotional attachment
   B. moral reasoning
   C. unconscious guilt

 D. conditioned compliance
       Answer: B. moral reasoning
   Rationale: Kohlberg emphasized how individuals reason about moral issues.

46. Gilligan criticized Kohlberg for:
   A. ignoring biological maturation
   B. overemphasizing punishment
   C. neglecting a care orientation in moral thought

 D. rejecting all stage theories
       Answer: C. neglecting a care orientation in moral thought
   Rationale: Gilligan argued for inclusion of care-based moral reasoning.
47. Marcia's identity statuses are based on the dimensions of:
   A. attachment and temperament
   B. crisis and commitment
   C. heredity and environment

 D. autonomy and shame
       Answer: B. crisis and commitment
   Rationale: Identity status depends on exploration and commitment.

48. An adolescent who has explored options and made personal choices about beliefs and
vocation is in:

   A. identity diffusion
   B. foreclosure
   C. moratorium

 D. identity achievement
       Answer: D. identity achievement
   Rationale: Identity achievement follows exploration and commitment.

49. Which parental style is generally associated with the most favorable adolescent outcomes?
   A. Harsh authoritarian control
   B. Indifferent noninvolvement
   C. Authoritative monitoring and responsiveness

 D. Inconsistent permissiveness
       Answer: C. Authoritative monitoring and responsiveness
   Rationale: This style promotes competence and well-being.

50. Juvenile delinquency is best understood as the result of:
   A. a single inherited criminal trait
   B. interaction among biological, family, peer, and community influences
   C. normal adolescent experimentation only

 D. poor academic ability alone
       Answer: B. interaction among biological, family, peer, and community influences
   Rationale: Delinquency arises from multiple interacting factors.

51. Emerging adulthood is characterized by:
   A. immediate assumption of stable adult roles for most people
   B. identity exploration and instability for many individuals
   C. universal marriage and parenthood by age 21

 D. absence of self-focus
       Answer: B. identity exploration and instability for many individuals
   Rationale: Emerging adulthood involves exploration in identity, relationships, and career, often
accompanied by instability.

52. Postformal thought is often described as:
   A. rigid and absolutist
   B. exclusively logical and context-free
   C. more flexible, practical, and relativistic

 D. identical to concrete operations
       Answer: C. more flexible, practical, and relativistic
   Rationale: Postformal thought integrates logic with real-world complexity and context.

53. Schaie's life-span model proposes that many adults gradually shift from acquiring
knowledge to:

   A. avoiding all intellectual activity
   B. applying knowledge to practical goals
   C. abandoning problem solving

 D. relying only on intuition
       Answer: B. applying knowledge to practical goals
   Rationale: Adults increasingly use knowledge for real-life responsibilities.

54. Sternberg's triarchic view of intelligence includes:
   A. linguistic, spatial, and bodily intelligence
   B. fluid, crystallized, and implicit memory
   C. analytical, creative, and practical intelligence

 D. symbolic, social, and emotional intelligence
       Answer: C. analytical, creative, and practical intelligence
   Rationale: Sternberg identified three components of intelligence: analytical, creative, and
practical.

55. Which pattern is most typical of health in emerging and young adulthood?
   A. Highest prevalence of chronic disability across the life span
   B. Peak physical functioning with substantial influence of lifestyle choices
   C. Minimal influence of behavior on health outcomes

 D. Uniform mental health across all individuals
       Answer: B. Peak physical functioning with substantial influence of lifestyle choices
   Rationale: Physical health peaks in this stage, but lifestyle choices strongly influence
outcomes.

56. Which issue is a common developmental task in emerging adulthood?
   A. Mastery of sensorimotor coordination
   B. Establishing intimate relationships while consolidating identity
   C. Achieving ego integrity

 D. Resolving separation anxiety from strangers
       Answer: B. Establishing intimate relationships while consolidating identity
   Rationale: This period involves identity formation and building close relationships.

57. In middle adulthood, fluid intelligence generally:
   A. rises steadily without exception
   B. remains unaffected by age
   C. tends to decline more than crystallized intelligence

 D. replaces expertise
       Answer: C. tends to decline more than crystallized intelligence
   Rationale: Fluid intelligence declines with age, while crystallized intelligence is more stable.

58. Crystallized intelligence refers to:
   A. speed of novel problem solving
   B. accumulated knowledge and verbal skill
   C. nonverbal reasoning independent of culture

 D. working memory span only
       Answer: B. accumulated knowledge and verbal skill
   Rationale: Crystallized intelligence reflects learned knowledge and experience.

59. Expertise in middle adulthood often compensates for declines in speed because experts:
   A. stop using memory
   B. rely on richer knowledge structures and efficient strategies
   C. avoid complex tasks

 D. use only rote memorization
       Answer: B. rely on richer knowledge structures and efficient strategies
   Rationale: Experts use experience and efficient strategies to maintain performance.

60. Erikson described the central psychosocial issue of middle adulthood as:
   A. trust versus mistrust
   B. identity versus role confusion
   C. generativity versus stagnation

 D. integrity versus despair
       Answer: C. generativity versus stagnation
   Rationale: Middle adulthood focuses on contributing to society and future generations.

61. Generativity is best defined as:
   A. preoccupation with one's own mortality
   B. concern for guiding the next generation
   C. withdrawal from productive roles

 D. rejection of family obligations
       Answer: B. concern for guiding the next generation
   Rationale: Generativity involves nurturing and guiding others.

62. Which event best reflects the "social clock" concept?
   A. Biologically timed puberty
   B. Social expectations regarding when life events should occur
   C. A personal trauma unrelated to age norms

 D. Genetic programming of menopause
       Answer: B. Social expectations regarding when life events should occur
   Rationale: The social clock refers to culturally expected timing of life events.
63. The "empty nest" is most accurately described as:
   A. uniformly harmful to marital satisfaction
   B. always associated with depression
   C. a transition whose effects vary by context and prior family relationships

 D. evidence of failed parenting
       Answer: C. a transition whose effects vary by context and prior family relationships
   Rationale: Its impact depends on individual and relational factors.

64. Midlife well-being is most likely when adults:
   A. avoid all role obligations
   B. rigidly resist change
   C. balance self-acceptance, purpose, and meaningful relationships

 D. disengage from family and work
       Answer: C. balance self-acceptance, purpose, and meaningful relationships
   Rationale: Well-being is associated with balance and meaningful engagement.

65. The term presbyopia refers to age-related:
   A. hearing loss
   B. difficulty focusing on near objects
   C. loss of smell

 D. memory impairment
       Answer: B. difficulty focusing on near objects
   Rationale: Presbyopia affects near vision due to lens changes.

66. Menopause refers to:
   A. any mood change in midlife
   B. end of fertility marked by permanent cessation of menstruation
   C. all reproductive changes beginning at puberty

 D. male decline in testosterone
       Answer: B. end of fertility marked by permanent cessation of menstruation
   Rationale: Menopause marks the end of reproductive capability.

67. Which statement about the "midlife crisis" is most accurate?
   A. It is a universal developmental event.
   B. It affects only men.
   C. It is better viewed as a possible experience for some, not an inevitable stage for all.

 D. It is synonymous with stagnation.
       Answer: C. It is better viewed as a possible experience for some, not an inevitable stage
for all.
   Rationale: Not all individuals experience a midlife crisis.

68. In late adulthood, the strongest predictors of longevity include:
   A. only inherited traits
   B. lifestyle, health care, and social conditions in addition to genetics
   C. intelligence alone

 D. birth order alone
       Answer: B. lifestyle, health care, and social conditions in addition to genetics
   Rationale: Longevity is influenced by multiple interacting factors.

69. The term young-old generally refers to adults:
   A. 45 to 59
   B. 60 to 64
   C. 65 to 74

 D. 75 to 84
       Answer: C. 65 to 74
   Rationale: Young-old refers to early older adulthood.

70. Which theory proposes that aging results from accumulated random damage to biological
systems?

   A. Psychoanalytic theory
   B. Variable-rate or damage theories
   C. Social clock theory

 D. Activity theory
       Answer: B. Variable-rate or damage theories
   Rationale: These theories explain aging as cumulative biological damage.

71. Which change in memory is most commonly associated with normal aging?
   A. Severe loss of procedural memory in all older adults
   B. Decline in working memory and processing speed
   C. Complete inability to learn new information

 D. Loss of semantic memory before sensory changes
       Answer: B. Decline in working memory and processing speed
   Rationale: Aging commonly affects speed and working memory.

72. Wisdom in late adulthood is best understood as:
   A. perfect recall of facts
   B. high IQ alone
   C. expert knowledge about life and good judgment in human affairs

 D. emotional detachment from others
       Answer: C. expert knowledge about life and good judgment in human affairs
   Rationale: Wisdom involves practical judgment and life understanding.

73. Erikson's final psychosocial crisis centers on:
   A. initiative versus guilt
   B. identity versus role confusion
   C. generativity versus stagnation
   D. ego integrity versus despair
  Answer: D. ego integrity versus despair

   Rationale: This stage involves reflecting on life with acceptance or regret.

74. Selective optimization with compensation refers to:
   A. avoiding all difficult tasks in old age
   B. maximizing youth-oriented goals only
   C. focusing on priorities, strengthening abilities, and offsetting losses

 D. depending entirely on others for functioning
       Answer: C. focusing on priorities, strengthening abilities, and offsetting losses
   Rationale: It is a strategy for adapting to aging-related changes.

75. Which statement about retirement is most accurate?
   A. Retirement has identical effects on everyone.
   B. Retirement adjustment depends on health, finances, voluntariness, and social roles.
   C. Retirement inevitably causes depression.

 D. Retirement eliminates developmental challenges.
       Answer: B. Retirement adjustment depends on health, finances, voluntariness, and social
roles.
   Rationale: Adjustment varies depending on multiple personal and contextual factors.

76. Widowhood in late adulthood is often:
   A. insignificant after long marriages
   B. a major transition influenced by gender, support, and prior relationship quality
   C. always more difficult for women than men in every context

 D. unrelated to health
       Answer: B. a major transition influenced by gender, support, and prior relationship quality
   Rationale: Widowhood effects vary based on individual and relational factors.

77. Disengagement theory proposes that healthy aging involves:
   A. increasing social participation at all costs
   B. mutual withdrawal between older adults and society
   C. greater attachment in all roles

 D. stronger adolescent identity exploration
       Answer: B. mutual withdrawal between older adults and society
   Rationale: The theory suggests reduced interaction between individuals and society in aging.

78. Activity theory would predict higher well-being in old age when people:
   A. maintain meaningful engagement
   B. avoid social roles
   C. reject adaptation

 D. minimize contact with others
       Answer: A. maintain meaningful engagement
   Rationale: Continued activity supports satisfaction in aging.
79. Which statement about grief is most accurate?
   A. All bereaved persons pass through identical stages in fixed order.
   B. Grief reactions vary widely across persons and cultures.
   C. Absence of crying means absence of grief.

 D. Grief is pathological unless it resolves within one month.
       Answer: B. Grief reactions vary widely across persons and cultures.
   Rationale: Grief is highly individualized and culturally influenced.

80. Life review in late adulthood can be developmentally useful because it:
   A. prevents all regret
   B. supports meaning-making and integration of one's life story
   C. replaces current relationships

 D. eliminates fear of death automatically
       Answer: B. supports meaning-making and integration of one's life story
   Rationale: Life review helps integrate experiences and find meaning.

81. Which situation best illustrates ambiguous loss?
   A. Death of an elderly parent after prolonged illness
   B. Loss of a spouse through divorce with clear legal closure
   C. A family member missing for years with unknown status

 D. Planned retirement from work
       Answer: C. A family member missing for years with unknown status
   Rationale: Ambiguous loss lacks closure and certainty.

82. Which statement best reflects current developmental understanding of death concepts?
   A. Children understand death fully from infancy.
   B. Understanding of death changes with cognitive development and experience.
   C. Adolescents rarely think about death.

 D. Older adults fear death in exactly the same way as children.
       Answer: B. Understanding of death changes with cognitive development and experience.
   Rationale: Death concepts evolve across development.

83. Under RA 10029, which statement is most accurate?
   A. Anyone with a psychology degree may independently practice as a psychologist.
   B. Only licensed and registered psychologists and psychometricians may legally practice

within the scope allowed by law.
   C. Psychometricians may independently provide all forms of psychotherapy.

 D. Registration is optional if supervision is available.
       Answer: B. Only licensed and registered psychologists and psychometricians may legally
practice within the scope allowed by law.
   Rationale: RA 10029 regulates the legal practice of psychology professions.

84. A registered psychometrician is asked to conduct psychotherapy for a client with major
depressive symptoms in a private clinic. The most ethical response is to:
   A. accept because any psychology professional may provide therapy
   B. accept if the client signs informed consent
   C. decline and refer to a qualified licensed psychologist or other authorized mental health
professional

 D. proceed only if sessions are brief
       Answer: C. decline and refer to a qualified licensed psychologist or other authorized
mental health professional
   Rationale: Practitioners must work within their legal scope and competence.

85. A psychometrician is instructed by a school principal to interpret a complex
neuropsychological battery beyond his training. Based on ethical standards on competence, he
should:

   A. interpret it anyway to satisfy the school
   B. guess cautiously and omit uncertain findings
   C. refuse or seek proper supervision/referral because the task is beyond his competence

 D. allow a teacher to interpret the profile
       Answer: C. refuse or seek proper supervision/referral because the task is beyond his
competence
   Rationale: Ethical practice requires working only within one's competence.

86. Which practice best protects confidentiality in telepsychology?
   A. Conducting sessions on any available public platform
   B. Storing records on an unsecured shared device
   C. Informing clients of privacy risks and using reasonable safeguards such as passwords and

secure transmission

 D. Sending raw test results through social media chat without warning
       Answer: C. Informing clients of privacy risks and using reasonable safeguards such as
passwords and secure transmission
   Rationale: Ethical practice requires safeguarding confidentiality, especially in digital contexts.

87. A client discloses imminent intent to seriously harm another person. Ethical handling of
confidentiality requires the practitioner to:

   A. keep the disclosure secret under all circumstances
   B. release all records publicly
   C. take protective action and disclose only information necessary to appropriate persons or
authorities

 D. ignore the threat because prediction is uncertain
       Answer: C. take protective action and disclose only information necessary to appropriate
persons or authorities
   Rationale: Confidentiality may be breached to prevent serious harm.

88. A practitioner is asked by a company to assess employees. Before beginning, the most
important clarification is:

   A. what snacks will be provided during testing
   B. who the client is, the purpose of the service, probable uses of information, and limits of
confidentiality

   C. whether all employees like psychological tests

 D. whether the company will permit retesting for everyone regardless of need
       Answer: B. who the client is, the purpose of the service, probable uses of information, and
limits of confidentiality
   Rationale: Clarifying roles and limits is essential in third-party services.

89. Which is the clearest example of a harmful multiple relationship?
   A. Teaching a large lecture class at a university
   B. Conducting therapy for one's close romantic partner
   C. Referring a client to a physician

 D. Consulting with another psychologist about a difficult case while protecting identity
       Answer: B. Conducting therapy for one's close romantic partner
   Rationale: Dual relationships that impair objectivity and risk harm are unethical.

90. A practitioner experiences serious personal distress that is impairing judgment and
concentration at work. The ethical standard most directly requires the practitioner to:

   A. continue working without change
   B. conceal the problem to protect reputation
   C. seek consultation or assistance and consider limiting, suspending, or terminating duties if
needed

 D. transfer all clients to unqualified staff immediately
       Answer: C. seek consultation or assistance and consider limiting, suspending, or
terminating duties if needed
   Rationale: Practitioners must address personal issues that impair competence.

91. In emergencies, a psychology practitioner who lacks full specialty competence may provide
temporary assistance only if the practitioner:

   A. continues indefinitely without referral
   B. gives services recklessly because need exists
   C. proceeds cautiously, provides needed support, and discontinues once competent ongoing
care becomes available

 D. ignores informed consent
       Answer: C. proceeds cautiously, provides needed support, and discontinues once
competent ongoing care becomes available
   Rationale: Emergency services must be temporary and responsible.

92. A psychometrician allows an untrained office assistant to administer and score psychological
tests alone. This is unethical primarily because it violates standards on:

   A. informed consent only
   B. delegation of work and assessment by unqualified persons
   C. public statements only
   D. continuing professional development only
  Answer: B. delegation of work and assessment by unqualified persons

   Rationale: Tasks must only be delegated to qualified individuals.

93. Which public statement is ethically acceptable?
   A. "Guaranteed cure for trauma in one session."
   B. "Top psychologist in the country--100% success rate."
   C. "Services include psychological assessment and consultation; fees and credentials are

available upon request."

 D. "Our methods work better than all other clinics."
       Answer: C. "Services include psychological assessment and consultation; fees and
credentials are available upon request."
   Rationale: Ethical statements must be accurate and non-deceptive.

94. A practitioner wants to use a client's case in a lecture. Ethical practice requires:
   A. use of the material freely because teaching is beneficial
   B. disclosure of personally identifiable details if the audience is professional
   C. written consent, legal authorization, or adequate disguise of identity

 D. verbal mention without consent as long as no recording exists
       Answer: C. written consent, legal authorization, or adequate disguise of identity
   Rationale: Confidentiality must be protected when using case material.

95. Which action is most consistent with ethical reporting of another practitioner's violation?
   A. Filing a complaint based on rumor alone
   B. Ignoring substantial harm to avoid conflict
   C. Attempting informal resolution when appropriate and reporting to proper authorities when

substantial harm is likely

 D. Posting allegations on social media first
       Answer: C. Attempting informal resolution when appropriate and reporting to proper
authorities when substantial harm is likely
   Rationale: Ethical response involves appropriate action based on severity.

96. A court orders a psychological evaluation. Before proceeding, the evaluator should inform
the examinee about:

   A. only the date of the appointment
   B. the evaluator's personal beliefs
   C. the nature of services, that the evaluation is court-ordered, and the limits of confidentiality

 D. the likely court decision
       Answer: C. the nature of services, that the evaluation is court-ordered, and the limits of
confidentiality
   Rationale: Clients must be informed about service conditions and confidentiality.

97. Which action best reflects the duty to minimize invasion of privacy?
   A. Sharing full client history in staff lounges
   B. Revealing only information relevant to the professional purpose
   C. Discussing all details with family members for support

 D. Keeping no records at all
       Answer: B. Revealing only information relevant to the professional purpose
   Rationale: Only necessary information should be disclosed.

98. A psychometrician receives raw test data from a hospital and wants to send it to a friend for
practice interpretation. The most ethical response is to:

   A. send it if names are removed incompletely
   B. send it because colleagues may always access test data
   C. refrain unless proper authorization exists and disclosure is limited to qualified persons for
legitimate purposes

 D. post selected protocols in a closed online study group
       Answer: C. refrain unless proper authorization exists and disclosure is limited to qualified
persons for legitimate purposes
   Rationale: Confidential data must only be shared with proper authorization.

99. Which statement best reflects ethical obligations regarding competence maintenance?
   A. Once licensed, further professional development is optional
   B. Competence is maintained through ongoing education, training, and other CPD activities
   C. Experience automatically replaces the need for updated learning

 D. CPD applies only to psychologists, not psychometricians
       Answer: B. Competence is maintained through ongoing education, training, and other
CPD activities
   Rationale: Continuous professional development ensures competence.

100. A psychometrician is supervised in a clinic and asked to explain assessment results to a
client. Which response is most appropriate?

    A. Provide interpretations only within competence and role, with proper supervision when
needed

    B. Improvise diagnostic conclusions to sound confident
    C. Withhold all feedback permanently

 D. Give the raw manual and ask the client to interpret the profile alone
        Answer: A. Provide interpretations only within competence and role, with proper
supervision when needed
    Rationale: Ethical practice requires staying within competence and supervision boundaries.
DEVELOPMENTAL PSYCHOLOGY
EXAM 6
DEVELOPMENTAL PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 6

1. Which statement best reflects the life-span perspective in developmental psychology?
  A. Development ends when biological maturity is reached.
  B. Development consists only of age-related gains.
  C. Development is lifelong, multidimensional, and influenced by context.

 D. Development is determined mainly by heredity.
       Answer: C. Development is lifelong, multidimensional, and influenced by context.
  Rationale: The life-span perspective views development as a lifelong process involving gains
and losses across multiple domains and shaped by biological, psychological, social, historical,
and cultural contexts.

2. A developmental psychologist studies how poverty, family structure, school setting, and
culture jointly affect a child's adjustment. Which feature of development is most clearly
emphasized?

  A. Single-cause explanation
  B. Contextual influence
  C. Biological determinism

 D. Fixed maturation
       Answer: B. Contextual influence
  Rationale: The question emphasizes interacting environmental systems such as poverty,
family, school, and culture, which reflects contextual influences on development.

3. Which situation is the best example of a normative history-graded influence?
  A. A child's severe hearing loss at birth
  B. A family's move to another city
  C. A generation experiencing a global pandemic during adolescence

 D. A teenager's first romantic breakup
       Answer: C. A generation experiencing a global pandemic during adolescence
  Rationale: A normative history-graded influence is a large-scale event affecting many people
of a generation at a particular historical time.

4. A researcher wants to examine age-related differences in memory by comparing 8-year-olds,
16-year-olds, and 24-year-olds at one point in time. Which design is being used?

  A. Longitudinal
  B. Cross-sectional
  C. Sequential

 D. Experimental
       Answer: B. Cross-sectional
  Rationale: Cross-sectional research compares people of different ages at the same time.

5. Which statement best distinguishes a theory from a hypothesis?
  A. A theory is narrower and less evidence-based than a hypothesis.
  B. A hypothesis organizes a broad body of findings into a framework.
  C. A theory provides an overarching explanation; a hypothesis is a testable prediction.

 D. A theory is descriptive only, whereas a hypothesis is explanatory only.
       Answer: C. A theory provides an overarching explanation; a hypothesis is a testable
prediction.
  Rationale: A theory organizes findings into a broad explanatory framework, while a hypothesis
is a specific proposition that can be tested empirically.

6. Which theorist is most closely associated with the psychosocial stages of development across
the life span?

  A. Jean Piaget
  B. Erik Erikson
  C. B. F. Skinner

 D. Lev Vygotsky
       Answer: B. Erik Erikson
  Rationale: Erikson proposed psychosocial stages extending across the whole life span.

7. A child first calls every four-legged animal "dog," then gradually learns to distinguish dogs
from cats and goats. This illustrates:

  A. object permanence
  B. overextension
  C. conservation

 D. centration
       Answer: B. overextension
  Rationale: Overextension occurs when a child applies one word too broadly, such as calling all
four-legged animals "dog."

8. Which research method is most appropriate for obtaining rich, in-depth information about one
rare developmental condition?

  A. Survey
  B. Case study
  C. Cross-sectional design

 D. Correlational meta-analysis
       Answer: B. Case study
  Rationale: Case studies provide detailed information about a rare condition or unusual
developmental pattern.

9. Which statement best captures the developmental issue of nature and nurture?
  A. Only genetic factors matter in development.
  B. Only environmental factors matter in development.
  C. Development results from the interaction of heredity and environment.

 D. Nature matters only before birth, nurture only after birth.
       Answer: C. Development results from the interaction of heredity and environment.
  Rationale: Modern developmental psychology rejects an either-or view and emphasizes
interaction between genes and experience.
10. Which is the strongest example of a sensitive period?
   A. A period after which learning is biologically impossible
   B. A time when a person is especially responsive to certain experiences
   C. A time when maturation stops temporarily

 D. A stage in which all children behave identically
       Answer: B. A time when a person is especially responsive to certain experiences
   Rationale: A sensitive period is a time of heightened receptivity to environmental influences,
though learning may still occur later.

11. Which event occurs first in prenatal development?
   A. Implantation
   B. Formation of the zygote
   C. Fetal movement

 D. Differentiation of body systems
       Answer: B. Formation of the zygote
   Rationale: Prenatal development begins at fertilization, when sperm and ovum unite to form a
zygote.

12. A pregnant woman consumes alcohol heavily throughout pregnancy. Which outcome is most
strongly associated with this exposure?

   A. Superior motor development
   B. Increased attachment security
   C. Fetal alcohol-related developmental impairment

 D. Advanced language development
       Answer: C. Fetal alcohol-related developmental impairment
   Rationale: Heavy prenatal alcohol exposure is strongly linked to fetal alcohol spectrum
disorders and multiple developmental impairments.

13. Genetic counseling is most directly useful for:
   A. increasing intelligence through training
   B. determining parenting style
   C. estimating the probability of inherited disorders

 D. eliminating all environmental risks
       Answer: C. estimating the probability of inherited disorders
   Rationale: Genetic counseling helps prospective parents understand inherited risk and make
informed decisions.

14. Which statement about heredity is most accurate?
   A. Heritability refers to the extent to which a trait is caused only by genes in one person.
   B. Heritability estimates describe variation within a population, not destiny for an individual.
   C. Highly heritable traits cannot be modified by experience.
   D. Polygenic traits are controlled by a single dominant gene.
  Answer: B. Heritability estimates describe variation within a population, not destiny for an

individual.
   Rationale: Heritability is a population statistic and does not determine an individual's

outcome.

15. Which condition results from an extra chromosome 21?
   A. Turner syndrome
   B. Klinefelter syndrome
   C. Down syndrome

 D. Tay-Sachs disease
       Answer: C. Down syndrome
   Rationale: Down syndrome typically results from trisomy 21.

16. Which maternal factor is most likely to threaten prenatal development?
   A. Moderate exercise approved by a physician
   B. Adequate folic acid intake
   C. Chronic malnutrition

 D. Regular prenatal checkups
       Answer: C. Chronic malnutrition
   Rationale: Maternal malnutrition is a major prenatal risk affecting fetal growth and
development.

17. A father's heavy exposure to toxins before conception is important because:
   A. paternal factors never affect prenatal outcomes
   B. sperm quality may be altered
   C. fathers determine only social development

 D. paternal age affects only language
       Answer: B. sperm quality may be altered
   Rationale: Paternal toxic exposure can affect sperm and contribute to reproductive and
developmental risk.

18. The period from conception to about 2 weeks is called the:
   A. fetal period
   B. embryonic period
   C. germinal period

 D. neonatal period
       Answer: C. germinal period
   Rationale: The germinal period covers conception to implantation, approximately the first two
weeks.

19. During childbirth, the longest stage for most first-time mothers is typically:
   A. delivery of the placenta
   B. transition
   C. dilation and effacement of the cervix
 D. crowning
       Answer: C. dilation and effacement of the cervix
   Rationale: The first stage of labor, involving dilation and effacement, is usually the longest in
first births.

20. Low birth weight is a major concern because it is associated with:
   A. guaranteed intellectual disability
   B. increased risk for developmental and health problems
   C. inevitable emotional disturbance

 D. advanced sensory maturity
       Answer: B. increased risk for developmental and health problems
   Rationale: Low birth weight is associated with elevated risk for survival, neurological, and
developmental difficulties.

21. Which newborn assessment most directly evaluates behavioral responses and neurological
functioning?

   A. Stanford-Binet
   B. Apgar scale only
   C. Neonatal behavioral assessment

 D. Wechsler scale
       Answer: C. Neonatal behavioral assessment
   Rationale: Behavioral neonatal assessments examine reflexes, responsiveness, state
regulation, and neurological functioning.

22. The cephalocaudal principle means development proceeds:
   A. from the center of the body outward
   B. from lower body parts to upper body parts
   C. from head to tail

 D. from large muscles to small muscles only
       Answer: C. from head to tail
   Rationale: The cephalocaudal principle means development proceeds from the head
downward.

23. Which brain process is especially important for increasing efficiency in early development?
   A. Neural pruning
   B. Menopause
   C. Pubertal surge

 D. Crystallization
       Answer: A. Neural pruning
   Rationale: Neural pruning removes unused connections, making brain functioning more
efficient.

24. Object permanence refers to understanding that:
   A. objects are always pleasant
   B. hidden objects continue to exist
   C. objects can be classified by color

 D. symbols and objects are identical
       Answer: B. hidden objects continue to exist
   Rationale: Object permanence is the understanding that objects exist even when out of sight.

25. Which Piagetian stage characterizes the first two years of life?
   A. Preoperational
   B. Sensorimotor
   C. Concrete operational

 D. Formal operational
       Answer: B. Sensorimotor
   Rationale: Piaget described birth to about age 2 as the sensorimotor stage.

26. A baby repeatedly shakes a rattle for the sound it makes. In Piaget's view, this is best
described as:

   A. symbolic reasoning
   B. deferred imitation
   C. circular reaction

 D. conservation
       Answer: C. circular reaction
   Rationale: Repeatedly reproducing an interesting event discovered by chance is a circular
reaction.

27. Habituation in infancy is useful to researchers because it indicates:
   A. refusal to learn
   B. decreased response after repeated stimulation
   C. mastery of language

 D. onset of attachment
       Answer: B. decreased response after repeated stimulation
   Rationale: Habituation is reduced attention or response after repeated exposure to the same
stimulus.

28. Which best reflects the information-processing approach to infant cognition?
   A. Infants cannot remember until language develops.
   B. Cognitive growth involves changes in attention, memory, and processing speed.
   C. Infants develop entirely through unconscious conflicts.

 D. Thinking develops in fixed moral stages.
       Answer: B. Cognitive growth involves changes in attention, memory, and processing
speed.
   Rationale: Information-processing theories explain development through changes in mental
processes such as attention and memory.
29. Which theorist argued that language acquisition depends on an inborn mechanism for
learning language?

   A. Skinner
   B. Bandura
   C. Chomsky

 D. Watson
       Answer: C. Chomsky
   Rationale: Chomsky proposed an inborn basis for language acquisition.

30. A toddler says "goed" instead of "went." This is an example of:
   A. underextension
   B. overregularization
   C. echolalia

 D. telegraphic speech
       Answer: B. overregularization
   Rationale: Applying regular grammatical rules to irregular verbs, such as "goed," is
overregularization.

31. In Erikson's theory, the major psychosocial task of infancy is:
   A. autonomy versus shame and doubt
   B. trust versus mistrust
   C. initiative versus guilt

 D. identity versus role confusion
       Answer: B. trust versus mistrust
   Rationale: Erikson identified trust versus mistrust as the core psychosocial conflict of infancy.

32. Ainsworth's strange situation was designed primarily to assess:
   A. temperament
   B. attachment security
   C. language delay

 D. executive function
       Answer: B. attachment security
   Rationale: Ainsworth's strange situation assesses patterns of infant-caregiver attachment.

33. Which infant is most likely to be classified as securely attached?
   A. One who ignores the caregiver at reunion
   B. One who is disorganized and fearful without pattern
   C. One who seeks comfort and is soothed upon reunion

 D. One who clings and resists contact simultaneously
       Answer: C. One who seeks comfort and is soothed upon reunion
   Rationale: Securely attached infants use the caregiver as a secure base and are comforted
upon reunion.

34. Social referencing refers to:
   A. using adults' emotional cues to guide behavior
   B. referencing one's grades for self-esteem
   C. naming emotions correctly

 D. comparing IQ scores with peers
       Answer: A. using adults' emotional cues to guide behavior
   Rationale: Social referencing occurs when infants consult caregivers' emotional reactions to
interpret unfamiliar situations.

35. Temperament refers to:
   A. learned moral values
   B. biologically based individual differences in emotional style and self-regulation
   C. a child's IQ ranking

 D. the quality of attachment alone
       Answer: B. biologically based individual differences in emotional style and self-regulation
   Rationale: Temperament refers to early emerging, partly biological differences in emotional
reactivity and regulation.

36. Which is the best example of autonomy in toddlerhood?
   A. Solving algebra independently
   B. Insisting on feeding oneself
   C. Understanding formal logic

 D. Achieving identity commitment
       Answer: B. Insisting on feeding oneself
   Rationale: Self-directed acts such as feeding oneself reflect growing autonomy in
toddlerhood.

37. Which parenting outcome is most likely when caregivers are warm, responsive, and
consistent?

   A. Insecure attachment becomes inevitable
   B. Trust and early self-regulation are facilitated
   C. Language is delayed

 D. Moral development stops
       Answer: B. Trust and early self-regulation are facilitated
   Rationale: Warm, responsive, and consistent caregiving supports trust, secure attachment,
and regulation.

38. Which is a core developmental risk of severe neglect in infancy?
   A. Immediate formal operational thought
   B. Nonorganic failure to thrive
   C. Accelerated puberty

 D. Excessive conservation ability
       Answer: B. Nonorganic failure to thrive
   Rationale: Severe neglect can result in slowed growth and impaired development without a
medical cause.
39. In Piaget's preoperational stage, a child focuses on one aspect of a situation and neglects
others. This is called:

   A. reversibility
   B. centration
   C. decentration

 D. seriation
       Answer: B. centration
   Rationale: Centration is focusing on one dimension while ignoring others, a hallmark of
preoperational thought.

40. A preschooler believes that a taller glass always has more liquid than a shorter glass,
despite equal amounts. This error shows lack of:

   A. object permanence
   B. class inclusion
   C. conservation

 D. hypothetical reasoning
       Answer: C. conservation
   Rationale: The child fails to understand that quantity remains the same despite changes in
appearance.

41. Which development is most characteristic of early childhood language growth?
   A. Loss of grammar
   B. Rapid vocabulary expansion
   C. Decline in symbolic thought

 D. Elimination of private speech
       Answer: B. Rapid vocabulary expansion
   Rationale: Early childhood is marked by strong vocabulary growth and increasingly complex
grammar.

42. According to Vygotsky, tasks a child cannot yet do alone but can do with guidance fall within
the:

   A. latent learning range
   B. zone of proximal development
   C. sensorimotor sequence

 D. conservation range
       Answer: B. zone of proximal development
   Rationale: Vygotsky's zone of proximal development includes tasks achievable with guidance
but not yet independently.

43. Which best describes private speech in early childhood?
   A. A sign of social incompetence
   B. Externalized self-guidance that aids problem solving
   C. Evidence of insecure attachment
 D. A symptom of language disorder
       Answer: B. Externalized self-guidance that aids problem solving
   Rationale: Private speech helps children guide their own behavior and thinking.

44. In Erikson's theory, the central psychosocial conflict of early childhood is:
   A. trust versus mistrust
   B. autonomy versus shame and doubt
   C. initiative versus guilt

 D. industry versus inferiority
       Answer: C. initiative versus guilt
   Rationale: Erikson viewed early childhood as the stage when children take initiative and
develop purpose.

45. Which parenting style is generally associated with the most favorable child outcomes?
   A. Authoritarian
   B. Permissive
   C. Neglectful

 D. Authoritative
       Answer: D. Authoritative
   Rationale: Authoritative parenting combines warmth with firm, rational control and is linked to
positive outcomes.

46. Which statement about play in early childhood is most accurate?
   A. Play is developmentally unimportant.
   B. Play supports cognitive, social, and emotional development.
   C. Play matters only for motor development.

 D. Play is purely recreational and not symbolic.
       Answer: B. Play supports cognitive, social, and emotional development.
   Rationale: Play contributes to imagination, self-regulation, perspective-taking, and peer
interaction.

47. A child who can understand that another person may hold a false belief is demonstrating:
   A. theory of mind
   B. overimitation
   C. stranger anxiety

 D. conservation
       Answer: A. theory of mind
   Rationale: Understanding that others can hold beliefs different from reality reflects theory of
mind.

48. Which type of aggression is especially common in early childhood?
   A. Institutional aggression
   B. Instrumental aggression
   C. Ideological aggression
 D. Geriatric aggression
       Answer: B. Instrumental aggression
   Rationale: Young children often use aggression instrumentally to obtain an object, space, or
goal.

49. In middle childhood, Piaget's major cognitive stage is:
   A. sensorimotor
   B. preoperational
   C. concrete operational

 D. formal operational
       Answer: C. concrete operational
   Rationale: Middle childhood is the period of concrete operations in Piaget's theory.

50. A school-age child can arrange sticks from shortest to longest. This skill is called:
   A. transduction
   B. seriation
   C. animism

 D. scaffolding
       Answer: B. seriation
   Rationale: Seriation is the ability to arrange objects in order along a dimension such as
length.

51. Metamemory refers to:
   A. loss of childhood memories
   B. understanding how memory works
   C. traumatic memory repression

 D. photographic recall
       Answer: B. understanding how memory works
   Rationale: Metamemory is knowledge about memory processes and strategies.

52. Which child is showing improved executive functioning?
   A. One who cannot inhibit impulsive responses
   B. One who plans a multistep homework routine
   C. One who loses all perspective-taking

 D. One who can only think intuitively
       Answer: B. One who plans a multistep homework routine
   Rationale: Planning, monitoring, and inhibiting impulses are core parts of executive
functioning.

53. In Erikson's theory, successful middle childhood development is marked by:
   A. identity achievement
   B. industry
   C. intimacy
   D. ego integrity
  Answer: B. industry

   Rationale: Industry reflects competence and productivity in school and work-like tasks during
middle childhood.

54. Which factor most strongly supports resilience in children facing adversity?
   A. Persistent peer rejection
   B. At least one stable, supportive relationship
   C. Severe chronic bullying

 D. Total academic failure
       Answer: B. At least one stable, supportive relationship
   Rationale: Protective relationships are among the strongest predictors of resilience under
adversity.

55. A child who is widely liked because of cooperative and prosocial behavior is likely
considered:

   A. neglected
   B. controversial
   C. popular

 D. rejected-aggressive
       Answer: C. popular
   Rationale: Popular children are generally well-liked and often socially skilled and prosocial.

56. Bullying differs from ordinary conflict because bullying involves:
   A. equal power between children
   B. accidental harm only
   C. repeated aggression and power imbalance

 D. only physical violence
       Answer: C. repeated aggression and power imbalance
   Rationale: Bullying involves repeated harmful behavior and unequal power between
perpetrator and target.

57. Puberty is best defined as:
   A. the legal beginning of adulthood
   B. the psychosocial search for identity
   C. the process leading to sexual maturity

 D. the mastery of abstract thought
       Answer: C. the process leading to sexual maturity
   Rationale: Puberty is the biological transition culminating in reproductive maturity.

58. Which structure is especially notable for continued development during adolescence and is
linked to planning and impulse control?

   A. Medulla
   B. Prefrontal cortex
   C. Cerebellum only
 D. Pituitary gland only
       Answer: B. Prefrontal cortex
   Rationale: The prefrontal cortex continues maturing in adolescence and supports planning,
inhibition, and judgment.

59. Adolescent egocentrism is most closely associated with:
   A. object permanence and habituation
   B. imaginary audience and personal fable
   C. conservation and reversibility

 D. initiative and guilt
       Answer: B. imaginary audience and personal fable
   Rationale: Adolescent egocentrism involves believing others are constantly watching and that
one's experiences are unique.

60. In Piaget's theory, formal operational thought allows adolescents to:
   A. rely only on trial-and-error behavior
   B. think abstractly and hypothetically
   C. lose capacity for deductive reasoning

 D. understand only concrete objects
       Answer: B. think abstractly and hypothetically
   Rationale: Formal operations enable hypothetical-deductive reasoning and abstract thought.

61. Kohlberg's theory primarily concerns development in:
   A. attachment
   B. language
   C. moral reasoning

 D. temperament
       Answer: C. moral reasoning
   Rationale: Kohlberg proposed stages of moral reasoning.

62. A teenager says, "A rule is wrong if it violates human dignity, even if it is legal." This reflects:
   A. preconventional morality
   B. conventional morality only
   C. postconventional reasoning

 D. no moral development
       Answer: C. postconventional reasoning
   Rationale: Judging rules by universal ethical principles rather than mere legality reflects
postconventional reasoning.

63. Marcia's identity status model is based on the dimensions of:
   A. punishment and reward
   B. crisis and commitment
   C. heredity and environment
   D. trust and attachment
  Answer: B. crisis and commitment

   Rationale: Marcia described identity status in terms of exploration and commitment, often
summarized as crisis and commitment.

64. Which adolescent is in identity moratorium?
   A. One with firm commitments never questioned
   B. One exploring options without final commitment
   C. One with neither exploration nor commitment

 D. One forced into achievement by peers
       Answer: B. One exploring options without final commitment
   Rationale: Moratorium involves active exploration without having made a firm commitment.

65. Which parenting pattern is generally associated with better adolescent adjustment?
   A. Extremely lax monitoring and detachment
   B. Warmth combined with appropriate monitoring
   C. Harsh punishment without communication

 D. Complete peer control
       Answer: B. Warmth combined with appropriate monitoring
   Rationale: Adolescents generally fare better when parents combine support with reasonable
supervision.

66. Which factor is most strongly associated with increased risk for delinquency?
   A. Strong school bonding
   B. Deviant peer affiliation
   C. Secure parental attachment

 D. Consistent supervision
       Answer: B. Deviant peer affiliation
   Rationale: Association with deviant peers is a strong predictor of delinquent behavior.

67. Emerging adulthood is best described as a period:
   A. from birth to age 2
   B. of absolute role stability
   C. of exploration in love, work, and identity

 D. in which identity development ends
       Answer: C. of exploration in love, work, and identity
   Rationale: Emerging adulthood is characterized by instability and exploration in major life
domains.

68. Postformal thought in adulthood is often characterized by:
   A. rigid either-or logic only
   B. immature egocentrism
   C. pragmatic and relativistic thinking

 D. inability to handle contradiction
       Answer: C. pragmatic and relativistic thinking
   Rationale: Postformal thought emphasizes practical, flexible, and context-sensitive reasoning.

69. Sternberg's triarchic theory includes analytical, creative, and:
   A. procedural intelligence
   B. practical intelligence
   C. sensory intelligence

 D. moral intelligence
       Answer: B. practical intelligence
   Rationale: Sternberg's triarchic theory includes analytical, creative, and practical intelligence.

70. Which issue is especially salient in emerging and young adulthood?
   A. Trust versus mistrust
   B. Intimacy versus isolation
   C. Industry versus inferiority

 D. Ego integrity versus despair
       Answer: B. Intimacy versus isolation
   Rationale: Young adulthood centers on forming close, committed relationships without losing
selfhood.

71. According to Erikson, failure to resolve the central psychosocial task of young adulthood
most likely results in:

   A. identity diffusion only
   B. shame and doubt
   C. isolation

 D. stagnation
       Answer: C. isolation
   Rationale: Erikson proposed that failure to establish intimacy can result in isolation.

72. Which statement about cohabitation and marriage is most accurate from a developmental
perspective?

   A. Relationship outcomes depend only on age.
   B. Relationship quality is influenced by personal, cultural, and contextual factors.
   C. Marriage always decreases stress for all adults.

 D. Cohabitation never leads to long-term commitment.
       Answer: B. Relationship quality is influenced by personal, cultural, and contextual factors.
   Rationale: Developmental perspectives emphasize that relationship outcomes depend on
multiple interacting factors.

73. Which is the best example of generativity in middle adulthood?
   A. Withdrawal from all social roles
   B. Concern for guiding the next generation
   C. Exclusive focus on adolescent peer approval

 D. Persistent identity foreclosure
       Answer: B. Concern for guiding the next generation
   Rationale: Generativity involves investing in and contributing to younger generations and
society.

74. The idea of a social clock refers to:
   A. biological aging of neurons
   B. culturally influenced expectations about timing of life events
   C. a fixed genetic schedule that is identical for all people

 D. time perception in late adulthood
       Answer: B. culturally influenced expectations about timing of life events
   Rationale: The social clock refers to socially shared beliefs about when major life events
should occur.

75. Which cognitive pattern is most typical in middle adulthood?
   A. Both fluid and crystallized intelligence decline equally early
   B. Crystallized intelligence is often maintained or improved, while some fluid abilities decline
   C. All intellectual abilities increase uniformly

 D. Expertise becomes irrelevant
       Answer: B. Crystallized intelligence is often maintained or improved, while some fluid
abilities decline
   Rationale: Knowledge-based abilities often remain strong in midlife, while processing speed
and novel reasoning may decline somewhat.

76. Which best explains why expertise can offset some age-related cognitive slowing in
adulthood?

   A. Experts ignore prior knowledge
   B. Practice and domain-specific knowledge support efficient performance
   C. Experts rely only on working memory capacity

 D. Expertise prevents all biological aging
       Answer: B. Practice and domain-specific knowledge support efficient performance
   Rationale: Expertise compensates through efficient strategies and accumulated knowledge.

77. Which physical change is common in middle adulthood?
   A. Full reversal of sensory decline
   B. Gradual changes in vision, hearing, and reproductive functioning
   C. Universal severe dementia

 D. End of all creativity
       Answer: B. Gradual changes in vision, hearing, and reproductive functioning
   Rationale: These are common midlife physical changes.

78. A middle-aged adult reevaluates priorities after noticing that life is finite, yet remains
productive and invested in family and work. This is best interpreted as:

   A. inevitable midlife crisis
   B. adaptive midlife reflection
   C. pathological regression
 D. identity confusion typical of infancy
       Answer: B. adaptive midlife reflection
   Rationale: Reevaluating life priorities without dysfunction is a normal and often adaptive
developmental process.

79. Which statement about aging is most accurate?
   A. Aging affects all body systems in exactly the same way and rate.
   B. Aging is highly variable and influenced by lifestyle, health, and context.
   C. Cognitive decline in old age is always pathological.

 D. Personality becomes completely unstable in late adulthood.
       Answer: B. Aging is highly variable and influenced by lifestyle, health, and context.
   Rationale: Late adulthood shows substantial individual variability shaped by behavior, health
care, and environment.

80. Fluid intelligence refers mainly to:
   A. accumulated knowledge and vocabulary
   B. speed of processing and novel problem solving
   C. moral identity and wisdom

 D. autobiographical memory only
       Answer: B. speed of processing and novel problem solving
   Rationale: Fluid intelligence concerns solving new problems and thinking quickly and flexibly.

81. Which memory system is most likely to show age-related decline in late adulthood?
   A. Procedural memory only
