   B. Working memory and episodic recall
   C. Memory for overlearned skills only

 D. All memory systems decline equally
       Answer: B. Working memory and episodic recall
   Rationale: These systems commonly show age-related changes, especially under high
processing demands.

82. Wisdom in late adulthood is best understood as:
   A. perfect memory recall
   B. absence of emotional conflict
   C. expert knowledge about life and good judgment

 D. total disengagement from society
       Answer: C. expert knowledge about life and good judgment
   Rationale: Wisdom refers to deep, balanced, experience-based judgment about life matters.

83. In Erikson's theory, the major psychosocial task of late adulthood is:
   A. intimacy versus isolation
   B. industry versus inferiority
   C. ego integrity versus despair
   D. autonomy versus shame and doubt
  Answer: C. ego integrity versus despair

   Rationale: In late adulthood, people evaluate their lives and either achieve integrity or
experience despair.

84. Which older adult best exemplifies successful aging?
   A. One free of all illness and disability
   B. One who adapts effectively, maintains engagement, and compensates for losses
   C. One who rejects all social ties

 D. One who denies any change in functioning
       Answer: B. One who adapts effectively, maintains engagement, and compensates for
losses
   Rationale: Successful aging is not the absence of all illness but effective adaptation and
continued meaningful engagement.

85. Selective optimization with compensation refers to:
   A. refusing help to maintain pride
   B. focusing on priority goals, maximizing strengths, and adapting to losses
   C. avoiding all challenges in late life

 D. depending entirely on others
       Answer: B. focusing on priority goals, maximizing strengths, and adapting to losses
   Rationale: Selective optimization with compensation involves choosing key goals,
strengthening performance, and compensating for decline.

86. Which experience is most common after retirement for many adults?
   A. A single uniform reaction
   B. Adjustment that varies depending on health, finances, identity, and social support
   C. Immediate severe depression in all cases

 D. Total loss of all roles
       Answer: B. Adjustment that varies depending on health, finances, identity, and social
support
   Rationale: Retirement experiences are diverse and shaped by multiple personal and
contextual variables.

87. Bereavement refers to:
   A. the biological process of dying
   B. the social and personal experience of loss due to death
   C. only funeral rituals

 D. denial of death
       Answer: B. the social and personal experience of loss due to death
   Rationale: Bereavement refers to the condition of having lost someone through death and the
associated adjustment process.

88. Which statement about grief is most accurate?
   A. Everyone passes through identical stages in the same order.
   B. Grief reactions vary widely across persons and cultures.
   C. Healthy grief ends within a fixed number of days.

 D. Strong grief always indicates psychopathology.
       Answer: B. Grief reactions vary widely across persons and cultures.
   Rationale: Contemporary views recognize variability in grief expression, timing, and coping.

89. A person continues to function in daily life while gradually adjusting to a spouse's death and
experiencing recurring sadness. This pattern is:

   A. necessarily abnormal
   B. consistent with common bereavement variation
   C. evidence of psychosis

 D. proof of absent attachment
       Answer: B. consistent with common bereavement variation
   Rationale: Bereaved persons often continue functioning while experiencing waves of
sadness; this can be part of normal adaptation.

90. Which is the best example of an ethical issue at the end of life?
   A. Preference for symbolic play
   B. Questions about autonomy, advance directives, and hastening death
   C. Toilet training resistance

 D. Class inclusion
       Answer: B. Questions about autonomy, advance directives, and hastening death
   Rationale: End-of-life ethics commonly involve autonomy, informed choice, legal directives,
and decisions about life-sustaining treatment.

91. Under the PAP Code of Ethics, which principle requires psychologists and psychometricians
to safeguard privacy and confidentiality?

   A. Integrity only
   B. Respect for the Dignity of Persons and Peoples
   C. Social popularity

 D. Operant conditioning
       Answer: B. Respect for the Dignity of Persons and Peoples
   Rationale: The PAP Code explicitly links dignity with privacy, informed consent, and protection
of confidentiality.

92. A psychometrician is asked to administer and interpret a specialized test for which they have
no training. The most ethical response is to:

   A. proceed to avoid disappointing the client
   B. interpret the test using intuition
   C. refuse or refer unless proper competence and supervision are present

 D. let an untrained assistant handle it
       Answer: C. refuse or refer unless proper competence and supervision are present
   Rationale: Ethical practice requires work within one's competence and appropriate referral or
supervision when beyond one's training.
93. Which is most consistent with informed consent in psychological services?
   A. Obtaining signature only after the session ends
   B. Explaining the nature, purpose, and limits of confidentiality before proceeding
   C. Avoiding discussion of risks to prevent anxiety

 D. Relying on verbal implication in all cases
       Answer: B. Explaining the nature, purpose, and limits of confidentiality before proceeding
   Rationale: Informed consent requires understandable explanation before services begin,
including confidentiality limits.

94. A school contracts a psychology practitioner to assess a student. Ethically, the practitioner
should first clarify:

   A. only the testing fee
   B. who the client is, how results will be used, and limits of confidentiality
   C. only the school's preferred diagnosis

 D. only whether parents are strict
       Answer: B. who the client is, how results will be used, and limits of confidentiality
   Rationale: Third-party requests require clear role clarification, client identification, intended
use of information, and confidentiality limits.

95. Under ethical standards, confidential information may be disclosed without consent primarily
when:

   A. a colleague is curious
   B. disclosure is entertaining
   C. permitted or mandated by law, or needed to protect from harm

 D. a practitioner wants to post a case online
       Answer: C. permitted or mandated by law, or needed to protect from harm
   Rationale: Ethical disclosure without consent is limited to lawful or protective purposes and
only to the extent necessary.

96. A practitioner posts on social media that their intervention "guarantees success for all
children with developmental delays." This is primarily unethical because it:

   A. uses too few words
   B. may be false or deceptive advertising
   C. mentions child development

 D. avoids chapter references
       Answer: B. may be false or deceptive advertising
   Rationale: Guarantees of universal success are misleading and violate standards against
false or deceptive public statements.

97. According to ethical standards, telepsychology:
   A. is exempt from ordinary ethical rules
   B. may ignore confidentiality because it is online
   C. follows the same ethical principles as face-to-face services
 D. is prohibited in all situations
       Answer: C. follows the same ethical principles as face-to-face services
   Rationale: The PAP Code states that telepsychology remains governed by the same ethical
principles as in-person practice.

98. Under RA 10029 and the PAP Code, practice is limited by:
   A. personal confidence alone
   B. popularity in the community
   C. legal licensure and professional boundaries of competence

 D. number of social media followers
       Answer: C. legal licensure and professional boundaries of competence
   Rationale: RA 10029 and the PAP Code emphasize lawful licensure and practice within
competence boundaries.

99. A psychometrician becomes aware that another practitioner's serious misconduct is likely to
cause substantial harm. What is the most ethical action?

   A. Ignore it to avoid conflict
   B. Spread rumors informally
   C. Take further action and report to appropriate authorities, unless confidentiality rules clearly
prohibit it

 D. Publicly shame the person online first
       Answer: C. Take further action and report to appropriate authorities, unless confidentiality
rules clearly prohibit it
   Rationale: When substantial harm is likely, ethical standards support reporting through proper
channels, while still respecting confidentiality limitations.

100. A practitioner's personal distress has become so severe that it impairs judgment during
assessment work. Ethically, the practitioner should:

    A. continue working to prove resilience
    B. conceal the problem from everyone
    C. seek consultation or assistance and consider limiting, suspending, or terminating duties

 D. delegate all work to unqualified staff
        Answer: C. seek consultation or assistance and consider limiting, suspending, or
terminating duties
    Rationale: Ethical competence requires practitioners to address personal problems that
impair professional functioning and protect clients from harm.
DEVELOPMENTAL PSYCHOLOGY
EXAM 7
DEVELOPMENTAL PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 7

1. Which statement best reflects the life-span perspective in developmental psychology?
  A. Development ends in late adolescence because personality is already fixed
  B. Development involves only growth and not decline
  C. Development is lifelong, multidimensional, and shaped by interacting influences

 D. Development is determined mainly by heredity alone
       Answer: C. Development is lifelong, multidimensional, and shaped by interacting
influences
  Rationale: The life-span perspective holds that development continues from conception to
death and is shaped by multiple interacting biological, cognitive, social, and contextual
influences.

2. Which pair correctly represents two major domains of development?
  A. Reflexive and nonreflexive
  B. Physical and psychosocial
  C. Sensorimotor and operational

 D. Conscious and unconscious
       Answer: B. Physical and psychosocial
  Rationale: Development is commonly divided into major domains, including physical,
cognitive, and psychosocial development.

3. A child born during a nationwide economic recession experiences long-term educational
disadvantage because of reduced family income. This is best classified as:

  A. Normative age-graded influence
  B. Normative history-graded influence
  C. Nonnormative influence

 D. Genotype-environment covariance
       Answer: B. Normative history-graded influence
  Rationale: A nationwide economic recession affects many individuals in a particular historical
period, making it a normative history-graded influence.

4. A developmental psychologist is primarily interested in:
  A. Diagnosing only mental disorders
  B. Studying change and stability across the life span
  C. Measuring intelligence only in school-age children

 D. Conducting therapy for all age groups
       Answer: B. Studying change and stability across the life span
  Rationale: Developmental psychology focuses on the scientific study of patterns of change
and stability throughout the entire life span.

5. Which question reflects the issue of continuity versus discontinuity?
  A. Is behavior shaped more by rewards or punishment?
  B. Does development occur gradually or in distinct stages?
  C. Is intelligence inherited or learned?

 D. Does aging affect memory more than language?
       Answer: B. Does development occur gradually or in distinct stages?
  Rationale: The continuity versus discontinuity issue asks whether development unfolds
gradually or through distinct qualitative stages.

6. Freud's theory is most closely associated with the view that:
  A. learning occurs mainly by observation
  B. development is driven by unconscious motives and early experiences
  C. cognition develops through social speech alone

 D. behavior is fully explained by reinforcement schedules
       Answer: B. development is driven by unconscious motives and early experiences
  Rationale: Freud emphasized unconscious drives and early life experiences as central forces
in personality development.

7. Erikson differed from Freud mainly by emphasizing:
  A. psychosexual stages over the entire life span
  B. psychosocial challenges across the life span
  C. classical conditioning in personality growth

 D. moral reasoning in adolescence only
       Answer: B. psychosocial challenges across the life span
  Rationale: Erikson broadened developmental theory by focusing on psychosocial crises that
continue across the entire life span.

8. Piaget described children as:
  A. passive recipients of environmental input
  B. active constructors of knowledge
  C. driven mainly by unconscious conflicts

 D. shaped only by cultural tools
       Answer: B. active constructors of knowledge
  Rationale: Piaget viewed children as active learners who build understanding through
interaction with their environment.

9. Vygotsky emphasized that cognitive growth is strongly influenced by:
  A. maturation of the id
  B. reinforcement contingencies alone
  C. social interaction and culture

 D. inherited intelligence only
       Answer: C. social interaction and culture
  Rationale: Vygotsky stressed that cognitive development is shaped by social interaction,
language, and cultural context.

10. In Bronfenbrenner's ecological theory, the child's immediate setting is the:
   A. chronosystem
   B. exosystem
   C. mesosystem

 D. microsystem
       Answer: D. microsystem
   Rationale: The microsystem refers to the child's direct, immediate environment, such as
family, school, and peers.

11. A researcher who follows the same group of children from age 5 to age 15 is using a:
   A. cross-sectional design
   B. longitudinal design
   C. correlational design

 D. case-study design
       Answer: B. longitudinal design
   Rationale: A longitudinal design studies the same individuals over time to examine
developmental change.

12. Which is the strongest advantage of an experiment?
   A. It always reflects real-life conditions
   B. It can establish cause-and-effect relationships better than most other designs
   C. It avoids all ethical issues

 D. It eliminates the need for sampling
       Answer: B. It can establish cause-and-effect relationships better than most other designs
   Rationale: Experiments allow manipulation and control of variables, making them especially
useful for identifying causal relationships.

13. Which practice best protects research participants ethically?
   A. Withholding all information about the study from all participants
   B. Using deception whenever it makes data collection easier
   C. Obtaining informed consent and minimizing foreseeable harm

 D. Publishing raw identifying data for replication
       Answer: C. Obtaining informed consent and minimizing foreseeable harm
   Rationale: Ethical research requires respecting participant autonomy through informed
consent and protecting them from unnecessary harm.

14. Fertilization normally occurs in the:
   A. uterus
   B. cervix
   C. fallopian tube

 D. placenta
       Answer: C. fallopian tube
   Rationale: Fertilization typically takes place in the fallopian tube before the zygote travels to
the uterus for implantation.

15. A fertilized ovum that divides into two separate embryos will most likely result in:
   A. fraternal twins
   B. monozygotic twins
   C. triplets

 D. dizygotic twins of different sexes
       Answer: B. monozygotic twins
   Rationale: Monozygotic twins result when one fertilized egg splits into two embryos.

16. The observable expression of genetic inheritance is called the:
   A. genotype
   B. phenotype
   C. gamete

 D. zygote
       Answer: B. phenotype
   Rationale: Phenotype refers to the observable characteristics produced by the interaction of
genotype and environment.

17. Down syndrome is most commonly associated with:
   A. recessive inheritance
   B. sex-linked inheritance
   C. chromosomal abnormality involving an extra chromosome 21

 D. lack of prenatal nutrition only
       Answer: C. chromosomal abnormality involving an extra chromosome 21
   Rationale: Down syndrome is most commonly caused by trisomy 21, or the presence of an
extra chromosome 21.

18. The period of prenatal development when the organs begin to form is the:
   A. germinal period
   B. fetal period
   C. embryonic period

 D. neonatal period
       Answer: C. embryonic period
   Rationale: Organ formation begins during the embryonic period, making this phase especially
critical for normal development.

19. Which maternal factor is strongly associated with fetal alcohol spectrum disorders?
   A. high-protein diet
   B. alcohol use during pregnancy
   C. advanced paternal age alone

 D. short labor duration
       Answer: B. alcohol use during pregnancy
   Rationale: Fetal alcohol spectrum disorders result from prenatal exposure to alcohol.

20. The age of viability refers to the point at which:
   A. fertilization can occur
   B. the fetus can survive outside the womb with medical support
   C. the mother first feels fetal movement

 D. labor begins spontaneously
       Answer: B. the fetus can survive outside the womb with medical support
   Rationale: Viability is the point at which the fetus has developed enough to survive outside
the uterus, usually with medical assistance.

21. Cephalocaudal development refers to development proceeding:
   A. from the center outward
   B. from head to toe
   C. from toe to head

 D. from large muscles to small muscles only
       Answer: B. from head to toe
   Rationale: Cephalocaudal development describes the pattern in which growth and motor
control proceed from the head downward.

22. The rooting reflex helps the infant:
   A. grasp objects
   B. turn toward a touch on the cheek and seek the nipple
   C. maintain balance

 D. coordinate walking movements
       Answer: B. turn toward a touch on the cheek and seek the nipple
   Rationale: The rooting reflex helps the infant locate a food source by turning toward
stimulation near the mouth.

23. A baby born weighing significantly less than expected for gestational age is at increased risk
primarily because:

   A. low birth weight is always caused by poor parenting
   B. prematurity and restricted growth are linked with developmental complications
   C. intelligence is fixed at birth

 D. it guarantees lifelong disability
       Answer: B. prematurity and restricted growth are linked with developmental complications
   Rationale: Low birth weight is associated with increased risk for health and developmental
problems, especially when due to prematurity or growth restriction.

24. Which statement about infant brain development is most accurate?
   A. Brain development is complete at birth
   B. Experience has little effect on neural connections
   C. Neural growth is rapid early in life, and experience helps strengthen or eliminate

connections

 D. Pruning always indicates damage
       Answer: C. Neural growth is rapid early in life, and experience helps strengthen or
eliminate connections
   Rationale: Early brain development involves rapid neural growth, and experience plays a
major role in strengthening useful connections and pruning unused ones.

25. According to Piaget, object permanence develops during the:
   A. preoperational stage
   B. formal operational stage
   C. sensorimotor stage

 D. concrete operational stage
       Answer: C. sensorimotor stage
   Rationale: Piaget placed the emergence of object permanence within the sensorimotor stage
of infancy.

26. Habituation in infancy refers to:
   A. distress at a new stimulus
   B. decreasing response to repeated stimulation
   C. fear of strangers

 D. learned helplessness
       Answer: B. decreasing response to repeated stimulation
   Rationale: Habituation occurs when an infant shows reduced response after repeated
exposure to the same stimulus, indicating familiarity.

27. A researcher repeatedly presents a visual pattern to an infant until the infant loses interest,
then introduces a new pattern. This primarily assesses:

   A. social referencing
   B. habituation and discrimination
   C. attachment security

 D. moral reasoning
       Answer: B. habituation and discrimination
   Rationale: This method examines whether the infant becomes habituated to a repeated
stimulus and notices a difference when a new stimulus appears.

28. The concept of the zone of proximal development is associated with:
   A. Piaget
   B. Freud
   C. Vygotsky

 D. Skinner
       Answer: C. Vygotsky
   Rationale: Vygotsky introduced the zone of proximal development to describe the range of
tasks a child can perform with guidance but not yet independently.

29. Child-directed speech is characterized by:
   A. rapid rate and abstract vocabulary
   B. short sentences, exaggerated intonation, and simple words
   C. grammatical errors designed to confuse the child
 D. total absence of emotional tone
       Answer: B. short sentences, exaggerated intonation, and simple words
   Rationale: Child-directed speech uses simple structure and expressive tone to support
language learning and attention.

30. Noam Chomsky is best known for proposing that:
   A. language is learned only by imitation
   B. language development depends on a built-in capacity for language
   C. intelligence precedes all communication

 D. private speech is the main basis of language
       Answer: B. language development depends on a built-in capacity for language
   Rationale: Chomsky proposed that humans are biologically prepared for language acquisition
through an innate language capacity.

31. Trust versus mistrust is the central psychosocial conflict of:
   A. infancy
   B. early childhood
   C. middle childhood

 D. adolescence
       Answer: A. infancy
   Rationale: Erikson identified trust versus mistrust as the major psychosocial conflict of
infancy.

32. Mary Ainsworth is best known for her work on:
   A. moral reasoning
   B. attachment patterns
   C. operant conditioning

 D. identity statuses
       Answer: B. attachment patterns
   Rationale: Ainsworth is known for identifying attachment patterns through her Strange
Situation research.

33. A securely attached infant is most likely to:
   A. ignore the caregiver completely
   B. use the caregiver as a secure base for exploration
   C. avoid all contact after separation

 D. show no distress under any condition
       Answer: B. use the caregiver as a secure base for exploration
   Rationale: Securely attached infants explore their environment confidently while relying on
the caregiver as a source of safety and comfort.

34. Social referencing occurs when infants:
   A. imitate television characters
   B. look to a trusted adult for cues about an unfamiliar situation
   C. prefer peers to caregivers

 D. develop object permanence
       Answer: B. look to a trusted adult for cues about an unfamiliar situation
   Rationale: Social referencing involves using another person's emotional cues to guide one's
behavior in uncertain situations.

35. Temperament refers to:
   A. learned moral values
   B. biologically based, relatively stable styles of emotional reactivity and regulation
   C. unconscious sexual drives

 D. fixed intelligence levels
       Answer: B. biologically based, relatively stable styles of emotional reactivity and regulation
   Rationale: Temperament refers to early-emerging, biologically influenced patterns of
emotional response and self-regulation.

36. The rouge test is commonly used to assess:
   A. language delay
   B. self-recognition
   C. stranger anxiety

 D. handedness
       Answer: B. self-recognition
   Rationale: The rouge test measures whether a child recognizes the self in a mirror, which
indicates self-awareness.

37. According to Erikson, autonomy versus shame and doubt is central during:
   A. infancy
   B. toddlerhood
   C. middle childhood

 D. adolescence
       Answer: B. toddlerhood
   Rationale: Erikson viewed toddlerhood as the period in which children develop autonomy
through growing self-control and independence.

38. Piaget's preoperational child is especially likely to show:
   A. hypothetical-deductive reasoning
   B. conservation
   C. egocentrism and centration

 D. formal logic
       Answer: C. egocentrism and centration
   Rationale: Preoperational thinking is marked by egocentrism and centration, limiting the
child's ability to consider multiple aspects of a situation.

39. A child says that a taller glass has more water than a shorter, wider glass, even after seeing
the same amount poured from one to the other. This shows failure of:
   A. accommodation
   B. object permanence
   C. conservation

 D. reversibility only
       Answer: C. conservation
   Rationale: The child fails to understand that quantity remains constant despite changes in
appearance, demonstrating lack of conservation.

40. Theory of mind refers to understanding that:
   A. all children think alike
   B. people have mental states such as beliefs, desires, and intentions
   C. behavior is determined entirely by reinforcement

 D. dreams are more real than waking life
       Answer: B. people have mental states such as beliefs, desires, and intentions
   Rationale: Theory of mind is the understanding that people's behavior is influenced by
internal mental states.

41. Private speech in young children is best interpreted by Vygotsky as:
   A. evidence of pathology
   B. immature egocentrism only
   C. a tool for self-guidance and self-regulation

 D. random language without function
       Answer: C. a tool for self-guidance and self-regulation
   Rationale: Vygotsky viewed private speech as a meaningful tool children use to guide thinking
and behavior.

42. Which parenting style is generally linked with the most positive developmental outcomes?
   A. Authoritarian
   B. Neglectful
   C. Authoritative

 D. Permissive
       Answer: C. Authoritative
   Rationale: Authoritative parenting combines warmth and structure, which is generally
associated with healthier developmental outcomes.

43. Preschool children's play increasingly becomes:
   A. entirely reflexive
   B. more symbolic and socially coordinated
   C. less imaginative over time

 D. unrelated to cognitive growth
       Answer: B. more symbolic and socially coordinated
   Rationale: As preschoolers develop cognitively and socially, their play becomes more
imaginative, symbolic, and cooperative.
44. According to Erikson, the central conflict of early childhood is:
   A. initiative versus guilt
   B. identity versus role confusion
   C. industry versus inferiority

 D. integrity versus despair
       Answer: A. initiative versus guilt
   Rationale: Erikson identified initiative versus guilt as the key psychosocial conflict of early
childhood.

45. Middle childhood is marked cognitively by the emergence of:
   A. sensorimotor intelligence
   B. concrete operational thought
   C. preconventional morality only

 D. postformal thought
       Answer: B. concrete operational thought
   Rationale: During middle childhood, children develop concrete operational thinking, allowing
more logical reasoning about tangible situations.

46. In concrete operational thought, children improve especially in:
   A. abstract hypothetical reasoning
   B. conservation and classification
   C. egocentric speech

 D. object permanence
       Answer: B. conservation and classification
   Rationale: Concrete operational children become better at mental operations such as
conservation, classification, and logical grouping.

47. Metamemory refers to:
   A. loss of memory with age
   B. one's knowledge about how memory works
   C. unconscious memories

 D. photographic memory
       Answer: B. one's knowledge about how memory works
   Rationale: Metamemory is awareness and understanding of memory processes and
strategies.

48. A child who organizes information into meaningful groups to remember it is using:
   A. scaffolding
   B. centration
   C. a mnemonic strategy

 D. reciprocal determinism
       Answer: C. a mnemonic strategy
   Rationale: Organizing information into meaningful groups is a memory aid, or mnemonic
strategy, that improves recall.
49. Which statement about IQ is most accurate?
   A. It is unaffected by environment
   B. It is a perfect measure of all forms of intelligence
   C. It reflects certain cognitive abilities but is influenced by both heredity and environment

 D. It remains identical across the entire life span in all areas
       Answer: C. It reflects certain cognitive abilities but is influenced by both heredity and
environment
   Rationale: IQ reflects important cognitive abilities, but it is shaped by both genetic and
environmental influences and is not a complete measure of all intelligence.

50. Erikson's industry versus inferiority is especially relevant to:
   A. willingness to explore unfamiliar settings
   B. mastery of valued skills in school and society
   C. formation of marital intimacy

 D. adjustment to retirement
       Answer: B. mastery of valued skills in school and society
   Rationale: Industry versus inferiority centers on children's efforts to develop competence in
tasks valued by school, family, and society.

51. Peer acceptance in middle childhood is important because it is linked to:
   A. no later adjustment outcomes
   B. social competence and emotional well-being
   C. automatic academic failure

 D. independence from all adults
       Answer: B. social competence and emotional well-being
   Rationale: Positive peer relationships contribute to children's social adjustment, self-esteem,
and emotional development.

52. Bullying is best understood as:
   A. harmless teasing between equals
   B. repeated aggression involving a power imbalance
   C. a sign of advanced social intelligence

 D. always physical rather than relational
       Answer: B. repeated aggression involving a power imbalance
   Rationale: Bullying involves repeated harmful behavior in which one person holds more
power than the target.

53. Puberty refers to:
   A. cognitive maturity
   B. physical changes leading to sexual maturity
   C. social independence from parents

 D. the start of legal adulthood
       Answer: B. physical changes leading to sexual maturity
   Rationale: Puberty consists of biological changes that lead to reproductive maturity.

54. Early-maturing boys are often:
   A. always socially rejected
   B. viewed more positively in many peer contexts
   C. less likely to engage in risk behavior

 D. indistinguishable from late maturers in all settings
       Answer: B. viewed more positively in many peer contexts
   Rationale: Early-maturing boys are often perceived as more mature or socially desirable in
peer settings.

55. Piaget's formal operational stage involves:
   A. object permanence
   B. symbolic play only
   C. abstract and hypothetical reasoning

 D. learning by conditioning only
       Answer: C. abstract and hypothetical reasoning
   Rationale: Formal operational thought allows adolescents to reason abstractly and think
hypothetically.

56. Adolescent egocentrism includes the belief that:
   A. adults think exactly like adolescents
   B. one's experiences are unique and others are constantly noticing them
   C. no one can reason logically

 D. moral rules never change
       Answer: B. one's experiences are unique and others are constantly noticing them
   Rationale: Adolescent egocentrism includes the personal fable and imaginary audience,
reflecting beliefs of uniqueness and constant observation by others.

57. Kohlberg's theory focused on the development of:
   A. attachment security
   B. moral reasoning
   C. psychosexual identity

 D. intelligence testing
       Answer: B. moral reasoning
   Rationale: Kohlberg's theory examined how moral reasoning develops through increasingly
complex levels and stages.

58. Carol Gilligan criticized Kohlberg partly because his model:
   A. ignored moral reasoning completely
   B. overemphasized care and relationships
   C. may have undervalued a care-based orientation in moral thought

 D. was based entirely on infant studies
       Answer: C. may have undervalued a care-based orientation in moral thought
   Rationale: Gilligan argued that Kohlberg's model may have overlooked moral reasoning
centered on care, relationships, and responsibility.

59. James Marcia's identity statuses are based on the dimensions of:
   A. trust and mistrust
   B. assimilation and accommodation
   C. crisis/exploration and commitment

 D. ego and superego
       Answer: C. crisis/exploration and commitment
   Rationale: Marcia classified identity development according to whether an individual has
explored alternatives and made commitments.

60. An adolescent actively exploring alternatives but not yet committed is in:
   A. identity achievement
   B. foreclosure
   C. moratorium

 D. diffusion
       Answer: C. moratorium
   Rationale: Moratorium describes a status in which the adolescent is actively exploring but has
not yet committed to a clear identity choice.

61. Authoritative parenting during adolescence is generally associated with:
   A. poorer monitoring and higher delinquency
   B. better adjustment and self-regulation
   C. complete absence of parent-child conflict

 D. automatic academic excellence without effort
       Answer: B. better adjustment and self-regulation
   Rationale: Authoritative parenting supports adolescent competence, better adjustment, and
stronger self-regulation.

62. Juvenile delinquency is best understood as resulting from:
   A. one single biological cause
   B. only poor parenting
   C. interaction of biological, family, peer, and community influences

 D. moral immaturity alone
       Answer: C. interaction of biological, family, peer, and community influences
   Rationale: Juvenile delinquency is multidetermined and is best explained by interacting
biological, family, peer, and broader social factors.

63. Emerging adulthood is best described as:
   A. a period of fixed adult roles immediately after puberty
   B. a transitional period of exploration in love, work, and identity
   C. a stage limited to married persons
   D. the same as middle adulthood
  Answer: B. a transitional period of exploration in love, work, and identity

   Rationale: Emerging adulthood is characterized by identity exploration and instability in major
areas such as relationships and vocation.

64. Postformal thought in adulthood is often described as:
   A. less logical than childhood thought
   B. more rigid than adolescent thought
   C. practical, flexible, and able to deal with ambiguity

 D. identical to sensorimotor thinking
       Answer: C. practical, flexible, and able to deal with ambiguity
   Rationale: Postformal thought is often viewed as realistic, flexible, and capable of handling
contradictions and ambiguity.

65. Schaie's life-span model is associated with:
   A. adult cognitive development
   B. attachment development
   C. psychosexual stages

 D. operant conditioning
       Answer: A. adult cognitive development
   Rationale: Schaie's life-span model describes changing uses and patterns of intelligence
across adulthood.

66. Sternberg's triarchic theory includes:
   A. id, ego, and superego
   B. analytical, creative, and practical intelligence
   C. sensory, short-term, and long-term memory

 D. crystallized, fluid, and emotional intelligence only
       Answer: B. analytical, creative, and practical intelligence
   Rationale: Sternberg proposed that intelligence consists of analytical, creative, and practical
components.

67. The psychosocial task most associated with young adulthood in Erikson's theory is:
   A. initiative versus guilt
   B. industry versus inferiority
   C. intimacy versus isolation

 D. integrity versus despair
       Answer: C. intimacy versus isolation
   Rationale: Erikson identified intimacy versus isolation as the central psychosocial conflict of
young adulthood.

68. In research on adult relationships, cohabitation is best viewed as:
   A. always identical in meaning across all couples
   B. uniformly associated with poor outcomes
   C. variable in meaning and outcome depending on context and commitment
 D. impossible before marriage
       Answer: C. variable in meaning and outcome depending on context and commitment
   Rationale: Cohabitation differs widely in meaning, stability, and outcome depending on the
couple's circumstances and level of commitment.

69. Generativity in middle adulthood refers mainly to:
   A. withdrawal from society
   B. concern for guiding the next generation
   C. cognitive slowing

 D. dependence on adult children
       Answer: B. concern for guiding the next generation
   Rationale: Generativity refers to the adult's desire to contribute to society and guide future
generations.

70. The idea of a universal midlife crisis is best supported by research as:
   A. inevitable for nearly all adults
   B. a normative biological event
   C. not universal; midlife experiences vary greatly

 D. present only in women
       Answer: C. not universal; midlife experiences vary greatly
   Rationale: Research shows that a midlife crisis is not universal, and midlife experiences differ
substantially among adults.

71. Fluid intelligence generally refers to:
   A. accumulated knowledge
   B. vocabulary and acquired information
   C. novel problem-solving ability

 D. wisdom based on life review
       Answer: C. novel problem-solving ability
   Rationale: Fluid intelligence refers to the ability to solve new problems and think flexibly in
unfamiliar situations.

72. Crystallized intelligence generally refers to:
   A. speed of processing
   B. accumulated knowledge and verbal skills
   C. reflexive behavior

 D. visual acuity
       Answer: B. accumulated knowledge and verbal skills
   Rationale: Crystallized intelligence reflects knowledge, vocabulary, and skills acquired
through education and experience.

73. Which statement about creativity in middle adulthood is most accurate?
   A. Creativity always disappears by age 40
   B. Creativity may remain strong and can be supported by expertise and opportunity
   C. Creativity is unrelated to experience

 D. Only artists show creativity
       Answer: B. Creativity may remain strong and can be supported by expertise and
opportunity
   Rationale: Creativity can remain high in middle adulthood, especially when supported by
accumulated knowledge, expertise, and opportunity.

74. Retirement adjustment is usually best predicted by:
   A. age alone
   B. sudden cognitive decline in all retirees
   C. health, finances, identity, and social support

 D. whether one has grandchildren
       Answer: C. health, finances, identity, and social support
   Rationale: Retirement adjustment depends on multiple personal and contextual factors such
as health, financial security, sense of identity, and social support.

75. Selective optimization with compensation refers to:
   A. a method of infant conditioning
   B. a strategy of adapting to aging by focusing on priorities, maximizing strengths, and

offsetting losses
   C. a theory of adolescent risk-taking

 D. a test of executive function
       Answer: B. a strategy of adapting to aging by focusing on priorities, maximizing strengths,
and offsetting losses
   Rationale: Selective optimization with compensation describes how older adults adapt by
prioritizing goals, building on strengths, and compensating for losses.

76. Dementia is:
   A. a normal and inevitable part of aging
   B. severe cognitive impairment that interferes with daily functioning
   C. equivalent to wisdom

 D. caused only by depression
       Answer: B. severe cognitive impairment that interferes with daily functioning
   Rationale: Dementia is a serious cognitive decline that disrupts everyday functioning and is
not a normal consequence of aging.

77. Which memory tends to show relative preservation in many older adults?
   A. Working memory under all conditions
   B. Episodic recall for recent events only
   C. Some forms of semantic and procedural memory

 D. Sensory memory only
       Answer: C. Some forms of semantic and procedural memory
   Rationale: In many older adults, general knowledge and well-practiced skills remain relatively
preserved compared with some other memory systems.
78. Erikson's final psychosocial conflict is:
   A. trust versus mistrust
   B. identity versus role confusion
   C. generativity versus stagnation

 D. integrity versus despair
       Answer: D. integrity versus despair
   Rationale: Erikson's final psychosocial stage involves reflecting on one's life with either
acceptance and wholeness or regret and despair.

79. Ego integrity is most closely associated with:
   A. resentment over all life choices
   B. acceptance of one's life as meaningful and coherent
   C. refusal to acknowledge aging

 D. dependence on others for self-worth
       Answer: B. acceptance of one's life as meaningful and coherent
   Rationale: Ego integrity involves accepting one's life as meaningful, complete, and worth
living.

80. Widowhood in late adulthood is best understood as:
   A. a uniform experience with identical outcomes
   B. always more distressing for men than women
   C. a major transition shaped by prior relationship quality, health, support, and finances

 D. irrelevant to well-being after age 65
       Answer: C. a major transition shaped by prior relationship quality, health, support, and
finances
   Rationale: Widowhood is a major life transition whose impact depends on personal, relational,
and contextual factors.

81. Kübler-Ross is most associated with:
   A. operant conditioning
   B. stages commonly discussed in relation to dying
   C. attachment categories

 D. intelligence testing
       Answer: B. stages commonly discussed in relation to dying
   Rationale: Kübler-Ross is widely associated with the stages often discussed in relation to
responses to dying.

82. Bereavement refers to:
   A. the biological process of dying
   B. the emotional response to loss only in children
   C. the state of having suffered a loss through death

 D. denial of mortality
       Answer: C. the state of having suffered a loss through death
   Rationale: Bereavement refers to the condition of having experienced the death of someone
significant.

83. Which statement about grief is most accurate?
   A. Healthy grief follows the same fixed sequence in all people
   B. Grief patterns vary considerably across persons and cultures
   C. Grief should end completely within one month

 D. Intense grief always indicates psychopathology
       Answer: B. Grief patterns vary considerably across persons and cultures
   Rationale: Grief does not follow a single universal pattern and varies across individuals,
relationships, and cultural contexts.

84. A patient with terminal illness prepares an advance directive refusing certain life-sustaining
procedures. This primarily reflects:

   A. random impulsivity
   B. exercise of autonomous end-of-life decision making
   C. abandonment of treatment by the family

 D. unlawful refusal of care in all cases
       Answer: B. exercise of autonomous end-of-life decision making
   Rationale: An advance directive reflects a person's autonomous choice about future medical
care and end-of-life treatment.

85. According to the PAP Code of Ethics and RA 10029-related practice boundaries, only who
may legally practice psychology or psychometrics?

   A. Any psychology graduate with internship experience
   B. Only licensed and registered psychologists and psychometricians
   C. Any guidance counselor administering tests

 D. Any physician interested in mental testing
       Answer: B. Only licensed and registered psychologists and psychometricians
   Rationale: RA 10029 and related ethical standards require that the legal practice of
psychology and psychometrics be done only by licensed and registered professionals.

86. A psychometrician is asked to administer an unfamiliar specialized neuropsychological
battery without training. The most ethical response is to:

   A. proceed to gain experience
   B. administer only the easy subtests
   C. decline or refer unless competence is first obtained

 D. allow the client to self-administer online
       Answer: C. decline or refer unless competence is first obtained
   Rationale: Ethical practice requires working within one's professional competence and
making appropriate referrals when necessary.

87. Which action best reflects proper delegation of work?
   A. Delegating confidential test scoring to an untrained friend
   B. Assigning tasks only to persons competent to perform them and informing the client of
delegation

   C. Letting any staff member interpret test results

 D. Delegating work without supervision to save time
       Answer: B. Assigning tasks only to persons competent to perform them and informing the
client of delegation
   Rationale: Proper delegation requires that tasks be assigned only to competent individuals
and that the client be informed appropriately.

88. Before beginning telepsychology services, the practitioner should:
   A. assume online work is exempt from informed consent
   B. obtain informed consent and explain risks, limits, and procedures
   C. record sessions automatically without discussion

 D. ignore possible technology interruptions
       Answer: B. obtain informed consent and explain risks, limits, and procedures
   Rationale: Telepsychology requires informed consent, including discussion of privacy risks,
limitations, and the procedures for remote service delivery.

89. A client discloses suicidal intent with a clear imminent plan. Under the Code, the
psychologist may disclose information:

   A. never, because confidentiality is absolute
   B. only after the client signs a publicity waiver
   C. when necessary after careful deliberation to protect the client or community from imminent
danger

 D. only to friends chosen by the therapist
       Answer: C. when necessary after careful deliberation to protect the client or community
from imminent danger
   Rationale: Confidentiality may be limited when disclosure is necessary to protect the client or
others from imminent serious harm.

90. Which practice is ethically correct in assessment?
   A. Releasing raw test items freely to anyone who asks
   B. Using photocopied test materials if the originals are expensive
   C. Selecting valid, reliable, appropriate tools and protecting test security

 D. Interpreting results without considering client characteristics
       Answer: C. Selecting valid, reliable, appropriate tools and protecting test security
   Rationale: Ethical assessment requires the use of appropriate psychometric tools and the
protection of test materials and interpretation processes.

91. A practitioner posts on social media that their services guarantee cure for depression. This
is unethical mainly because it:

   A. is too brief to be useful
   B. makes deceptive and unsupported public claims
   C. uses social media
 D. discusses mental health publicly at all
       Answer: B. makes deceptive and unsupported public claims
   Rationale: Ethical standards prohibit false, deceptive, or misleading public statements about
professional services and outcomes.

92. A psychology practitioner is asked by a school principal to assess a student. Ethically, the
practitioner should clarify at the outset:

   A. only the testing fee
   B. who the client is, the role of the practitioner, probable uses of information, and limits of
confidentiality
   C. only the student's diagnosis

 D. that results will be shared with all teachers automatically
       Answer: B. who the client is, the role of the practitioner, probable uses of information, and
limits of confidentiality
   Rationale: In third-party requests for services, ethical practice requires clarifying roles, client
identity, intended use of information, and limits of confidentiality.

93. In research with participants below 18 years old, ethical practice requires:
   A. assent from the child only
   B. consent from parents only, never assent
   C. informed assent from the minor and informed consent from parent or legal guardian

 D. no consent if the study is educational
       Answer: C. informed assent from the minor and informed consent from parent or legal
guardian
   Rationale: Research with minors requires parental or guardian consent and, when
appropriate, the child's assent.

94. A researcher offers an excessively large payment to economically disadvantaged
participants for a high-risk study. The main ethical concern is:

   A. low external validity
   B. coercion or undue inducement
   C. poor operational definition

 D. maturation effects
       Answer: B. coercion or undue inducement
   Rationale: Excessive payment may pressure vulnerable individuals to participate against their
better judgment, compromising voluntary consent.

95. Which statement best reflects ethical handling of recorded client sessions?
   A. Recording is acceptable whenever it helps supervision
   B. Consent must be obtained before recording voices or images, with anticipated uses

explained
   C. Recording is allowed if the client remains silent
   D. Recordings can be posted for teaching if names are removed informally
  Answer: B. Consent must be obtained before recording voices or images, with anticipated

uses explained
   Rationale: Ethical practice requires prior informed consent before recording, along with a

clear explanation of how the recording will be used.

96. In early adulthood, intimacy is best understood as:
   A. sexual activity alone
   B. capacity for close, reciprocal commitment without losing one's identity
   C. dependence on parents for approval

 D. avoidance of emotional vulnerability
       Answer: B. capacity for close, reciprocal commitment without losing one's identity
   Rationale: Healthy intimacy involves forming close, mutual relationships while maintaining a
stable sense of self.

97. Which scenario best illustrates reciprocal determinism in Bandura's view?
   A. Biology alone shapes all behavior
   B. Behavior, personal factors, and environment influence one another
   C. Reinforcement is irrelevant to learning

 D. Cognitive factors never affect behavior
       Answer: B. Behavior, personal factors, and environment influence one another
   Rationale: Reciprocal determinism means that behavior, internal personal factors, and the
environment continuously interact and influence each other.

98. A child watches an older sibling aggressively seize toys and then imitates the behavior. This
is best explained by:

   A. classical conditioning
   B. observational learning
   C. object permanence

 D. equilibration
       Answer: B. observational learning
   Rationale: Observational learning occurs when behavior is acquired by watching and imitating
a model.

99. Which best illustrates a sensitive period?
   A. A time when learning is impossible after infancy
   B. A period when certain experiences are especially influential for development
   C. A stage that occurs only in adolescence

 D. A theory that maturation has no role
       Answer: B. A period when certain experiences are especially influential for development
   Rationale: A sensitive period is a developmental window during which particular experiences
have especially strong effects on growth.

100. A practitioner's personal stress is beginning to impair concentration during sessions. The
most ethical action is to:
    A. continue practice unchanged to avoid losing income
    B. increase caseload to improve confidence
    C. seek consultation or assistance and consider limiting, suspending, or terminating affected
duties

 D. ask clients to adjust to the practitioner's condition
        Answer: C. seek consultation or assistance and consider limiting, suspending, or
terminating affected duties
    Rationale: Ethical practice requires practitioners to monitor impairment and take appropriate
steps to protect clients when personal problems interfere with competence.
DEVELOPMENTAL PSYCHOLOGY
EXAM 8
DEVELOPMENTAL PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 8

1. Which statement best reflects the life-span perspective in developmental psychology?
  A. Development ends once biological maturity is reached.
  B. Development consists only of age-related gains.
  C. Development involves both change and stability from conception to death.

 D. Development is determined primarily by heredity.
       Answer: C. Development involves both change and stability from conception to death.
  Rationale: Life-span developmental psychology views development as a lifelong process
involving both continuity and change across all periods of life.

2. A developmental psychologist wants to compare the vocabulary of 4-year-olds, 8-year-olds,
and 12-year-olds at one point in time. Which design is most appropriate?

  A. Longitudinal design
  B. Cross-sectional design
  C. Sequential design

 D. Case study design
       Answer: B. Cross-sectional design
  Rationale: A cross-sectional design compares groups of different ages at the same time,
making it appropriate for vocabulary comparisons across age groups.

3. Which theorist emphasized the psychosocial crisis of trust versus mistrust during infancy?
  A. Jean Piaget
  B. Erik Erikson
  C. B. F. Skinner

 D. Lawrence Kohlberg
       Answer: B. Erik Erikson
  Rationale: Erikson proposed psychosocial stages, and trust versus mistrust is the major crisis
of infancy in his theory.

4. A child solves a difficult puzzle successfully only when guided by an older sibling. This best
illustrates:

  A. object permanence
  B. conservation
  C. zone of proximal development

 D. operant conditioning
       Answer: C. zone of proximal development
  Rationale: The zone of proximal development refers to tasks a child can do with assistance
but not yet independently, highlighting guided learning.

5. Which concept refers to influences that affect many people of a particular generation?
  A. Nonnormative influence
  B. Normative history-graded influence
  C. Sensitive period
 D. Phenotype
       Answer: B. Normative history-graded influence
  Rationale: Normative history-graded influences are common experiences shared by a
generation, such as war, recession, or pandemic.

6. Which statement best distinguishes maturation from learning?
  A. Maturation refers to change due to instruction.
  B. Maturation refers to genetically programmed sequences of development.
  C. Learning refers only to school-based acquisition.

 D. Learning occurs independently of experience.
       Answer: B. Maturation refers to genetically programmed sequences of development.
  Rationale: Maturation involves biologically guided growth processes that unfold in a relatively
orderly sequence.

7. A fertilized ovum divides and forms a blastocyst before implantation. This process occurs
during:

  A. infancy
  B. embryonic development
  C. the germinal period

 D. the fetal period
       Answer: C. the germinal period
  Rationale: The germinal period begins at fertilization and includes early cell division and
implantation.

8. Which prenatal period is characterized by the formation of major organs and body systems?
  A. Germinal period
  B. Embryonic period
  C. Fetal period

 D. Neonatal period
       Answer: B. Embryonic period
  Rationale: Major organ formation occurs during the embryonic period, making this stage highly
sensitive to teratogens.

9. A counselor explains to prospective parents that they already have one child with a
chromosomal disorder and want to know the probability of recurrence in future pregnancies. The
most appropriate referral is for:

  A. behavior modification
  B. genetic counseling
  C. occupational therapy

 D. speech intervention
       Answer: B. genetic counseling
  Rationale: Genetic counseling helps families understand inherited risks, recurrence
probabilities, and options related to genetic conditions.
10. Which maternal behavior poses a major teratogenic risk during pregnancy?
   A. Reading aloud daily
   B. Moderate hydration
   C. Heavy alcohol use

 D. Routine prenatal consultation
       Answer: C. Heavy alcohol use
   Rationale: Heavy alcohol use is a major prenatal risk and can produce serious teratogenic
effects, including fetal alcohol spectrum problems.

11. Which statement about low-birth-weight infants is most accurate?
   A. All low-birth-weight infants are postmature.
   B. Low birth weight may result from prematurity or restricted fetal growth.
   C. Low birth weight has no association with later developmental outcomes.

 D. Low birth weight always indicates chromosomal abnormality.
       Answer: B. Low birth weight may result from prematurity or restricted fetal growth.
   Rationale: Low birth weight is a descriptive outcome that may arise from being born too early
or from poor fetal growth.

12. In a newborn, the Apgar scale is primarily used to:
   A. diagnose intelligence level
   B. assess physical condition shortly after birth
   C. determine attachment style

 D. predict adult personality
       Answer: B. assess physical condition shortly after birth
   Rationale: The Apgar score is a rapid postnatal indicator of newborn status, including heart
rate, respiration, muscle tone, reflexes, and color.

13. Which developmental pattern is illustrated when infants gain control of the head before the
legs?

   A. Proximodistal trend
   B. Cephalocaudal trend
   C. Classical conditioning

 D. Canalization
       Answer: B. Cephalocaudal trend
   Rationale: Cephalocaudal development proceeds from head to tail, so control of the head
appears before lower-body control.

14. A baby turns toward a loud sound and later reaches for the source. This behavior reflects
early:

   A. sensory and perceptual development
   B. symbolic reasoning
   C. formal operational thought

 D. moral internalization
       Answer: A. sensory and perceptual development
   Rationale: Orienting to sound and coordinating perception with action reflect early sensory
and perceptual functioning.

15. According to Piaget, the major cognitive achievement of the sensorimotor stage is:
   A. mastery of hypothetical reasoning
   B. conservation of number
   C. object permanence

 D. deductive logic
       Answer: C. object permanence
   Rationale: A major sensorimotor achievement is understanding that objects continue to exist
even when not currently perceived.

16. An infant repeatedly shakes a rattle and smiles when the sound occurs, then continues
doing so. This is best explained by:

   A. operant conditioning
   B. imprinting
   C. delayed imitation

 D. conservation
       Answer: A. operant conditioning
   Rationale: The infant repeats a behavior because it produces an interesting consequence,
which is the essence of operant conditioning.

17. Which finding would most strongly support Vygotsky's view of cognitive development?
   A. Children learn best when left entirely on their own.
   B. Social interaction helps children internalize culturally valued ways of thinking.
   C. Cognitive growth depends only on biological maturation.

 D. Development progresses through fixed universal stages without cultural variation.
       Answer: B. Social interaction helps children internalize culturally valued ways of thinking.
   Rationale: Vygotsky emphasized that cognitive growth is socially mediated and culturally
organized.

18. A toddler calls all four-legged animals "dog." This is an example of:
   A. overregularization
   B. overextension
   C. private speech

 D. egocentrism
       Answer: B. overextension
   Rationale: Overextension occurs when a child uses one word too broadly, such as calling all
four-legged animals "dog."

19. Which statement best reflects the role of temperament in infancy?
   A. Temperament is identical in all infants.
   B. Temperament refers to biologically based individual differences in emotional style and

regulation.
   C. Temperament is determined solely by parenting style.

 D. Temperament becomes relevant only in adolescence.
       Answer: B. Temperament refers to biologically based individual differences in emotional
style and regulation.
   Rationale: Temperament involves early-appearing, partly biologically rooted patterns of
emotional reactivity and self-regulation.

20. A securely attached infant is most likely to:
   A. ignore the caregiver completely after separation
   B. use the caregiver as a base for exploration
   C. show no distress in unfamiliar settings

 D. reject contact after reunion
       Answer: B. use the caregiver as a base for exploration
   Rationale: Securely attached infants balance exploration with trust in the caregiver's
availability.

21. The "social smile" is best understood as an early sign of:
   A. formal logic
   B. social responsiveness
   C. moral reasoning

 D. autobiographical memory
       Answer: B. social responsiveness
   Rationale: The social smile reflects early engagement with others and growing social
reciprocity.

22. During toddlerhood, the increasing use of "mine" and "me do it" most directly reflects:
   A. initiative
   B. emerging self-concept and autonomy
   C. generativity

 D. identity foreclosure
       Answer: B. emerging self-concept and autonomy
   Rationale: Toddler insistence on self-ownership and independent action reflects a growing
sense of self and autonomy.

23. Which parental response is most likely to promote conscience development in toddlers?
   A. Harsh punishment without explanation
   B. Consistent guidance paired with warmth
   C. Total absence of limits

 D. Frequent ridicule of mistakes
       Answer: B. Consistent guidance paired with warmth
   Rationale: Warm, consistent discipline supports internalization, empathy, and conscience
formation more effectively than harshness.

24. Failure to thrive in infancy is most likely to raise concern about:
   A. only genetics
   B. only nutrition
   C. possible neglect or severe caregiving problems

 D. superior adaptation
       Answer: C. possible neglect or severe caregiving problems
   Rationale: Failure to thrive can reflect nutritional problems and may also signal neglect,
deprivation, or severe caregiving disturbance.

25. A preschooler believes the moon follows her wherever she goes. This best illustrates:
   A. conservation
   B. animism and egocentric thought
   C. postformal thought

 D. inductive logic
       Answer: B. animism and egocentric thought
   Rationale: Preschoolers may attribute life-like qualities or self-related meanings to inanimate
events, reflecting preoperational limitations.

26. Which task is a preschooler in Piaget's preoperational stage most likely to fail?
   A. Deferred imitation
   B. Symbolic play
   C. Conservation of liquid quantity

 D. Using simple sentences
       Answer: C. Conservation of liquid quantity
   Rationale: Preoperational children often judge quantity by appearance and typically fail
conservation tasks.

27. A child talks aloud while assembling blocks and gradually becomes better organized.
Vygotsky would describe this as:

   A. echolalia
   B. private speech aiding self-regulation
   C. moral realism

 D. object permanence
       Answer: B. private speech aiding self-regulation
   Rationale: Vygotsky viewed self-directed speech as a tool children use to guide behavior and
thinking.

28. Which factor most strongly supports emergent literacy in early childhood?
   A. Exclusive reliance on worksheets
   B. Rich language exposure and shared book reading
   C. Delaying speech until school age

 D. Avoiding pretend play
       Answer: B. Rich language exposure and shared book reading
   Rationale: Emergent literacy is fostered by conversational language, storytelling, print
exposure, and reading interactions.
29. A preschool child can understand that another person may hold a false belief. This suggests
development of:

   A. reversibility
   B. theory of mind
   C. transitive inference

 D. postconventional morality
       Answer: B. theory of mind
   Rationale: Understanding that others can hold beliefs different from reality reflects theory of
mind.

30. According to Erikson, the central psychosocial conflict of early childhood is:
   A. trust versus mistrust
   B. autonomy versus shame and doubt
   C. initiative versus guilt

 D. industry versus inferiority
       Answer: C. initiative versus guilt
   Rationale: In early childhood, children strive to act purposefully and develop initiative while
learning limits.

31. Which parenting style is generally associated with the most favorable developmental
outcomes in children?

   A. Authoritarian
   B. Permissive
   C. Neglectful

 D. Authoritative
       Answer: D. Authoritative
   Rationale: Authoritative parenting combines warmth with structure and is most consistently
linked with adaptive developmental outcomes.

32. Rough-and-tumble play in middle childhood is best understood as:
   A. always a sign of aggression disorder
   B. developmentally normal physical play that can support social competence
   C. evidence of moral decline

 D. incompatible with peer acceptance
       Answer: B. developmentally normal physical play that can support social competence
   Rationale: Rough-and-tumble play is often normal, distinct from hostile aggression, and can
help children practice social negotiation.

33. A school-age child who can mentally reverse operations and understand conservation is in
Piaget's:

   A. preoperational stage
   B. concrete operational stage
   C. formal operational stage
 D. sensorimotor stage
       Answer: B. concrete operational stage
   Rationale: Concrete operational thought includes conservation, decentration, and mental
reversibility.

34. Which ability improves notably in middle childhood and contributes to better academic
performance?

   A. Reflexive grasping
   B. Executive functioning
   C. Sensorimotor circular reactions

 D. Neonatal state regulation
       Answer: B. Executive functioning
   Rationale: Planning, inhibition, working memory, and organized attention improve in middle
childhood and support academic success.

35. A child says, "I used to forget my assignments, so now I put them in the same folder every
day." This best illustrates:

   A. metamemory
   B. animism
   C. identity moratorium

 D. tertiary circular reactions
       Answer: A. metamemory
   Rationale: Metamemory is knowledge about one's own memory processes and strategies for
improving recall.

36. A school-age child who believes that effort leads to improvement in schoolwork is showing:
   A. learned helplessness
   B. self-efficacy
   C. identity diffusion

 D. role confusion
       Answer: B. self-efficacy
   Rationale: Self-efficacy is the belief that one can succeed through effort and effective action.

37. According to Erikson, a major developmental task of middle childhood is resolving:
   A. initiative versus guilt
   B. identity versus role confusion
   C. industry versus inferiority

 D. intimacy versus isolation
       Answer: C. industry versus inferiority
   Rationale: School-age children develop competence through achievement and comparison
with peers, making industry versus inferiority central.

38. Which child is most likely to be sociometrically popular?
   A. One who is consistently disruptive and domineering
   B. One who is cooperative, helpful, and socially skilled
   C. One who refuses all group activities

 D. One who threatens peers to gain status
       Answer: B. One who is cooperative, helpful, and socially skilled
   Rationale: Popular children are generally prosocial, emotionally regulated, and effective in
peer interactions.

39. Bullying differs from ordinary conflict because bullying typically involves:
   A. equal power between children
   B. playful teasing only
   C. repeated aggression and power imbalance

 D. immediate reconciliation
       Answer: C. repeated aggression and power imbalance
   Rationale: Bullying involves repetition and unequal power, distinguishing it from ordinary peer
disagreements.

40. Resilience in middle childhood is best defined as:
   A. absence of stress
   B. capacity to adapt positively despite adversity
   C. superior intelligence alone

 D. refusal to depend on others
       Answer: B. capacity to adapt positively despite adversity
   Rationale: Resilience refers to successful adaptation in the face of risk or challenge.

41. Which event marks the beginning of adolescence most directly from a biological standpoint?
   A. Entry into college
   B. Menopause
   C. Puberty

 D. Retirement
       Answer: C. Puberty
   Rationale: Puberty marks the biological transition into adolescence through sexual maturation
and hormonal change.

42. Which statement about the adolescent brain is most accurate?
   A. Brain development is fully complete by age 10.
   B. Emotional and reward systems may mature faster than impulse control systems.
   C. Adolescents cannot think abstractly.

 D. The prefrontal cortex develops before limbic sensitivity increases.
       Answer: B. Emotional and reward systems may mature faster than impulse control
systems.
   Rationale: This imbalance helps explain adolescent risk taking and strong emotional
reactivity.

43. An adolescent who believes "everyone is watching me" is showing:
   A. object permanence
   B. imaginary audience
   C. conservation

 D. social referencing
       Answer: B. imaginary audience
   Rationale: The imaginary audience is the adolescent belief that others are constantly
observing and evaluating them.

44. Piaget associated adolescence with the emergence of:
   A. sensorimotor intelligence
   B. concrete operations only
   C. formal operational thought

 D. preconceptual reasoning
       Answer: C. formal operational thought
   Rationale: Formal operations involve abstract, hypothetical, and systematic reasoning
associated with adolescence.

45. Kohlberg's conventional level of moral reasoning is characterized by:
   A. obedience solely to avoid punishment
   B. judgments based on social approval and maintaining order
   C. reliance on abstract universal principles only

 D. complete rejection of rules
       Answer: B. judgments based on social approval and maintaining order
   Rationale: Conventional morality emphasizes conforming to expectations and maintaining
social rules.

46. An adolescent chooses not to cheat because doing so would betray a personal principle of
fairness even if no one would know. This best reflects:

   A. preconventional reasoning
   B. conventional reasoning
   C. postconventional reasoning

 D. amoral behavior
       Answer: C. postconventional reasoning
   Rationale: Postconventional reasoning relies on internalized principles that may transcend
immediate external consequences.

47. Marcia's concept of identity moratorium refers to:
   A. commitment without exploration
   B. lack of crisis and lack of commitment
   C. active exploration without firm commitment

 D. firm commitment after no questioning
       Answer: C. active exploration without firm commitment
   Rationale: Moratorium is the status in which the adolescent is exploring alternatives but has
not yet committed.
48. Which factor is most protective against adolescent delinquency?
   A. Persistent peer rejection plus weak monitoring
   B. Strong parental monitoring and prosocial peer ties
   C. Easy access to drugs

 D. Chronic school disengagement
       Answer: B. Strong parental monitoring and prosocial peer ties
   Rationale: Protective factors against delinquency include supportive supervision, school
engagement, and association with prosocial peers.

49. Which statement about adolescent-parent relationships is most accurate?
   A. Normal adolescence always involves severe rebellion.
   B. Conflict usually reflects complete detachment from family.
   C. Most adolescents remain attached to parents even while seeking autonomy.

 D. Parent influence disappears once peers become important.
       Answer: C. Most adolescents remain attached to parents even while seeking autonomy.
   Rationale: Adolescence usually involves renegotiation of relationships rather than complete
rupture from parents.

50. A teenager engages in unprotected sex because she believes "it won't happen to me." This
best illustrates:

   A. hypothetical reasoning
   B. invulnerability fable
   C. deferred imitation

 D. secure attachment
       Answer: B. invulnerability fable
   Rationale: The invulnerability fable is the belief that one is uniquely protected from harm,
which can promote risky behavior.

51. Emerging adulthood is best characterized as a period of:
   A. complete dependence with no identity exploration
   B. identity exploration and instability in roles and relationships
   C. universal marriage and parenthood

 D. decline in cognitive flexibility
       Answer: B. identity exploration and instability in roles and relationships
   Rationale: Emerging adulthood commonly includes exploration in love, work, worldview, and
lifestyle.

52. Sternberg's triarchic view of adult intelligence emphasizes:
   A. only verbal IQ
   B. only fluid reasoning
   C. analytical, creative, and practical abilities

 D. only innate aptitude
       Answer: C. analytical, creative, and practical abilities
   Rationale: Sternberg's triarchic view includes analytical, creative, and practical intelligence.

53. Emotional intelligence refers primarily to the ability to:
   A. memorize emotional terms
   B. understand and regulate emotions effectively
   C. avoid all negative feelings

 D. suppress empathy entirely
       Answer: B. understand and regulate emotions effectively
   Rationale: Emotional intelligence involves perceiving, understanding, and managing emotions
in oneself and others.

54. A young adult who can evaluate evidence from multiple perspectives and tolerate ambiguity
is demonstrating:

   A. postformal or mature adult thinking
   B. sensorimotor reasoning
   C. animistic thought

 D. egocentrism
       Answer: A. postformal or mature adult thinking
   Rationale: Mature adult thought often involves relativism, practicality, and tolerance for
ambiguity.

55. Which issue is a major psychosocial task in emerging and young adulthood according to
Erikson?

   A. Industry versus inferiority
   B. Intimacy versus isolation
   C. Ego integrity versus despair

 D. Trust versus mistrust
       Answer: B. Intimacy versus isolation
   Rationale: Young adulthood centers on forming close, committed relationships without losing
identity.

56. Which statement about marriage and cohabitation in young adulthood is most accurate?
   A. All cohabiting relationships are unstable.
   B. Relationship quality depends only on legal status.
   C. Developmental outcomes vary with commitment, communication, and context.

 D. Marriage eliminates all conflict.
       Answer: C. Developmental outcomes vary with commitment, communication, and context.
   Rationale: Relationship quality depends on multiple contextual and interpersonal variables
rather than legal status alone.

57. Parenthood often requires:
   A. no role adjustment
   B. immediate decline in all well-being
   C. negotiation of responsibilities and adaptation to new demands
 D. abandonment of adult identity
       Answer: C. negotiation of responsibilities and adaptation to new demands
   Rationale: Parenthood changes roles, time use, finances, and relationship patterns, requiring
adaptation.

58. Fluid intelligence generally refers to:
   A. accumulated knowledge and verbal skill
   B. speed and flexible reasoning in novel situations
   C. autobiographical memory only

 D. emotional attachment
       Answer: B. speed and flexible reasoning in novel situations
   Rationale: Fluid intelligence supports problem solving in unfamiliar situations without relying
mainly on prior learning.

59. Crystallized intelligence generally refers to:
   A. culturally acquired knowledge and expertise
   B. rapid sensory processing
   C. reflexive action

 D. hormonal regulation
       Answer: A. culturally acquired knowledge and expertise
   Rationale: Crystallized intelligence reflects accumulated knowledge, vocabulary, and learned
skills.

60. Which statement best reflects a contemporary view of midlife?
   A. Midlife is universally a time of crisis.
   B. Midlife is purely biological and unaffected by culture.
   C. Midlife experiences vary widely depending on context and personal meaning.

 D. Personality stops changing completely at age 40.
       Answer: C. Midlife experiences vary widely depending on context and personal meaning.
   Rationale: Contemporary developmental psychology rejects the idea that midlife follows one
uniform pattern for everyone.

61. A 48-year-old worker solves job-related problems efficiently by drawing on years of
experience. This best illustrates:

   A. tertiary circular reactions
   B. expertise
   C. imaginary audience

 D. basic trust
       Answer: B. expertise
   Rationale: Expertise reflects highly practiced, domain-specific skill and efficient problem
solving based on experience.

62. Erikson associated middle adulthood most strongly with:
   A. identity versus role confusion
   B. generativity versus stagnation
   C. autonomy versus shame and doubt

 D. trust versus mistrust
       Answer: B. generativity versus stagnation
   Rationale: Middle adulthood emphasizes contributing to society and guiding the next
generation rather than becoming self-absorbed.

63. Which person best exemplifies generativity?
   A. A middle-aged adult mentoring younger colleagues and investing in the next generation
   B. An adolescent resisting parental curfew
   C. A toddler insisting on independence

 D. An older adult conducting life review
       Answer: A. A middle-aged adult mentoring younger colleagues and investing in the next
generation
   Rationale: Generativity is expressed through care, mentorship, productivity, and concern for
the future of others.

64. The "empty nest" transition is best understood as:
   A. uniformly harmful to all parents
   B. often shaped by marital quality, cultural expectations, and parental identity
   C. always followed by depression

 D. unrelated to development
       Answer: B. often shaped by marital quality, cultural expectations, and parental identity
   Rationale: The empty nest can be experienced as loss, relief, growth, or mixed feelings
depending on broader context.

65. Midlife well-being is generally most strongly associated with:
   A. perfection in every role
   B. supportive relationships, health, purpose, and adaptive coping
   C. complete absence of work demands

 D. denial of aging
       Answer: B. supportive relationships, health, purpose, and adaptive coping
   Rationale: Midlife well-being is multidimensional and supported by social, physical, and
psychological resources.

66. Which statement about aging is most accurate?
   A. All older adults experience dementia.
   B. Aging involves both losses and strengths, with wide individual variability.
   C. Cognitive decline is uniform across all abilities.

 D. Personality becomes impossible to study in late adulthood.
       Answer: B. Aging involves both losses and strengths, with wide individual variability.
