   Rationale: Late adulthood includes heterogeneity; some capacities decline while others
remain stable or improve.
67. Which concept refers to the increasing proportion of older adults in the population?
   A. Pubertal timing
   B. Mortality revolution
   C. Graying of the population

 D. Sequential trend
       Answer: C. Graying of the population
   Rationale: This phrase refers to the growing proportion of older adults in the population.

68. Which cognitive ability tends to remain relatively more stable in late adulthood compared
with processing speed?

   A. Speeded perceptual comparison
   B. Working memory span
   C. Crystallized knowledge

 D. Reaction time
       Answer: C. Crystallized knowledge
   Rationale: Accumulated knowledge often remains comparatively stable in late adulthood even
as processing speed slows.

69. Wisdom in late adulthood is best described as:
   A. memorizing facts more quickly than young adults
   B. expert knowledge in the pragmatics of life
   C. complete emotional detachment

 D. absence of mistakes
       Answer: B. expert knowledge in the pragmatics of life
   Rationale: Wisdom involves sound judgment about life matters, uncertainty, values, and
human affairs.

70. Selective optimization with compensation refers to:
   A. random activity in old age
   B. a strategy of focusing on priorities, maximizing strengths, and offsetting losses
   C. refusing help from others

 D. withdrawing from all roles
       Answer: B. a strategy of focusing on priorities, maximizing strengths, and offsetting losses
   Rationale: Selective optimization with compensation describes adaptive self-regulation in
aging.

71. Erikson's final psychosocial crisis is:
   A. integrity versus despair
   B. intimacy versus isolation
   C. autonomy versus shame

 D. initiative versus guilt
       Answer: A. integrity versus despair
   Rationale: Erikson proposed that late adulthood centers on evaluating one's life with
acceptance versus regret.
72. Which factor is most consistently associated with better adjustment in late adulthood?
   A. Social isolation
   B. Meaningful social support
   C. Rigid avoidance of change

 D. Total dependence in all tasks
       Answer: B. Meaningful social support
   Rationale: Supportive relationships buffer stress, reduce loneliness, and promote adjustment
in later life.

73. Widowhood adjustment in late adulthood is influenced most by:
   A. only chronological age
   B. only income
   C. prior relationship quality, health, support, and coping resources

 D. complete absence of grief
       Answer: C. prior relationship quality, health, support, and coping resources
   Rationale: Adjustment to widowhood is shaped by multiple personal and contextual factors,
not by age alone.

74. Which statement about retirement is most accurate?
   A. Retirement affects all adults in the same way.
   B. Retirement adjustment depends on finances, health, identity, and social roles.
   C. Retirement always worsens mental health.

 D. Retirement eliminates developmental tasks.
       Answer: B. Retirement adjustment depends on finances, health, identity, and social roles.
   Rationale: Retirement is a developmental transition whose impact varies depending on
resources, meaning, and planning.

75. In Kübler-Ross's framework, the five reactions to dying are best understood as:
   A. fixed stages everyone experiences in order
   B. possible reactions that vary across individuals
   C. evidence of psychopathology

 D. traits of old age only
       Answer: B. possible reactions that vary across individuals
   Rationale: Contemporary understanding treats Kübler-Ross's reactions as possible
responses, not rigid universal stages.

76. Bereavement refers to:
   A. only the funeral ritual
   B. the state of loss after death of a significant person
   C. denial of mortality

 D. assisted suicide
       Answer: B. the state of loss after death of a significant person
   Rationale: Bereavement refers to the objective condition of having lost someone significant
through death.

77. Which loss is often especially associated with prolonged disruption of identity and daily
routine in late life?

   A. Losing a pencil
   B. Failing a classroom quiz
   C. Death of a long-term spouse

 D. Missing one work meeting
       Answer: C. Death of a long-term spouse
   Rationale: Loss of a spouse often disrupts identity, companionship, routines, and emotional
security, especially in later life.

78. Which statement best reflects contemporary understanding of grief?
   A. Healthy grief follows one universal timetable.
   B. Grief is always brief if the person is resilient.
   C. Grief varies in pattern, intensity, and duration across persons and cultures.

 D. Children do not grieve meaningfully.
       Answer: C. Grief varies in pattern, intensity, and duration across persons and cultures.
   Rationale: Current perspectives emphasize variability in grieving rather than one universal
pathway.

79. A patient signs a document specifying preferred medical treatment should decisional
capacity be lost. This is a:

   A. mnemonic
   B. life review
   C. advance directive

 D. sociometric rating
       Answer: C. advance directive
   Rationale: An advance directive records treatment wishes in case the person later loses
decisional capacity.

80. Which statement best reflects the developmental meaning of life review in later life?
   A. It is merely nostalgia with no adaptive value.
   B. It can help integrate experiences and support a sense of meaning.
   C. It is identical to denial.

 D. It occurs only in dementia.
       Answer: B. It can help integrate experiences and support a sense of meaning.
   Rationale: Life review can promote coherence, acceptance, and ego integrity in later life.

81. Under RA 10029 and the PAP Code, which statement is most accurate?
   A. Anyone with psychology units may independently practice as a psychologist.
   B. Only licensed and registered psychologists and psychometricians may legally practice

within the bounds prescribed by law.
   C. A psychometrician may practice psychotherapy independently as a routine service.

 D. Licensure is optional if one has many years of experience.
       Answer: B. Only licensed and registered psychologists and psychometricians may legally
practice within the bounds prescribed by law.
   Rationale: RA 10029 and the PAP Code require that only licensed and registered
psychologists and psychometricians practice legally, and only within the limits of their
professional scope.

82. A psychometrician is asked to provide therapy to a client with depression in a private clinic.
The most ethical response is to:

   A. accept because test users are automatically therapists
   B. provide therapy if the client insists
   C. decline and refer appropriately, because psychometricians are prohibited from routine
therapy practice

 D. proceed without documentation
       Answer: C. decline and refer appropriately, because psychometricians are prohibited from
routine therapy practice
   Rationale: A psychometrician's ethical and legal role does not include routine independent
psychotherapy, so declining and referring appropriately protects the client and respects scope of
practice.

83. A practitioner is asked to assess a client using an instrument that has no validity, no
reliability evidence, and no appropriate norms for the client's population. The best action is to:

   A. use it anyway if it is popular online
   B. use it if the client is curious
   C. avoid using it and select a more appropriate assessment tool

 D. photocopy it first to improve standardization
       Answer: C. avoid using it and select a more appropriate assessment tool
   Rationale: Ethical assessment requires valid, reliable, and appropriate tools so that
conclusions are accurate, fair, and professionally defensible.

84. Which action best protects test security?
   A. Posting test items on social media for discussion
   B. Allowing unqualified staff to keep protocols at home
   C. Restricting access to qualified personnel and securing materials

 D. Giving raw test data to anyone who requests it
       Answer: C. Restricting access to qualified personnel and securing materials
   Rationale: Test security is protected when materials are stored safely and access is limited to
properly qualified persons.

85. A psychologist is consulted by a school about a child referred by parents. Which release of
results is most ethical?

   A. Give complete raw data to all teachers immediately
   B. Release results only to agreed referral sources and explain findings in understandable
language

   C. Announce results during a faculty meeting

 D. Post the report in the classroom file for open access
       Answer: B. Release results only to agreed referral sources and explain findings in
understandable language
   Rationale: Ethical release of results requires limiting disclosure to proper recipients and
communicating findings clearly and appropriately.

86. Which statement about confidentiality is most accurate under the PAP Code?
   A. Confidentiality has no limits once a person becomes a client.
   B. Confidential information may be disclosed only when mandated or permitted by law, or to

prevent harm, and only to the extent necessary.
   C. Any family member may automatically access records.

 D. Confidentiality applies only to written notes, not digital files.
       Answer: B. Confidential information may be disclosed only when mandated or permitted
by law, or to prevent harm, and only to the extent necessary.
   Rationale: Confidentiality is a core ethical duty, but disclosure may occur in legally or ethically
justified situations and only in the minimum amount necessary.

87. Before conducting assessment or intervention through telepsychology, the practitioner
should:

   A. assume online practice has no special risks
   B. avoid discussing privacy because it may worry the client
   C. explain risks to privacy, limits of confidentiality, and technology-related concerns

 D. allow anyone nearby to observe the session
       Answer: C. explain risks to privacy, limits of confidentiality, and technology-related
concerns
   Rationale: Telepsychology requires informed discussion of privacy risks, confidentiality limits,
and technology-related issues before services begin.

88. A practitioner realizes that a personal problem is significantly interfering with competent
service delivery. The most ethical course is to:

   A. ignore it to maintain reputation
   B. continue because clients should adapt
   C. seek consultation or assistance and limit, suspend, or terminate duties as needed

 D. disclose all personal details to every client
       Answer: C. seek consultation or assistance and limit, suspend, or terminate duties as
needed
   Rationale: Ethical practice requires practitioners to protect clients by addressing personal
problems that impair competence and by adjusting professional duties when needed.

89. A psychology practitioner agrees to serve a client referred by a corporation. At the outset,
the practitioner should clarify:
   A. only the fee schedule
   B. who the client is, the role of the practitioner, probable uses of information, and limits of
confidentiality
   C. nothing, to preserve spontaneity

 D. only the practitioner's opinion about management
       Answer: B. who the client is, the role of the practitioner, probable uses of information, and
limits of confidentiality
   Rationale: Third-party service arrangements require early clarification of roles, client identity,
expected use of information, and confidentiality boundaries.

90. A practitioner discovers that a colleague may have committed an ethical violation. Which
response is most consistent with the Code?

   A. Publicly shame the colleague online
   B. Ignore the issue regardless of potential harm
   C. Consider informal resolution first when appropriate and confidentiality is not violated;
report further when substantial harm is likely

 D. File a complaint without evidence
       Answer: C. Consider informal resolution first when appropriate and confidentiality is not
violated; report further when substantial harm is likely
   Rationale: The Code supports addressing possible violations responsibly, beginning with
informal resolution when appropriate and escalating when serious harm may result.

91. Entering a business partnership with a current therapy client would most likely be
problematic because it creates:

   A. normative influence
   B. multiple relationship and conflict of interest concerns
   C. formal operational thought

 D. secure attachment
       Answer: B. multiple relationship and conflict of interest concerns
   Rationale: A business partnership with a current client can impair objectivity, blur boundaries,
and increase the risk of exploitation.

92. Which practice best reflects informed consent?
   A. Using technical jargon so clients appreciate expertise
   B. Providing reasonably understandable information about nature, risks, fees, third-party

involvement, and limits of confidentiality
   C. Obtaining consent only after the intervention is completed

 D. Skipping assent from minors when possible
       Answer: B. Providing reasonably understandable information about nature, risks, fees,
third-party involvement, and limits of confidentiality
   Rationale: Informed consent is valid only when clients receive understandable, relevant
information before services begin.
93. A client requests that a teleassessment feedback session be recorded. The most ethical
response is to:

   A. secretly record without discussion
   B. refuse all recordings in every case
   C. address the request transparently within proper consent, confidentiality, and
documentation procedures

 D. send raw data instead of feedback
       Answer: C. address the request transparently within proper consent, confidentiality, and
documentation procedures
   Rationale: Recording requests should be managed openly and ethically through proper
consent, privacy safeguards, and documentation.

94. A psychology intern is assigned tasks beyond current competence and without supervision.
The supervisor should:

   A. allow independence to build confidence
   B. assign only responsibilities the intern can perform competently with appropriate
supervision
   C. avoid documenting delegation

 D. let the intern interpret all tests independently
       Answer: B. assign only responsibilities the intern can perform competently with
appropriate supervision
   Rationale: Ethical delegation requires matching duties to the intern's training and ensuring
adequate supervision to protect clients and support learning.

95. A psychologist is required by law to provide emergency assistance in a setting where full
services are unavailable. The Code allows the psychologist to:

   A. provide no help at all unless ideal conditions exist
   B. provide limited emergency services cautiously, then discontinue once emergency ends and
arrange appropriate services
   C. begin permanent therapy regardless of competence

 D. ignore referral needs afterward
       Answer: B. provide limited emergency services cautiously, then discontinue once
emergency ends and arrange appropriate services
   Rationale: In emergencies, limited assistance may be ethically provided to prevent harm, but
it should end when the crisis ends and be followed by appropriate referral.

96. Which action best reflects integrity in professional statements?
   A. Exaggerating success rates to attract clients
   B. Stating credentials and services accurately without deceptive claims
   C. Advertising oneself as an expert in all areas of psychology

 D. Using unverifiable testimonials as proof of scientific validity
       Answer: B. Stating credentials and services accurately without deceptive claims
   Rationale: Integrity in professional communication requires honesty and accuracy about
credentials, competence, and services.
97. A psychometrician may administer psychological tests:
   A. entirely outside the boundaries of RA 10029 if supervised informally by a friend
   B. within the legal scope of practice and, when applicable, under supervision of a registered

psychologist
   C. only if no psychologist exists in the region, with no limits

 D. only after giving therapy first
       Answer: B. within the legal scope of practice and, when applicable, under supervision of a
registered psychologist
   Rationale: A psychometrician may administer tests only within the legal scope of practice and
subject to proper supervisory and ethical requirements when applicable.

98. In explaining assessment results to parents of a minor, the practitioner should primarily:
   A. use highly technical language to maintain authority
   B. reveal all test items to prove transparency
   C. communicate findings in clear, nontechnical language while preserving confidentiality

 D. allow untrained relatives to interpret the report
       Answer: C. communicate findings in clear, nontechnical language while preserving
confidentiality
   Rationale: Ethical feedback requires understandable communication while still protecting
confidential and professionally sensitive information.

99. Which scenario best illustrates an ethical breach involving confidentiality?
   A. Discussing de-identified case material in supervision for professional purposes
   B. Sharing a client's identifiable history in a public seminar without written consent or

adequate disguise
   C. Documenting informed consent in the record

 D. Explaining limits of confidentiality before assessment
       Answer: B. Sharing a client's identifiable history in a public seminar without written
consent or adequate disguise
   Rationale: Public disclosure of identifiable client information without proper consent or
adequate protection violates confidentiality.

100. Which ethical principle is most directly upheld when a practitioner declines work outside
current competence and makes an appropriate referral?

    A. Competent caring and nonmaleficence
    B. Mere professional convenience
    C. Social desirability

 D. Absolute autonomy without responsibility
        Answer: A. Competent caring and nonmaleficence
    Rationale: Refusing work beyond one's competence and making an appropriate referral
protects clients from harm and reflects ethical responsibility for competent care.
DEVELOPMENTAL PSYCHOLOGY
EXAM 9
DEVELOPMENTAL PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 9

1. A researcher examines how individuals adjust their goals after experiencing major life
setbacks. This best reflects which characteristic of development?

  A. Universality
  B. Plasticity
  C. Irreversibility

 D. Determinism
       Answer: B. Plasticity
  Rationale: Plasticity refers to the capacity for change and adaptation in response to life
experiences and challenges.

2. Which concept emphasizes that development results from ongoing, bidirectional interactions
between biology and environment?

  A. Epigenesis
  B. Reflex integration
  C. Canalization

 D. Maturation
       Answer: A. Epigenesis
  Rationale: Epigenesis highlights the continuous interaction between genetic and
environmental influences shaping development.

3. A developmental psychologist studies how economic recession influences career decisions of
young adults. This is best classified as:

  A. Normative age-graded influence
  B. Normative history-graded influence
  C. Non-normative influence

 D. Biological influence
       Answer: B. Normative history-graded influence
  Rationale: Historical events affecting large groups at a specific time are normative
history-graded influences.

4. A major limitation of longitudinal research is:
  A. inability to study change over time
  B. susceptibility to cohort effects
  C. participant attrition and practice effects

 D. lack of ecological validity
       Answer: C. participant attrition and practice effects
  Rationale: Longitudinal studies often face participant dropout and repeated testing effects over
time.

5. When a child learns that birds have wings and later includes bats in the same category, this
reflects:

  A. accommodation
  B. assimilation
  C. equilibration

 D. centration
       Answer: B. assimilation
  Rationale: Assimilation involves incorporating new information into existing cognitive
schemas.

6. A theorist who explains behavior primarily through unconscious motivations and early
childhood conflicts aligns with:

  A. Cognitive theory
  B. Psychoanalytic theory
  C. Sociocultural theory

 D. Ecological theory
       Answer: B. Psychoanalytic theory
  Rationale: Psychoanalytic theory emphasizes unconscious processes and early experiences.

7. Which prenatal factor most strongly contributes to neural tube defects?
  A. Excess iron
  B. Lack of folic acid
  C. High protein intake

 D. Low glucose levels
       Answer: B. Lack of folic acid
  Rationale: Folic acid deficiency is strongly associated with neural tube defects.

8. A pregnant woman experiences chronic stress, leading to elevated cortisol levels. This may
most directly affect the fetus by:

  A. enhancing neural pruning
  B. altering brain development
  C. improving immune functioning

 D. increasing birth weight
       Answer: B. altering brain development
  Rationale: Elevated maternal stress hormones can disrupt fetal brain development.

9. A newborn turns its head toward a touch on the cheek. This reflex is:
  A. Moro reflex
  B. Babinski reflex
  C. rooting reflex

 D. sucking reflex
       Answer: C. rooting reflex
  Rationale: The rooting reflex helps infants locate food by turning toward cheek stimulation.

10. Which condition is characterized by failure to thrive due to severe emotional neglect?
   A. Teratogenic syndrome
   B. Nonorganic failure to thrive
   C. Sudden infant death syndrome

 D. Neonatal jaundice
       Answer: B. Nonorganic failure to thrive
   Rationale: Emotional deprivation can lead to growth failure without medical cause.

11. An infant repeatedly drops a spoon from a high chair to watch it fall. This behavior reflects:
   A. tertiary circular reactions
   B. primary circular reactions
   C. reflexive schemes

 D. symbolic play
       Answer: A. tertiary circular reactions
   Rationale: Tertiary circular reactions involve experimenting with actions to observe new
outcomes.

12. The realization that objects continue to exist even when not perceived emerges toward the
end of:

   A. preoperational stage
   B. sensorimotor stage
   C. concrete operational stage

 D. formal operational stage
       Answer: B. sensorimotor stage
   Rationale: Object permanence develops during the sensorimotor stage.

13. A toddler who uses two-word combinations like "want milk" is demonstrating:
   A. holophrastic speech
   B. telegraphic speech
   C. babbling

 D. echolalia
       Answer: B. telegraphic speech
   Rationale: Telegraphic speech consists of short, meaningful word combinations.

14. According to information-processing theory, improvement in children's thinking is largely due
to:

   A. stage transitions
   B. increased processing efficiency
   C. moral reasoning

 D. unconscious drives
       Answer: B. increased processing efficiency
   Rationale: Cognitive development is explained by improvements in attention, memory, and
speed.

15. A caregiver consistently responds to an infant's needs in a timely and sensitive manner. This
most likely promotes:

   A. avoidant attachment
   B. disorganized attachment
   C. secure attachment

 D. resistant attachment
       Answer: C. secure attachment
   Rationale: Consistent and responsive caregiving fosters secure attachment.

16. A child insists that a toy animal is alive because it moves. This reflects:
   A. conservation
   B. animistic thinking
   C. reversibility

 D. seriation
       Answer: B. animistic thinking
   Rationale: Animism involves attributing life to inanimate objects.

17. When children focus on one aspect of a situation and ignore others, they demonstrate:
   A. decentration
   B. centration
   C. classification

 D. transitivity
       Answer: B. centration
   Rationale: Centration is focusing on a single dimension of a situation.

18. A teacher helps a child solve a puzzle by giving hints and gradually reducing assistance.
This is an example of:

   A. conditioning
   B. scaffolding
   C. reinforcement

 D. extinction
       Answer: B. scaffolding
   Rationale: Scaffolding involves guided support that is gradually withdrawn.

19. A child begins to understand that gender remains the same despite changes in appearance.
This is:

   A. gender identity
   B. gender constancy
   C. gender typing

 D. gender schema
       Answer: B. gender constancy
   Rationale: Gender constancy is the understanding that gender is stable over time.

20. A parenting style characterized by high warmth and low control is:
   A. authoritarian
   B. authoritative
   C. permissive
 D. neglectful
       Answer: C. permissive
   Rationale: Permissive parenting is warm but lacks firm control or discipline.

21. A child becomes upset when excluded from a group activity. This reflects development in:
   A. motor skills
   B. emotional regulation
   C. peer relations

 D. sensory processing
       Answer: C. peer relations
   Rationale: Social exclusion directly involves peer interaction and reflects development in
social relationships.

22. Which cognitive ability improves significantly during middle childhood?
   A. Reflexive behavior
   B. Hypothetical reasoning
   C. Logical operations on concrete objects

 D. Magical thinking
       Answer: C. Logical operations on concrete objects
   Rationale: Middle childhood is characterized by concrete operational thinking involving logical
reasoning about tangible objects.

23. A child who understands that 5 + 3 = 8 and 8 - 3 = 5 demonstrates:
   A. centration
   B. reversibility
   C. conservation

 D. seriation
       Answer: B. reversibility
   Rationale: Reversibility is the ability to mentally reverse operations, a key feature of concrete
operational thought.

24. Which factor most strongly predicts academic success in middle childhood?
   A. Birth order
   B. Parental income alone
   C. Self-regulation and motivation

 D. Physical strength
       Answer: C. Self-regulation and motivation
   Rationale: Self-regulation and motivation are strong predictors of academic achievement.

25. A child who is rejected by peers is most likely to exhibit:
   A. high social competence
   B. increased prosocial behavior
   C. aggression or withdrawal
   D. advanced moral reasoning
  Answer: C. aggression or withdrawal

   Rationale: Peer rejection is often associated with maladaptive behaviors such as aggression
or withdrawal.

26. Adolescents' tendency to believe their experiences are unique is called:
   A. personal fable
   B. imaginary audience
   C. identity diffusion

 D. moral relativism
       Answer: A. personal fable
   Rationale: Personal fable refers to the belief in one's uniqueness and invulnerability.

27. The onset of puberty is triggered primarily by:
   A. environmental stressors
   B. activation of the hypothalamic-pituitary axis
   C. peer influence

 D. cognitive development
       Answer: B. activation of the hypothalamic-pituitary axis
   Rationale: Hormonal activation of this axis initiates puberty.

28. Adolescents who can think about abstract ideals such as justice are demonstrating:
   A. concrete operations
   B. preoperational thinking
   C. formal operational thinking

 D. sensorimotor reasoning
       Answer: C. formal operational thinking
   Rationale: Formal operations enable abstract and hypothetical reasoning.

29. A teenager who adopts parents' beliefs without exploration is in identity:
   A. achievement
   B. moratorium
   C. foreclosure

 D. diffusion
       Answer: C. foreclosure
   Rationale: Foreclosure involves commitment without prior exploration.

30. Which factor most increases risk for adolescent substance use?
   A. Strong parental monitoring
   B. Academic engagement
   C. Association with deviant peers

 D. High self-esteem
       Answer: C. Association with deviant peers
   Rationale: Peer influence is a major risk factor for substance use.
31. Emerging adulthood is often characterized by:
   A. stability and commitment
   B. exploration and instability
   C. complete independence

 D. fixed identity
       Answer: B. exploration and instability
   Rationale: This period involves identity exploration and instability in roles.

32. Which factor contributes most to successful romantic relationships in early adulthood?
   A. Physical attractiveness alone
   B. Emotional communication
   C. Financial status only

 D. Cultural norms exclusively
       Answer: B. Emotional communication
   Rationale: Effective communication is key to relationship satisfaction.

33. Cognitive development in adulthood often involves:
   A. decline in all abilities
   B. increase in speed only
   C. integration of experience and logic

 D. elimination of emotion
       Answer: C. integration of experience and logic
   Rationale: Adult cognition integrates practical experience with logical reasoning.

34. Which type of intelligence is most likely to decline with age?
   A. Crystallized
   B. Fluid
   C. Practical

 D. Emotional
       Answer: B. Fluid
   Rationale: Fluid intelligence declines earlier than crystallized intelligence.

35. A midlife adult mentoring younger colleagues demonstrates:
   A. stagnation
   B. disengagement
   C. generativity

 D. identity diffusion
       Answer: C. generativity
   Rationale: Generativity involves contributing to the next generation.

36. Which factor best predicts life satisfaction in middle adulthood?
   A. Physical strength
   B. Number of possessions
   C. Quality of relationships
 D. Educational attainment only
       Answer: C. Quality of relationships
   Rationale: Strong interpersonal relationships are key to well-being.

37. Age-related loss of hearing is called:
   A. presbyopia
   B. presbycusis
   C. cataract

 D. glaucoma
       Answer: B. presbycusis
   Rationale: Presbycusis refers to age-related hearing loss.

38. Which theory suggests aging is programmed into genetic codes?
   A. Wear-and-tear theory
   B. Programmed aging theory
   C. Activity theory

 D. Disengagement theory
       Answer: B. Programmed aging theory
   Rationale: This theory proposes that aging follows a biological timetable.

39. Older adults often compensate for memory decline by:
   A. avoiding tasks
   B. using external aids
   C. ignoring errors

 D. reducing interaction
       Answer: B. using external aids
   Rationale: External aids help compensate for memory limitations.

40. Which factor contributes most to successful aging?
   A. Isolation
   B. Passive lifestyle
   C. Active engagement

 D. Avoidance of change
       Answer: C. Active engagement
   Rationale: Continued engagement supports well-being in old age.

41. A person reviewing life positively despite regrets is experiencing:
   A. despair
   B. stagnation
   C. ego integrity

 D. diffusion
       Answer: C. ego integrity
   Rationale: Ego integrity reflects acceptance of one's life.
42. Grief that persists intensely over a long period may be classified as:
   A. normative grief
   B. anticipatory grief
   C. complicated grief

 D. acute grief
       Answer: C. complicated grief
   Rationale: Complicated grief involves prolonged and intense distress.

43. Which coping strategy is most adaptive after loss?
   A. Denial indefinitely
   B. Avoidance
   C. Meaning-making

 D. Suppression
       Answer: C. Meaning-making
   Rationale: Finding meaning supports emotional recovery.

44. A psychometrician is asked to independently diagnose a psychiatric disorder. The correct
action is to:

   A. proceed with diagnosis
   B. consult a psychologist and limit role
   C. ignore request

 D. refer only after assessment
       Answer: B. consult a psychologist and limit role
   Rationale: Diagnosis is beyond the independent scope of a psychometrician.

45. Administering a test without proper training violates:
   A. beneficence
   B. competence
   C. confidentiality

 D. autonomy
       Answer: B. competence
   Rationale: Ethical standards require proper training and qualification.

46. Sharing test items publicly compromises:
   A. validity
   B. reliability
   C. test security

 D. standardization
       Answer: C. test security
   Rationale: Public exposure of items compromises test integrity.

47. Informed consent requires:
   A. full disclosure of procedures and risks
   B. only verbal agreement
   C. no explanation

 D. assumption of understanding
       Answer: A. full disclosure of procedures and risks
   Rationale: Informed consent requires clear and complete explanation.

48. A psychometrician must refuse tasks that:
   A. are routine
   B. exceed competence
   C. involve paperwork

 D. require supervision
       Answer: B. exceed competence
   Rationale: Professionals must not perform tasks beyond their expertise.

49. Keeping client records secure primarily supports:
   A. efficiency
   B. confidentiality
   C. convenience

 D. accessibility
       Answer: B. confidentiality
   Rationale: Secure records protect client privacy.

50. A practitioner must clarify limits of confidentiality especially when:
   A. working alone
   B. conducting research
   C. dealing with third-party requests

 D. working with adults only
       Answer: C. dealing with third-party requests
   Rationale: Third-party involvement requires clear boundaries of confidentiality.

51. An adolescent who spends considerable time evaluating how others may judge appearance
and behavior is most clearly demonstrating:

   A. object permanence
   B. imaginary audience
   C. industry

 D. selective optimization
       Answer: B. imaginary audience
   Rationale: Imaginary audience reflects adolescents' heightened self-consciousness and belief
that others are constantly observing them.

52. A young person delays marriage and parenthood in order to explore educational and
occupational options. This pattern is most characteristic of:

   A. late adulthood
   B. middle childhood
   C. emerging adulthood
 D. middle adulthood
       Answer: C. emerging adulthood
   Rationale: Emerging adulthood is defined by exploration and delayed role commitments.

53. Which situation best illustrates postformal thought?
   A. A student insists that one formula solves every interpersonal problem
   B. A worker recognizes that two conflicting viewpoints may both contain truth depending on

context
   C. A child sorts blocks by color only

 D. An adolescent rejects all ambiguity in moral dilemmas
       Answer: B. A worker recognizes that two conflicting viewpoints may both contain truth
depending on context
   Rationale: Postformal thought allows integration of multiple perspectives and acceptance of
contradictions.

54. A newly married couple experiences conflict because one partner expects all household
decisions to be shared while the other expects one person to lead. This is best understood as a
difference in:

   A. sensorimotor schemas
   B. marital scripts and role expectations
   C. reflex organization

 D. psychomotor speed
       Answer: B. marital scripts and role expectations
   Rationale: Conflict arises from differing internalized expectations about roles in relationships.

55. Which factor is most likely to strengthen identity development in emerging adulthood?
   A. Foreclosure without exploration
   B. Rigid dependence on parental choices
   C. Opportunities for exploration with realistic commitment

 D. Avoidance of major decisions indefinitely
       Answer: C. Opportunities for exploration with realistic commitment
   Rationale: Healthy identity formation requires both exploration and commitment.

56. A young adult selects a career based not only on salary but also on personal meaning and
long-term values. This best reflects:

   A. practical and reflective adult cognition
   B. centration
   C. delayed imitation

 D. circular reaction
       Answer: A. practical and reflective adult cognition
   Rationale: Adult cognition integrates experience, values, and logic in decision-making.

57. Which statement best describes the relationship between health behavior and development
in young adulthood?
   A. Health is determined almost entirely by heredity
   B. Lifestyle choices can significantly shape present and future functioning
   C. Young adults are largely unaffected by sleep, diet, and exercise habits

 D. Mental health is unrelated to physical health during this period
       Answer: B. Lifestyle choices can significantly shape present and future functioning
   Rationale: Health behaviors strongly influence long-term physical and psychological
outcomes.

58. An individual who is highly skilled at interpreting social situations, regulating emotional
responses, and responding appropriately is demonstrating:

   A. fluid intelligence only
   B. emotional intelligence
   C. psychomotor efficiency

 D. conservation ability
       Answer: B. emotional intelligence
   Rationale: Emotional intelligence involves understanding and managing emotions in oneself
and others.

59. In adult cognitive development, expertise is most likely to:
   A. eliminate all age-related decline
   B. compensate partly for slower processing in familiar domains
   C. replace memory demands entirely

 D. make practice unnecessary
       Answer: B. compensate partly for slower processing in familiar domains
   Rationale: Expertise helps maintain performance by relying on experience and efficient
strategies.

60. A couple who can discuss disagreements openly, negotiate responsibilities, and adjust to
changing demands are showing:

   A. role confusion
   B. high relationship competence
   C. disengagement

 D. identity diffusion
       Answer: B. high relationship competence
   Rationale: Effective communication and flexibility reflect strong relational functioning.

61. Which statement about middle adulthood is most accurate?
   A. All adults in midlife undergo a dramatic psychological crisis
   B. Midlife is shaped by individual, cultural, and contextual differences
   C. Personality change completely stops by age 40

 D. Family roles become developmentally unimportant by midlife
       Answer: B. Midlife is shaped by individual, cultural, and contextual differences
   Rationale: Midlife experiences vary widely depending on multiple personal and contextual
factors.
62. A 48-year-old adult returns to graduate school while also supporting aging parents and an
adolescent child. This scenario best illustrates:

   A. age segregation
   B. multidirectionality in development
   C. reflex integration

 D. preoperational thought
       Answer: B. multidirectionality in development
   Rationale: Development involves simultaneous gains and challenges across domains.

63. Which physical change is more typical of middle adulthood than of earlier adulthood?
   A. rapid gains in reaction time
   B. improved sensory acuity
   C. gradual decline in visual accommodation

 D. total loss of reproductive concerns in all adults
       Answer: C. gradual decline in visual accommodation
   Rationale: Middle adulthood involves gradual sensory decline such as reduced near vision.

64. A midlife adult who reexamines life priorities after the death of a close friend and decides to
focus more on meaningful relationships is showing:

   A. identity process and life review at midlife
   B. sensorimotor adaptation
   C. egocentric reasoning

 D. attachment disorganization
       Answer: A. identity process and life review at midlife
   Rationale: Midlife often involves reflection and reevaluation of goals and identity.

65. Which characteristic is most associated with generativity?
   A. Withdrawal from social contribution
   B. Concern for guiding and supporting the next generation
   C. Refusal to assume family or community roles

 D. Exclusive focus on personal gratification
       Answer: B. Concern for guiding and supporting the next generation
   Rationale: Generativity involves contributing to the well-being of future generations.

66. Which factor is most strongly linked to well-being in long-term midlife relationships?
   A. Constant idealization without conflict
   B. Marital quality rather than marital status alone
   C. Economic dependence only

 D. Absence of all role strain
       Answer: B. Marital quality rather than marital status alone
   Rationale: Relationship satisfaction predicts well-being more than marital status alone.
67. An adult child begins to view a parent as a vulnerable older person rather than solely as an
authority figure. This shift is most related to:

   A. filial maturity
   B. object constancy
   C. gender typing

 D. hypothetical-deductive reasoning
       Answer: A. filial maturity
   Rationale: Filial maturity involves recognizing parents as individuals with needs and
limitations.

68. Which statement best reflects continuity theory in late adulthood?
   A. Older adults function best when all previous roles are abandoned
   B. Aging is easiest when familiar patterns of adaptation are maintained when possible
   C. Social withdrawal is always biologically required

 D. Successful aging requires identical lifestyles for all people
       Answer: B. Aging is easiest when familiar patterns of adaptation are maintained when
possible
   Rationale: Continuity theory emphasizes maintaining consistent behaviors and roles.

69. A retired teacher joins community organizations, volunteers regularly, and maintains close
friendships. This pattern most strongly supports:

   A. disengagement theory
   B. activity theory
   C. psychosexual fixation

 D. reflex theory
       Answer: B. activity theory
   Rationale: Active engagement in social roles promotes well-being in older adults.

70. Selective optimization with compensation is best illustrated by an older pianist who:
   A. stops playing completely after noticing slower finger movement
   B. practices shorter pieces more often and uses modified techniques to maintain performance
   C. denies all change in ability

 D. performs only unfamiliar works to increase stress tolerance
       Answer: B. practices shorter pieces more often and uses modified techniques to maintain
performance
   Rationale: This model involves adapting strategies to maintain functioning despite decline.

71. Which cognitive change is commonly associated with late adulthood?
   A. uniform collapse of all knowledge systems
   B. slower processing speed with preservation of some accumulated knowledge
   C. disappearance of long-term memory

 D. inability to solve any practical problem
       Answer: B. slower processing speed with preservation of some accumulated knowledge
   Rationale: Aging affects speed more than accumulated knowledge.
72. Wisdom is best conceptualized as:
   A. rapid recall of isolated facts
   B. highly efficient sensory processing
   C. sound judgment about complex matters of life

 D. freedom from emotional pain
       Answer: C. sound judgment about complex matters of life
   Rationale: Wisdom involves insight, reflection, and balanced judgment.

73. Which factor is most consistently associated with better adjustment in late adulthood?
   A. complete dependence on others
   B. strong social support and meaningful engagement
   C. avoidance of all role changes

 D. denial of health limitations
       Answer: B. strong social support and meaningful engagement
   Rationale: Social relationships are key predictors of successful aging.

74. A widowed older adult gradually reconstructs routines, maintains ties with family, and
discovers new sources of meaning. This most clearly reflects:

   A. adaptive coping after bereavement
   B. unresolved object permanence
   C. psychomotor compensation only

 D. formal operational emergence
       Answer: A. adaptive coping after bereavement
   Rationale: Adjustment after loss involves rebuilding routines and finding meaning.

75. Which statement about grief is most accurate?
   A. Everyone experiences grief in the same sequence and intensity
   B. Grief responses vary across persons, relationships, and cultural contexts
   C. Grief is pathological unless completed within a fixed time

 D. Emotional numbness is the only normal response to loss
       Answer: B. Grief responses vary across persons, relationships, and cultural contexts
   Rationale: Grief is individualized and culturally influenced.

76. An adult who experiences sorrow after the death of a former spouse while also feeling relief
after years of caregiving burden is showing:

   A. invalid grief
   B. disorganized attachment
   C. ambivalent but normal bereavement reactions

 D. absence of emotional involvement
       Answer: C. ambivalent but normal bereavement reactions
   Rationale: Mixed emotions are normal in grief.

77. Which situation best illustrates anticipatory grief?
   A. A child mourns a pet years after its death
   B. Family members begin emotional adjustment while a loved one is terminally ill
   C. A widower avoids all reminders of the deceased

 D. A teenager denies that death exists
       Answer: B. Family members begin emotional adjustment while a loved one is terminally ill
   Rationale: Anticipatory grief occurs before actual loss.

78. A clinician helping a bereaved client identify values, maintain bonds through memory, and
reconstruct purpose is most directly facilitating:

   A. meaning-making
   B. egocentrism
   C. extinction

 D. seriation
       Answer: A. meaning-making
   Rationale: Meaning-making helps individuals adapt after loss.

79. Which issue is most central in ethical discussions of end-of-life decision-making?
   A. Whether infants can conserve quantity
   B. Balancing autonomy, dignity, and protection from harm
   C. How to improve processing speed in late adulthood

 D. Whether attachment is secure or avoidant
       Answer: B. Balancing autonomy, dignity, and protection from harm
   Rationale: Ethical dilemmas involve balancing key principles.

80. A child begins to understand death as irreversible and universal. This reflects growth in:
   A. moral disengagement
   B. cognitive understanding of death
   C. sensorimotor adaptation

 D. social referencing
       Answer: B. cognitive understanding of death
   Rationale: Children gradually develop mature concepts of death.

81. A psychometrician employed in a clinic is instructed to sign a report containing diagnostic
conclusions beyond the psychometrician's lawful role. The most ethical response is to:

   A. sign to preserve workplace harmony
   B. sign if a supervisor verbally approves afterward
   C. refuse to exceed role boundaries and elevate the concern appropriately

 D. sign as long as the client will benefit
       Answer: C. refuse to exceed role boundaries and elevate the concern appropriately
   Rationale: Professionals must practice within legal scope under RA 10029.

82. A practitioner is asked to administer a specialized neuropsychological instrument never
previously studied or supervised. The best initial action is to:

   A. administer it and learn during testing
   B. decline or obtain proper training and supervision before use
   C. let clerical staff conduct the procedure

 D. interpret only high scores and omit weak areas
       Answer: B. decline or obtain proper training and supervision before use
   Rationale: Competence is required before administering tests.

83. Which action best reflects appropriate handling of confidential information?
   A. Discussing a case in a public elevator without names
   B. Sharing identifiable details in group chat for convenience
   C. Limiting disclosure to what is necessary for authorized professional purposes

 D. Forwarding full records to all referral sources automatically
       Answer: C. Limiting disclosure to what is necessary for authorized professional purposes
   Rationale: Confidentiality requires minimal necessary disclosure.

84. A psychometrician conducting online assessment notices that the client is being coached
off-camera by a relative. The best action is to:

   A. ignore it to preserve rapport
   B. continue and score normally
   C. address the concern, document the irregularity, and evaluate whether administration
remains valid

 D. delete the session without explanation
       Answer: C. address the concern, document the irregularity, and evaluate whether
administration remains valid
   Rationale: Integrity of testing must be maintained.

85. Under RA 10029-aligned practice, supervision is important primarily because it:
   A. removes the need for competence
   B. ensures tasks are performed within lawful and professional limits
   C. transfers all responsibility to the supervisor

 D. allows any delegated activity regardless of training
       Answer: B. ensures tasks are performed within lawful and professional limits
   Rationale: Supervision ensures ethical and legal compliance.

86. A practitioner realizes that fatigue and personal stress are affecting concentration during
assessment work. The most ethical response is to:

   A. proceed to avoid inconvenience
   B. falsify confidence and continue
   C. take appropriate steps to limit impairment and protect service quality

 D. blame the client for poor cooperation
       Answer: C. take appropriate steps to limit impairment and protect service quality
   Rationale: Practitioners must avoid impaired professional functioning.

87. Which situation is the clearest example of a multiple relationship that may impair objectivity?
   A. Conducting an intake interview with a stranger
   B. Assessing one's romantic partner for a formal report
   C. Referring a client to another clinic

 D. Keeping professional notes in a secure file
       Answer: B. Assessing one's romantic partner for a formal report
   Rationale: Dual relationships impair objectivity and professionalism.

88. A school contracts a practitioner to assess a student for placement, and the parents assume
the results are completely private from the school. The practitioner should first:

   A. avoid clarifying anything until results are released
   B. clarify who the client is, the purpose of the service, who will receive the report, and
confidentiality limits
   C. guarantee absolute secrecy to the parents

 D. send the full report to all teachers immediately
       Answer: B. clarify who the client is, the purpose of the service, who will receive the report,
and confidentiality limits
   Rationale: Clear informed consent requires understanding roles and limits.

89. Which action most directly protects test security?
   A. Posting sample secure items on social media for public education
   B. Leaving protocols in an unlocked reception area
   C. Restricting access to materials to qualified and authorized persons

 D. Allowing examinees to photograph testing materials for review
       Answer: C. Restricting access to materials to qualified and authorized persons
   Rationale: Test security depends on controlled access.

90. A psychometrician is asked to provide emergency support during a disaster despite lacking
full expertise in crisis intervention. Which response is most ethically appropriate?

   A. Refuse all involvement under any circumstance
   B. Provide limited assistance within closely related competence while facilitating referral and
discontinuing once appropriate services are available
   C. Offer long-term psychotherapy independently

 D. Make diagnostic conclusions outside training because urgency permits anything
       Answer: B. Provide limited assistance within closely related competence while facilitating
referral and discontinuing once appropriate services are available
   Rationale: Limited emergency support within competence is ethically acceptable.

91. Which statement best reflects ethical record-keeping?
   A. Records should contain only positive findings
   B. Records should be accurate, secure, and maintained in a professionally responsible

manner
   C. Records are optional if rapport is good

 D. Records may be altered later to match client preference
       Answer: B. Records should be accurate, secure, and maintained in a professionally
responsible manner
   Rationale: Proper documentation ensures accountability and ethical practice.

92. A practitioner is invited to advertise services by claiming guaranteed improvement and
"board-top caliber results." The most ethical judgment is that this claim is:

   A. acceptable if commonly used in marketing
   B. acceptable if clients like the slogan
   C. inappropriate because it is potentially deceptive and exaggerated

 D. required to remain competitive
       Answer: C. inappropriate because it is potentially deceptive and exaggerated
   Rationale: Ethical standards prohibit misleading claims.

93. Which response best reflects fairness in addressing a colleague's possible ethical violation?
   A. Filing a complaint recklessly without supporting facts
   B. Ignoring the issue because confrontation is uncomfortable
   C. Responding with appropriate concern, evidence, and regard for due process

 D. Publicly posting allegations online first
       Answer: C. Responding with appropriate concern, evidence, and regard for due process
   Rationale: Ethical response requires fairness and proper procedure.

94. A practitioner receives a subpoena for client records. The best ethical principle is to:
   A. release all information immediately without review
   B. refuse all legal requests automatically
   C. consider legal requirements carefully while limiting disclosure to what is necessary and

justified

 D. destroy the records to preserve confidentiality
       Answer: C. consider legal requirements carefully while limiting disclosure to what is
necessary and justified
   Rationale: Ethical practice balances legal compliance and confidentiality.

95. Which action best demonstrates respect for informed consent?
   A. Using technical language without checking comprehension
   B. Presenting procedures, risks, benefits, and limits in understandable terms before service

delivery
   C. Obtaining a signature after testing to save time

 D. Assuming silence implies consent
       Answer: B. Presenting procedures, risks, benefits, and limits in understandable terms
before service delivery
   Rationale: Informed consent requires clear understanding before participation.

96. A practitioner uses client material in a lecture but removes the name only, leaving many
identifying details. This is unethical because:

   A. any teaching about cases is forbidden
   B. disguising identity must be adequate to protect confidentiality
   C. educational settings are exempt from ethical duties
 D. names are the only protected identifiers
       Answer: B. disguising identity must be adequate to protect confidentiality
   Rationale: Confidentiality requires full de-identification.

97. Which scenario best illustrates a conflict between organizational demand and professional
ethics?

   A. A clinic asks for exact test data release to unauthorized staff for convenience
   B. A practitioner attends CPD training
   C. A client asks about office hours

 D. A supervisor requests punctual documentation
       Answer: A. A clinic asks for exact test data release to unauthorized staff for convenience
   Rationale: Organizational demands may conflict with ethical standards.

98. Continuing professional development is ethically important because it:
   A. replaces formal training entirely
   B. helps maintain competence in evolving areas of practice
   C. applies only to researchers

 D. is unrelated to license renewal and service quality
       Answer: B. helps maintain competence in evolving areas of practice
   Rationale: Ongoing education ensures updated knowledge and competence.

99. A practitioner working with a minor should be especially attentive to:
   A. eliminating assent procedures
   B. obtaining no consent when parents are present
   C. explaining services appropriately, seeking assent when possible, and considering the

child's welfare

 D. treating the child exactly as a legally autonomous adult in all matters
       Answer: C. explaining services appropriately, seeking assent when possible, and
considering the child's welfare
   Rationale: Ethical practice with minors requires assent and protection of welfare.

100. Which statement best captures the ethical foundation of professional psychological
practice?

    A. Personal opinion should override standards when intentions are good
    B. Competent care, integrity, respect for dignity, and responsibility to society guide conduct
    C. Efficiency is always more important than confidentiality

 D. Legal compliance alone is sufficient even when ethical reflection is absent
        Answer: B. Competent care, integrity, respect for dignity, and responsibility to society
guide conduct
    Rationale: Ethical practice is grounded in core professional principles of competence,
integrity, and respect.
DEVELOPMENTAL PSYCHOLOGY
EXAM 10
DEVELOPMENTAL PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 10

1. A developmental researcher argues that behavior can only be understood by examining how
biological, psychological, and social systems interact dynamically over time. This view is most
consistent with:

  A. reductionism
  B. dynamic systems approach
  C. maturation theory

 D. nativism
       Answer: B. dynamic systems approach
  Rationale: Development is best explained as the result of continuous interaction among
multiple systems rather than a single factor.

2. A child raised in two cultures shows flexible adaptation to different norms depending on
context. This best illustrates:

  A. plasticity
  B. fixation
  C. imprinting

 D. conservation
       Answer: A. plasticity
  Rationale: Plasticity refers to the capacity for change and adaptation in response to
environmental demands.

3. Which concept refers to the timing of biological and environmental events relative to their
impact on development?

  A. epigenesis
  B. developmental timing
  C. canalization

 D. cohort effect
       Answer: B. developmental timing
  Rationale: Developmental timing concerns when events occur and how their timing influences
developmental outcomes.

4. A study finds that individuals born in the same year share unique developmental experiences
due to historical events. This is known as:

  A. maturation effect
  B. cohort effect
  C. practice effect

 D. regression effect
       Answer: B. cohort effect
  Rationale: Cohort effects arise from shared historical experiences among individuals born at
the same time.

5. Which theorist emphasized ecological systems influencing development?
  A. Skinner
  B. Bronfenbrenner
  C. Pavlov

 D. Thorndike
       Answer: B. Bronfenbrenner
  Rationale: Bronfenbrenner proposed ecological systems theory, emphasizing environmental
layers shaping development.

6. A psychologist studies how parenting practices differ across socioeconomic groups and affect
child outcomes. This is an example of:

  A. micro-level analysis only
  B. macrosystem influence
  C. exosystem influence

 D. chronosystem analysis
       Answer: B. macrosystem influence
  Rationale: Socioeconomic factors reflect broader cultural and societal influences within the
macrosystem.

7. Which research design is most effective in separating age effects from cohort effects?
  A. cross-sectional
  B. longitudinal
  C. sequential

 D. correlational
       Answer: C. sequential
  Rationale: Sequential designs combine methods to distinguish age-related changes from
cohort influences.

8. A researcher repeatedly measures how a child learns a new task over several trials in a short
period. This is:

  A. longitudinal method
  B. microgenetic method
  C. experimental design

 D. ethnographic study
       Answer: B. microgenetic method
  Rationale: Microgenetic methods capture rapid changes during learning over short periods.

9. Which principle ensures that participants are not exposed to unnecessary harm during
research?

  A. justice
  B. beneficence
  C. fidelity

 D. autonomy
       Answer: B. beneficence
  Rationale: Beneficence requires minimizing harm and maximizing participant welfare.
10. A researcher conceals the true purpose of a study but explains it afterward. This process is
called:

   A. standardization
   B. manipulation
   C. debriefing

 D. anonymization
       Answer: C. debriefing
   Rationale: Debriefing involves explaining the true nature of the study after participation.

11. A trait that appears only when both alleles are identical is:
   A. dominant
   B. recessive
   C. polygenic

 D. multifactorial
       Answer: B. recessive
   Rationale: Recessive traits are expressed only when two identical alleles are present.

12. Identical twins who are raised apart still show similarities in personality. This supports:
   A. environmental determinism
   B. genetic influence
   C. cultural relativism

 D. social learning only
       Answer: B. genetic influence
   Rationale: Similarities despite different environments indicate strong genetic contributions.

13. Which prenatal complication involves improper implantation of the placenta?
   A. ectopic pregnancy
   B. placenta previa
   C. teratogenesis

 D. gestational diabetes
       Answer: B. placenta previa
   Rationale: Placenta previa occurs when the placenta blocks the cervical opening.

14. A pregnant woman experiences severe stress. The fetus is at risk primarily due to:
   A. increased nutrient intake
   B. hormonal changes affecting development
   C. improved oxygenation

 D. reduced blood circulation
       Answer: B. hormonal changes affecting development
   Rationale: Maternal stress hormones can negatively influence fetal development.

15. Which nutrient deficiency is strongly associated with neural tube defects?
   A. iron
   B. calcium
   C. folic acid

 D. vitamin C
       Answer: C. folic acid
   Rationale: Folic acid is essential for proper neural tube development.

16. Which factor most strongly predicts neonatal survival?
   A. birth order
   B. birth weight
   C. parental education

 D. infant temperament
       Answer: B. birth weight
   Rationale: Higher birth weight is strongly associated with increased survival rates.

17. A newborn turns its head toward a touch on the cheek. This is the:
   A. Babinski reflex
   B. rooting reflex
   C. Moro reflex

 D. grasp reflex
       Answer: B. rooting reflex
   Rationale: The rooting reflex helps infants locate a food source.

18. Which sense is least developed at birth?
   A. vision
   B. hearing
   C. smell

 D. touch
       Answer: A. vision
   Rationale: Vision is the least mature sensory system at birth.

19. An infant recognizes their caregiver's voice shortly after birth. This ability develops primarily
through:

   A. postnatal learning
   B. prenatal experience
   C. conditioning after birth

 D. imitation
       Answer: B. prenatal experience
   Rationale: Fetuses can hear and learn sounds before birth.

20. The concept of intermodal perception refers to:
   A. combining information from multiple senses
   B. focusing attention on one stimulus
   C. ignoring irrelevant stimuli
   D. reflexive responses
  Answer: A. combining information from multiple senses

   Rationale: Intermodal perception integrates sensory inputs across modalities.

21. A baby learns that shaking a rattle produces sound. This is an example of:
   A. operant conditioning
   B. classical conditioning
   C. habituation

 D. sensitization
       Answer: A. operant conditioning
   Rationale: The baby learns through consequences of behavior.

22. When infants modify schemas based on new experiences, this is called:
   A. assimilation
   B. accommodation
   C. equilibration

 D. conservation
       Answer: B. accommodation
   Rationale: Accommodation involves changing schemas to fit new information.

23. A toddler pretends a block is a phone. This demonstrates:
   A. symbolic thought
   B. egocentrism
   C. centration

 D. irreversibility
       Answer: A. symbolic thought
   Rationale: Symbolic thinking allows one object to represent another.

24. A child insists the moon is following them. This reflects:
   A. animism
   B. centration
   C. egocentrism

 D. transductive reasoning
       Answer: C. egocentrism
   Rationale: Egocentrism involves inability to distinguish one's perspective from reality.

25. A child believes breaking more cups is worse than breaking one cup accidentally. This
reflects:

   A. moral relativism
   B. heteronomous morality
   C. autonomous morality

 D. moral disengagement
       Answer: B. heteronomous morality
   Rationale: Young children judge actions based on consequences rather than intent.
26. A child improves reading skills through guided support from a teacher. This reflects:
   A. conditioning
   B. scaffolding
   C. imprinting

 D. habituation
       Answer: B. scaffolding
   Rationale: Scaffolding involves guided support from a more knowledgeable individual to
enhance learning.

27. Which factor most influences school readiness?
   A. genetic intelligence alone
   B. early learning experiences
   C. birth order

 D. gender
       Answer: B. early learning experiences
   Rationale: Exposure to stimulating and supportive environments prepares children for school
tasks.

28. A child with ADHD struggles mainly with:
   A. emotional attachment
   B. attention regulation
   C. language development

 D. moral reasoning
       Answer: B. attention regulation
   Rationale: ADHD is primarily characterized by difficulties in sustaining attention and
controlling impulses.

29. A child who is both assertive and cooperative is likely to be:
   A. rejected
   B. neglected
   C. popular

 D. controversial
       Answer: C. popular
   Rationale: Social competence, including assertiveness and cooperation, is associated with
peer acceptance.

30. A child imitates aggressive behavior seen in media. This supports:
   A. psychoanalytic theory
   B. social learning theory
   C. cognitive theory

 D. maturation theory
       Answer: B. social learning theory
   Rationale: Behavior is learned through observation and imitation of models.
31. Which statement best describes puberty as a developmental process?
   A. It is a single event completed in one month.
   B. It is a biologically driven transition involving hormonal and physical maturation.
   C. It occurs at the same age for all adolescents.

 D. It affects only physical growth and not behavior.
       Answer: B. It is a biologically driven transition involving hormonal and physical maturation.
   Rationale: Puberty is a gradual biological process involving hormonal changes and physical
development.

32. Early-maturing boys are often viewed by peers as:
   A. less competent and socially immature
   B. physically weaker and more dependent
   C. more confident and socially mature

 D. less likely to engage in risk-taking
       Answer: C. more confident and socially mature
   Rationale: Early maturation in boys is often associated with higher social status and
confidence.

33. Which brain region is especially linked to planning, impulse control, and decision-making in
adolescence?

   A. medulla
   B. cerebellum
   C. prefrontal cortex

 D. occipital lobe
       Answer: C. prefrontal cortex
   Rationale: The prefrontal cortex is responsible for executive functions and matures during
adolescence.

34. The tendency of adolescents to believe their feelings are unique and incomprehensible to
others is called:

   A. personal fable
   B. object permanence
   C. social referencing

 D. reaction formation
       Answer: A. personal fable
   Rationale: Adolescents often believe their experiences are unique and not understood by
others.

35. Which is the best example of formal operational thinking?
   A. A child groups objects by color.
   B. An adolescent reasons through hypothetical scientific problems.
   C. A toddler searches for a hidden toy.

 D. A preschooler engages in pretend play.
       Answer: B. An adolescent reasons through hypothetical scientific problems.
   Rationale: Formal operations involve abstract and hypothetical reasoning.

36. A teenager argues that a rule should be evaluated according to fairness rather than simple
obedience. This reflects movement toward:

   A. preconventional reasoning
   B. postconventional reasoning
   C. heteronomous morality

 D. conditioned compliance
       Answer: B. postconventional reasoning
   Rationale: Postconventional reasoning involves evaluating rules based on ethical principles.

37. Marcia's identity status involving commitment after exploration is:
   A. diffusion
   B. foreclosure
   C. achievement

 D. moratorium
       Answer: C. achievement
   Rationale: Identity achievement follows exploration and commitment.

38. An adolescent who has not explored career options and shows little concern about future
plans is in identity:

   A. diffusion
   B. achievement
   C. foreclosure

 D. moratorium
       Answer: A. diffusion
   Rationale: Diffusion reflects lack of both exploration and commitment.

39. Which parental style is most consistently associated with lower adolescent misconduct and
stronger self-regulation?

   A. authoritarian
   B. authoritative
   C. permissive

 D. uninvolved
       Answer: B. authoritative
   Rationale: Authoritative parenting combines warmth and control, promoting positive
outcomes.

40. A youth joins a peer group mainly to gain approval and belonging. This behavior most
directly reflects the developmental importance of:

   A. attachment in infancy
   B. peer affiliation in adolescence
   C. object permanence
   D. reflex development
  Answer: B. peer affiliation in adolescence

   Rationale: Peer relationships are central to social development during adolescence.

41. Emerging adulthood is most often marked by:
   A. complete role stability
   B. identity exploration and instability
   C. universal marriage and parenthood

 D. declining cognitive flexibility
       Answer: B. identity exploration and instability
   Rationale: Emerging adulthood involves exploration in identity and life directions.

42. Which term refers to thinking that integrates logic with practical experience and ambiguity in
adulthood?

   A. preoperational thought
   B. postformal thought
   C. sensorimotor thought

 D. concrete symbolism
       Answer: B. postformal thought
   Rationale: Postformal thought reflects flexible and realistic reasoning.

43. A young adult chooses a job that offers lower salary but stronger alignment with personal
values. This best reflects:

   A. crystallized intelligence
   B. postformal reasoning
   C. reaction formation

 D. stranger anxiety
       Answer: B. postformal reasoning
   Rationale: This decision shows integration of values and practical reasoning.

44. Sternberg's practical intelligence is best demonstrated when a person:
   A. memorizes vocabulary definitions
   B. solves everyday real-world problems effectively
   C. recalls childhood events accurately

 D. completes abstract analogies quickly
       Answer: B. solves everyday real-world problems effectively
   Rationale: Practical intelligence involves solving real-life problems.

45. A college student who struggles academically during the first semester but gradually adjusts
to campus demands is showing:

   A. role diffusion
   B. developmental adaptation
   C. learned helplessness

 D. irreversible decline
       Answer: B. developmental adaptation
   Rationale: Adjustment to new demands reflects adaptive development.

46. In Erikson's theory, the main psychosocial challenge of young adulthood is:
   A. autonomy versus shame
   B. identity versus role confusion
   C. intimacy versus isolation

 D. generativity versus stagnation
       Answer: C. intimacy versus isolation
   Rationale: Young adults seek meaningful relationships.

47. Which factor is most associated with strong relationship satisfaction in young adulthood?
   A. absolute absence of conflict
   B. rigid role expectations
   C. effective communication and mutual commitment

 D. identical personalities in all areas
       Answer: C. effective communication and mutual commitment
   Rationale: Healthy communication strengthens relationships.

48. Parenthood is often considered a developmental turning point because it commonly
involves:

   A. immediate loss of adult identity
   B. permanent decline in cognitive ability
   C. reorganization of roles, responsibilities, and relationships

 D. elimination of all marital conflict
       Answer: C. reorganization of roles, responsibilities, and relationships
   Rationale: Parenthood reshapes life roles and priorities.

49. Which statement best reflects developmental views of adulthood?
   A. Personality stops changing after adolescence.
   B. Adult development involves continuing adaptation across life roles.
   C. Growth in adulthood is purely biological.

 D. Adulthood is more stable than childhood in every domain.
       Answer: B. Adult development involves continuing adaptation across life roles.
   Rationale: Development continues throughout adulthood.

50. A person in midlife begins mentoring younger coworkers and investing in community
projects. This best illustrates:

   A. intimacy
   B. initiative
   C. generativity

 D. despair
       Answer: C. generativity
   Rationale: Generativity involves contributing to future generations.
51. Which of the following is most typical of fluid intelligence in midlife?
   A. It reflects accumulated knowledge.
   B. It often declines earlier than crystallized intelligence.
   C. It increases steadily into late adulthood.

 D. It is unrelated to processing speed.
       Answer: B. It often declines earlier than crystallized intelligence.
   Rationale: Fluid intelligence, which involves speed and novel problem solving, tends to
decline earlier than knowledge-based abilities.

52. A 48-year-old performs very well in job tasks requiring expert judgment built over decades.
This is best explained by:

   A. synaptic pruning
   B. reflective abstraction
   C. expertise

 D. overregularization
       Answer: C. expertise
   Rationale: Expertise develops through accumulated experience and improves performance in
familiar domains.

53. Which statement about menopause is most accurate?
   A. It is identical across all women and cultures.
   B. It is purely psychological.
   C. Its meaning and experience are influenced by biological and cultural factors.

 D. It marks the end of all well-being in midlife.
       Answer: C. Its meaning and experience are influenced by biological and cultural factors.
   Rationale: Menopause is shaped by both physiological processes and sociocultural context.

54. The "sandwich generation" refers to adults who are:
   A. balancing college and work
   B. caring for children while also supporting aging parents
   C. living with siblings in late adulthood

 D. raising grandchildren exclusively
       Answer: B. caring for children while also supporting aging parents
   Rationale: The sandwich generation manages dual caregiving roles for younger and older
family members.

55. Which midlife change is most likely to promote psychological well-being?
   A. narrowing all social roles
   B. maintaining meaningful commitments and flexibility
   C. avoiding reflection on life choices

 D. denying all physical changes
       Answer: B. maintaining meaningful commitments and flexibility
   Rationale: Flexibility and continued engagement are linked to positive midlife adjustment.
56. Late adulthood is often divided into "young-old," "old-old," and "oldest-old" primarily to
reflect:

   A. fixed personality types
   B. broad variability among older adults
   C. moral development stages

 D. different reflex patterns
       Answer: B. broad variability among older adults
   Rationale: These categories acknowledge diversity in functioning and experience among
older adults.

57. Which theory proposes that aging results partly from accumulated biological wear and
damage?

   A. psychoanalytic theory
   B. wear-and-tear theory
   C. social clock theory

 D. activity theory
       Answer: B. wear-and-tear theory
   Rationale: Wear-and-tear theory explains aging as the result of accumulated physical
damage over time.

58. Presbyopia refers to age-related difficulty with:
   A. hearing high-pitched sounds
   B. sleeping through the night
   C. focusing on near objects

 D. balance and gait only
       Answer: C. focusing on near objects
   Rationale: Presbyopia is the decline in the eye's ability to focus on close objects.

59. Which memory system tends to remain relatively stronger in normal aging compared with
working memory and processing speed?

   A. sensory register
   B. episodic memory
   C. semantic memory

 D. short-term rehearsal only
       Answer: C. semantic memory
   Rationale: Knowledge-based memory (semantic) is more preserved than speed-dependent
memory systems.

60. Wisdom in late adulthood is best understood as:
   A. perfect memory for facts
   B. broad and reflective judgment about life matters
   C. absence of emotional distress

 D. high processing speed only
       Answer: B. broad and reflective judgment about life matters
   Rationale: Wisdom involves insight, reflection, and sound judgment rather than speed or
memory alone.

61. Which statement best reflects activity theory of aging?
   A. Older adults adjust best by withdrawing from all major roles.
   B. Satisfaction in later life is associated with continued engagement in meaningful activities.
   C. Aging is controlled entirely by genetics.

 D. Social participation is harmful in old age.
       Answer: B. Satisfaction in later life is associated with continued engagement in meaningful
activities.
   Rationale: Activity theory states that staying active promotes life satisfaction in old age.

62. A retired adult who volunteers, maintains hobbies, and nurtures friendships is best
illustrating:

   A. disengagement
   B. activity theory
   C. role confusion

 D. learned dependency
       Answer: B. activity theory
   Rationale: Continued involvement in meaningful roles reflects activity theory principles.

63. Which factor is strongly associated with successful aging?
   A. complete avoidance of loss
   B. adaptation through selective optimization with compensation
   C. refusal to accept change

 D. isolation from younger generations
       Answer: B. adaptation through selective optimization with compensation
   Rationale: Successful aging involves adapting through strengths and compensating for
losses.

64. An older adult who uses a notebook and phone reminders to manage reduced memory is
showing:

   A. fixation
   B. compensation
   C. accommodation failure

 D. animism
       Answer: B. compensation
   Rationale: Using aids to offset decline reflects compensatory strategies.

65. In Erikson's framework, an older adult who accepts both achievements and regrets with a
sense of wholeness demonstrates:

   A. stagnation
   B. ego integrity
   C. foreclosure
 D. isolation
       Answer: B. ego integrity
   Rationale: Ego integrity reflects acceptance of one's life as meaningful.

66. Which statement best reflects contemporary views on grief?
   A. All mourners progress through identical stages.
   B. Grief follows a fixed timeline.
   C. Grief varies across individuals and cultures.

 D. Continuing bonds are always unhealthy.
       Answer: C. Grief varies across individuals and cultures.
   Rationale: Modern perspectives recognize variability in grief responses.

67. Which situation best illustrates ambiguous loss?
   A. Death after illness
   B. Disappearance of a loved one
   C. Retirement
