 D. Graduation
       Answer: B. Disappearance of a loved one
   Rationale: Ambiguous loss lacks closure and clarity.

68. A terminally ill patient reviewing life experiences to find meaning is engaging in:
   A. life review
   B. habituation
   C. reinforcement

 D. projection
       Answer: A. life review
   Rationale: Life review helps integrate experiences and achieve meaning.

69. Which issue most directly involves ethical considerations in late adulthood?
   A. vocabulary development
   B. right-to-die decisions
   C. reflexes

 D. play behavior
       Answer: B. right-to-die decisions
   Rationale: End-of-life decisions involve ethical dilemmas about autonomy and care.

70. A young child believes a dead person can still feel hunger. This reflects:
   A. formal reasoning
   B. mature understanding of death
   C. incomplete concept of death

 D. postformal thought
       Answer: C. incomplete concept of death
   Rationale: Young children lack full understanding of death's permanence.
71. A psychologist advertises guaranteed results for therapy. This is unethical because it
involves:

   A. lack of warmth
   B. deceptive statements
   C. weak reinforcement

 D. delayed consent
       Answer: B. deceptive statements
   Rationale: Guaranteeing outcomes is misleading and violates ethical standards.

72. A practitioner works outside their training without consultation. This violates:
   A. competence
   B. autonomy
   C. conditioning

 D. adaptation
       Answer: A. competence
   Rationale: Ethical practice requires working within one's professional competence.

73. Under RA 10029, a psychometrician may properly:
   A. provide psychotherapy
   B. administer psychological tests within scope
   C. diagnose independently

 D. perform all psychologist duties
       Answer: B. administer psychological tests within scope
   Rationale: Psychometricians are authorized to administer and score tests within legal limits.

74. A client expresses intent to harm themselves. The psychologist should:
   A. keep it confidential
   B. take necessary steps to protect life
   C. terminate immediately

 D. ignore the threat
       Answer: B. take necessary steps to protect life
   Rationale: Ethical duty allows breaching confidentiality to prevent harm.

75. A psychometrician is asked to interpret complex results beyond training. The best response
is to:

   A. proceed anyway
   B. guess cautiously
   C. refer to a qualified professional

 D. release raw data only
       Answer: C. refer to a qualified professional
   Rationale: Ethical practice requires staying within competence.

76. Which best reflects informed consent?
   A. explaining after service
   B. providing clear information before service
   C. only written consent

 D. optional explanation
       Answer: B. providing clear information before service
   Rationale: Informed consent ensures understanding before participation.

77. Leaving client records unsecured violates:
   A. boundaries
   B. confidentiality
   C. reinforcement

 D. learning
       Answer: B. confidentiality
   Rationale: Client information must be protected.

78. In third-party assessment, the psychologist must clarify:
   A. only fees
   B. role and limits of confidentiality
   C. client's personality

 D. test length
       Answer: B. role and limits of confidentiality
   Rationale: Ethical clarity is required in third-party contexts.

79. A psychologist experiencing impairment should:
   A. continue unchanged
   B. seek help and adjust duties
   C. ignore it

 D. deny it
       Answer: B. seek help and adjust duties
   Rationale: Ethical codes require addressing impairment.

80. Observing a colleague's harmful ethical violation requires:
   A. ignoring
   B. gossiping
   C. appropriate reporting

 D. public posting
       Answer: C. appropriate reporting
   Rationale: Ethical responsibility includes addressing violations.

81. Improvement after early deprivation supports:
   A. fixation
   B. plasticity
   C. rigidity

 D. determinism
       Answer: B. plasticity
   Rationale: Development can change with experience.

82. Cultural differences in child roles illustrate:
   A. biology only
   B. cultural context
   C. fixed intelligence

 D. maturation only
       Answer: B. cultural context
   Rationale: Culture shapes developmental expectations.

83. A child focuses only on height of liquid reflects:
   A. classification
   B. centration
   C. abstraction

 D. memory
       Answer: B. centration
   Rationale: Focusing on one feature shows centration.

84. Understanding intentions in moral judgment reflects:
   A. autonomous morality
   B. reflex action
   C. conditioning

 D. imitation
       Answer: A. autonomous morality
   Rationale: Mature moral reasoning considers intent.

85. Learning gender roles through observation reflects:
   A. instinct
   B. modeling
   C. reflex

 D. heredity
       Answer: B. modeling
   Rationale: Social learning explains gender behavior.

86. A toddler insisting "I do it myself" reflects:
   A. initiative
   B. industry
   C. autonomy

 D. intimacy
       Answer: C. autonomy
   Rationale: Toddlers seek independence.

87. Different performance in different settings reflects:
   A. context
   B. deficiency
   C. disorder

 D. delay
       Answer: A. context
   Rationale: Environment affects behavior.

88. Adolescent risk-taking reflects:
   A. full control maturity
   B. brain development imbalance
   C. no peer influence

 D. lack of reasoning
       Answer: B. brain development imbalance
   Rationale: Reward systems mature earlier than control systems.

89. Changing careers in adulthood reflects:
   A. regression
   B. reorganization
   C. fixation

 D. immaturity
       Answer: B. reorganization
   Rationale: Adults adapt and redefine identity.

90. Crystallized intelligence involves:
   A. speed
   B. accumulated knowledge
   C. reflex

 D. attention
       Answer: B. accumulated knowledge
   Rationale: It reflects learned knowledge.

91. Uneven decline in cognition reflects:
   A. total decline
   B. differential aging
   C. no change

 D. regression
       Answer: B. differential aging
   Rationale: Different abilities decline at different rates.

92. Healthy adjustment after loss reflects:
   A. pathology
   B. adaptation
   C. denial

 D. failure
       Answer: B. adaptation
   Rationale: Adjusting and rebuilding is healthy grief.

93. Effects of life transitions over time reflect:
   A. microsystem
   B. exosystem
   C. chronosystem

 D. macrosystem
       Answer: C. chronosystem
   Rationale: Chronosystem involves time-based influences.

94. Accurate assessment requires:
   A. single test
   B. multiple sources
   C. quick diagnosis

 D. ignoring context
       Answer: B. multiple sources
   Rationale: Comprehensive assessment improves validity.

95. Growth vs development distinction:
   A. emotional vs physical
   B. identical
   C. quantitative vs qualitative

 D. unrelated
       Answer: C. quantitative vs qualitative
   Rationale: Growth is size change; development is functional change.

96. Understanding part-whole relationships reflects:
   A. logic
   B. class inclusion
   C. memory

 D. imitation
       Answer: B. class inclusion
   Rationale: Recognizing subsets within a whole.

97. Resilience means:
   A. no adversity
   B. positive adaptation
   C. fixed trait

 D. independence only
       Answer: B. positive adaptation
   Rationale: Resilience is coping effectively despite adversity.

98. Using inappropriate norms reflects:
   A. security issue
   B. validity problem
   C. consent issue

 D. financial issue
       Answer: B. validity problem
   Rationale: Wrong norms reduce accuracy.

99. Exploitation is best illustrated by:
   A. referral
   B. financial pressure
   C. consent

 D. consultation
       Answer: B. financial pressure
   Rationale: Taking advantage of vulnerability is unethical.

100. Ethical telepractice requires:
    A. ignoring issues
    B. managing limitations and protecting confidentiality
    C. recording without consent

 D. using public apps
        Answer: B. managing limitations and protecting confidentiality
    Rationale: Ethical care includes safeguarding client welfare and privacy.
DEVELOPMENTAL PSYCHOLOGY
EXAM 11
DEVELOPMENTAL PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 11

1. A developmental researcher argues that childhood and adolescence are not fixed natural
categories but are partly shaped by cultural expectations and historical conditions. This view is
most consistent with the idea that developmental periods are:

  A. genetically programmed
  B. social constructions
  C. biologically invariant

 D. psychometrically derived
       Answer: B. social constructions
  Rationale: Developmental periods such as childhood and adolescence are considered social
constructions because their meaning and boundaries vary across cultures and historical eras.

2. Which situation best illustrates a nonnormative influence on development?
  A. Menarche during early adolescence
  B. Entering school at the usual age
  C. Being displaced by a sudden earthquake

 D. Age-related decline in visual acuity
       Answer: C. Being displaced by a sudden earthquake
  Rationale: A nonnormative influence is an unusual event that happens irregularly and affects a
person's development in a distinctive way, such as disaster-related displacement.

3. A psychologist wants to understand how experiences in home, school, peer group, and larger
culture jointly shape a child's adjustment. Which theorist's framework is most directly
applicable?

  A. Bronfenbrenner
  B. Skinner
  C. Kohlberg

 D. Hayflick
       Answer: A. Bronfenbrenner
  Rationale: Bronfenbrenner's ecological systems approach explains development through
interacting environmental systems such as family, school, peers, and culture.

4. In developmental research, the major strength of a longitudinal design is that it:
  A. eliminates sample bias completely
  B. reveals individual continuity and change over time
  C. is faster than cross-sectional research

 D. cannot be affected by attrition
       Answer: B. reveals individual continuity and change over time
  Rationale: Longitudinal research follows the same individuals across time, allowing direct
observation of developmental continuity and change.

5. Which is the clearest example of a natural experiment in developmental psychology?
  A. Randomly assigning children to sleep-deprived and well-rested groups
  B. Observing age differences in grief across a single survey
  C. Studying children's coping after an unexpected typhoon affects only one region

 D. Interviewing parents about their discipline practices
       Answer: C. Studying children's coping after an unexpected typhoon affects only one region
  Rationale: A natural experiment examines development under naturally occurring conditions
that researchers do not manipulate, such as disaster exposure.

6. A researcher conducts in-depth observation of a small indigenous community to understand
beliefs about pregnancy, childbirth, and child-rearing. The method is best described as:

  A. correlational design
  B. ethnographic study
  C. sequential design

 D. psychometric testing
       Answer: B. ethnographic study
  Rationale: Ethnographic studies involve detailed observation and cultural immersion to
understand beliefs, practices, and meaning systems in context.

7. Which statement best captures the principle of plasticity in development?
  A. Early experiences rigidly determine adult functioning.
  B. Development can be modified by experience, although within limits.
  C. Only children show developmental change.

 D. Aging eliminates the possibility of improvement.
       Answer: B. Development can be modified by experience, although within limits.
  Rationale: Plasticity means development is open to change through experience, training, and
context, though such change is not unlimited.

8. A developmental scientist emphasizes description, explanation, prediction, and intervention
as major goals of the field. Which statement is most accurate?

  A. Intervention is always the first goal of developmental science.
  B. Developmental science is limited to describing age trends.
  C. The field seeks both understanding and practical application.

 D. Prediction is impossible in human development.
       Answer: C. The field seeks both understanding and practical application.
  Rationale: Developmental science aims to describe, explain, predict, and sometimes
intervene, making it both scientific and applicable.

9. A newborn's father is 49 years old and the mother is 25. Which statement is most accurate
regarding paternal influences before birth?

  A. Only maternal factors matter in prenatal development.
  B. Paternal age and exposures can also contribute to developmental risk.
  C. Fathers influence development only after birth.

 D. Paternal factors matter only for personality traits.
       Answer: B. Paternal age and exposures can also contribute to developmental risk.
  Rationale: Prenatal development is influenced not only by maternal factors but also by
paternal age, genetics, and environmental exposures.

10. Which prenatal period is marked by the most rapid differentiation of major organs and body
systems?

   A. germinal
   B. neonatal
   C. embryonic

 D. infancy
       Answer: C. embryonic
   Rationale: The embryonic period is the phase in which major organs and body systems are
rapidly forming, making it highly sensitive to developmental disruption.

11. A fetus begins to respond differently to the mother's voice than to unfamiliar voices. This
finding most directly supports the view that:

   A. learning and memory begin only after birth
   B. prenatal sensory learning is possible
   C. fetuses cannot discriminate speech patterns

 D. cognition is absent before language develops
       Answer: B. prenatal sensory learning is possible
   Rationale: Differential response to the mother's voice shows that learning and memory
processes begin before birth.

12. A pregnant woman reports heavy smoking and high stress. Which outcome is most directly
associated with these prenatal risks?

   A. increased chance of low birth weight
   B. guaranteed intellectual disability
   C. elimination of genetic influence

 D. faster motor maturation after birth
       Answer: A. increased chance of low birth weight
   Rationale: Maternal smoking and high stress are associated with elevated risk for low birth
weight and related developmental vulnerabilities.

13. Which statement about assisted reproductive technologies is most accurate?
   A. They guarantee a single birth with no medical complications.
   B. They may increase the likelihood of multiple births and related risks.
   C. They eliminate the importance of prenatal care.

 D. They prevent all chromosomal abnormalities.
       Answer: B. They may increase the likelihood of multiple births and related risks.
   Rationale: Assisted reproductive technologies can increase the probability of multiple births,
which are associated with higher prenatal and perinatal risk.

14. A nurse explains that a newborn delivered two weeks before the expected date and
weighing 2,100 grams faces elevated developmental risk partly because of:
   A. postmaturity
   B. low birth weight
   C. tertiary circular reactions

 D. overregularization
       Answer: B. low birth weight
   Rationale: A birth weight of 2,100 grams falls within the low-birth-weight range, which is
associated with greater developmental and medical risk.

15. Which statement best reflects contemporary understanding of childbirth practices?
   A. Cesarean delivery is always safer than vaginal delivery.
   B. Medicated and nonmedicated childbirth each have potential benefits and limitations.
   C. Electronic fetal monitoring is unnecessary in all deliveries.

 D. Cultural practices have no relevance to childbirth experiences.
       Answer: B. Medicated and nonmedicated childbirth each have potential benefits and
limitations.
   Rationale: Contemporary developmental understanding recognizes that childbirth methods
differ in risks and benefits depending on medical need, context, and preference.

16. A newborn briefly turns the head toward a touch on the cheek and begins sucking. This
behavior most clearly illustrates:

   A. symbolic representation
   B. reflexive adaptation
   C. social smiling

 D. deferred imitation
       Answer: B. reflexive adaptation
   Rationale: Rooting and sucking are neonatal reflexes that support survival and early
adaptation outside the womb.

17. A pediatrician tells parents that a newborn's behavioral state shifts among quiet sleep, active
sleep, drowsiness, alert inactivity, waking activity, and crying. This information is most useful
because:

   A. newborn arousal states relate to feeding, soothing, and early interaction
   B. arousal states determine permanent temperament
   C. only crying states are developmentally meaningful

 D. arousal states are unrelated to caregiver adjustment
       Answer: A. newborn arousal states relate to feeding, soothing, and early interaction
   Rationale: Understanding newborn states helps caregivers respond appropriately to feeding
readiness, soothing needs, and interaction opportunities.

18. Which finding would most strongly support the psychometric approach to infant
assessment?

   A. Infant IQ scores perfectly predict adult occupation.
   B. Early developmental tests can help identify children who may need intervention.
   C. Standardized testing is useless before adolescence.
 D. Home environments have no relation to developmental outcomes.
       Answer: B. Early developmental tests can help identify children who may need
intervention.
   Rationale: The psychometric approach values early assessment because it can identify
developmental concerns and support timely intervention.

19. A toddler is shown how to press a sequence of buttons to make a toy light up and repeats
the sequence the next day. This method assesses:

   A. elicited imitation
   B. conservation
   C. class inclusion

 D. reciprocal determinism
       Answer: A. elicited imitation
   Rationale: Elicited imitation measures memory by asking infants or toddlers to reproduce a
sequence they have previously observed.

20. Which observation best illustrates cross-modal transfer?
   A. A child learns to ride a bicycle after repeated falls.
   B. An infant who has mouthed a pacifier later visually recognizes its shape.
   C. A toddler uses one word to express a full sentence.

 D. A preschooler sorts blocks by color and size.
       Answer: B. An infant who has mouthed a pacifier later visually recognizes its shape.
   Rationale: Cross-modal transfer occurs when information learned through one sensory
modality is recognized through another modality.

21. A parent frequently labels objects, follows the infant's gaze, and talks responsively during
play. This interaction most directly supports language development through:

   A. joint attention
   B. animism
   C. conservation

 D. social inhibition
       Answer: A. joint attention
   Rationale: Joint attention supports early word learning because the child and caregiver
coordinate attention to the same object or event.

22. According to the behaviorist approach, an infant who learns that crying brings a caregiver
quickly to the crib is demonstrating:

   A. classical conditioning only
   B. operant conditioning
   C. object permanence

 D. accommodation
       Answer: B. operant conditioning
   Rationale: If crying is reinforced by caregiver arrival, the behavior is maintained or
strengthened through operant conditioning.
23. Which statement is most consistent with information-processing research in infancy?
   A. Early attention and processing efficiency can have predictive value for later cognitive

functioning.
   B. Infant attention has no relation to later development.
   C. Cognitive processing begins only after age 2.

 D. Information-processing research rejects all biological influence.
       Answer: A. Early attention and processing efficiency can have predictive value for later
cognitive functioning.
   Rationale: Information-processing research suggests that early measures such as habituation
speed and attentional efficiency may relate to later cognition.

24. A toddler kisses a doll goodnight after watching a parent do so earlier in the day. This
behavior is the strongest evidence of:

   A. deferred imitation
   B. circular reaction
   C. sociometric status

 D. egocentric speech
       Answer: A. deferred imitation
   Rationale: Deferred imitation occurs when a child reproduces an observed act after a delay,
demonstrating representational memory.

25. In the study of early psychosocial development, the term goodness of fit refers to:
   A. the child's physical resemblance to the parents
   B. the match between a child's temperament and environmental demands
   C. the degree of attachment to siblings

 D. the fit between IQ score and school grade
       Answer: B. the match between a child's temperament and environmental demands
   Rationale: Goodness of fit refers to how well a child's temperament is supported or matched
by caregiving expectations and environment.

26. An infant looks frightened by a barking dog, then calms down after seeing the caregiver
smile. This is the clearest example of:

   A. self-recognition
   B. mutual regulation
   C. social referencing

 D. role rehearsal
       Answer: C. social referencing
   Rationale: The infant uses the caregiver's emotional expression to guide a response to an
uncertain situation.

27. A researcher finds that caregivers in one culture respond quickly to infant crying, while in
another culture they expect more self-soothing. This finding most strongly supports which
conclusion?
   A. Attachment has no cultural variability.
   B. Early caregiving practices are shaped partly by cultural beliefs.
   C. Crying patterns are entirely genetically fixed.

 D. Only one caregiving pattern is developmentally normal.
       Answer: B. Early caregiving practices are shaped partly by cultural beliefs.
   Rationale: Variation in responses to crying across cultures reflects culturally shaped beliefs
about infants, emotion, and caregiving.

28. Which situation best illustrates the development of autonomy in toddlerhood?
   A. An infant quiets only when rocked
   B. A toddler insists on feeding himself despite making a mess
   C. A preschooler invents an imaginary friend

 D. A school-age child compares his grades with classmates
       Answer: B. A toddler insists on feeding himself despite making a mess
   Rationale: Self-assertive independence in everyday tasks is a classic sign of autonomy
development in toddlerhood.

29. A toddler obeys only when the parent is standing nearby and monitoring behavior.
Kochanska would describe this pattern as:

   A. committed compliance
   B. receptive cooperation
   C. situational compliance

 D. moral internalization
       Answer: C. situational compliance
   Rationale: Situational compliance refers to obedience that depends on immediate external
monitoring or control.

30. Which child is at greatest risk for problems associated with nonorganic failure to thrive?
   A. a child with warm caregiving and adequate nutrition
   B. a child experiencing severe neglect and poor caregiver interaction
   C. a child who begins to walk later than average

 D. a child with a secure attachment to both parents
       Answer: B. a child experiencing severe neglect and poor caregiver interaction
   Rationale: Nonorganic failure to thrive is strongly associated with neglect, poor emotional
care, and disturbed caregiver-child interaction.

31. A preschooler says, "The moon is following me." This statement most clearly reflects:
   A. transductive reasoning
   B. animistic and egocentric thinking
   C. formal operational logic

 D. postconventional morality
       Answer: B. animistic and egocentric thinking
   Rationale: The child attributes intentional action to the moon and interprets events from a
self-centered perspective.
32. Which task would be most difficult for a child in the preoperational period?
   A. engaging in pretend play
   B. using words to represent objects
   C. mentally reversing a conservation transformation

 D. drawing from memory
       Answer: C. mentally reversing a conservation transformation
   Rationale: Preoperational children typically struggle with reversibility and conservation
because they cannot yet mentally undo transformations reliably.

33. A child who understands that one object can be a "dog," a "pet," and an "animal" is
demonstrating:

   A. class inclusion
   B. overextension
   C. underregularization

 D. reflex integration
       Answer: A. class inclusion
   Rationale: Class inclusion involves understanding that an object can belong simultaneously to
a smaller and a larger category.

34. Which finding best reflects development in executive functioning during early childhood?
   A. children become less able to inhibit impulses
   B. children gradually improve in planning, attention control, and working memory
   C. executive functioning disappears as language grows

 D. executive functioning is unrelated to school readiness
       Answer: B. children gradually improve in planning, attention control, and working memory
   Rationale: Executive functioning includes inhibitory control, working memory, and planning, all
of which improve during early childhood.

35. A preschool teacher gives hints that help a child complete a puzzle the child could not solve
alone. This teaching practice is best described as:

   A. imprinting
   B. scaffolding
   C. reciprocal punishment

 D. selective optimization
       Answer: B. scaffolding
   Rationale: Scaffolding refers to temporary support that helps a child perform beyond current
independent ability.

36. Which statement about private speech is most accurate?
   A. It is always a sign of maladjustment.
   B. It reflects internalizing language for self-guidance.
   C. It shows inability to communicate socially.
   D. It disappears before age 3 in all children.
  Answer: B. It reflects internalizing language for self-guidance.

   Rationale: Private speech helps children guide thinking and behavior and is viewed as a step
toward internal verbal thought.

37. A child's emerging knowledge of print concepts, story structure, and sound-symbol
awareness is best described as:

   A. concrete operations
   B. emergent literacy
   C. latent learning

 D. semantic conditioning
       Answer: B. emergent literacy
   Rationale: Emergent literacy refers to the early skills, attitudes, and knowledge that form the
basis of later reading and writing.

38. A preschool child says, "I goed there yesterday." This error is best interpreted as evidence
that the child:

   A. lacks understanding of grammar entirely
   B. is applying a grammatical rule to an irregular verb
   C. has no memory for past events

 D. is confusing nouns and verbs
       Answer: B. is applying a grammatical rule to an irregular verb
   Rationale: "Goed" is an overregularization error showing that the child has learned a rule for
past tense formation and applies it too broadly.

39. Which statement best reflects the developmental value of play in early childhood?
   A. Play is mostly a distraction from cognitive growth.
   B. Play contributes to cognitive, social, emotional, and self-regulatory development.
   C. Only physically active play matters developmentally.

 D. Pretend play has no relation to symbolic thinking.
       Answer: B. Play contributes to cognitive, social, emotional, and self-regulatory
development.
   Rationale: Play supports symbolic thinking, peer interaction, emotion regulation, problem
solving, and role understanding.

40. A parent explains, "Hitting hurts people, so we use words instead." This discipline style most
directly promotes:

   A. fear-based obedience
   B. inductive reasoning and internalization
   C. learned helplessness

 D. passive resistance
       Answer: B. inductive reasoning and internalization
   Rationale: Explaining the consequences of behavior supports internal moral understanding
rather than simple obedience based on fear.
41. In middle childhood, one important sign of concrete operational thought is the ability to:
   A. reason only from immediate appearance
   B. think hypothetically about possibilities never experienced
   C. perform mental operations on tangible information

 D. reject rules in favor of intuition
       Answer: C. perform mental operations on tangible information
   Rationale: Concrete operational children can reason logically about real, tangible situations,
even if they still struggle with abstract hypotheticals.

42. A school-age child is more likely than a preschooler to succeed in which task?
   A. distinguishing appearance from reality only through guessing
   B. understanding seriation and transitive inference
   C. relying exclusively on centration

 D. confusing symbolic play with literal truth
       Answer: B. understanding seriation and transitive inference
   Rationale: School-age children improve in logical ordering and relational reasoning, such as
understanding that if A > B and B > C, then A > C.

43. Which statement about intelligence in middle childhood is most accurate?
   A. IQ is unaffected by school, health, and family context.
   B. Intelligence is shaped by both biological and environmental influences.
   C. Intelligence testing measures only creativity.

 D. IQ scores are meaningless after age 7.
       Answer: B. Intelligence is shaped by both biological and environmental influences.
   Rationale: Developmental evidence supports a combined role for heredity, schooling, health,
family context, and culture in intellectual development.

44. Gardner's view would be most consistent with the claim that a child who struggles in
arithmetic but excels in music:

   A. cannot be intelligent
   B. may show strength in a different form of intelligence
   C. has low general intelligence in all domains

 D. is displaying only crystallized intelligence
       Answer: B. may show strength in a different form of intelligence
   Rationale: Gardner proposed multiple intelligences, allowing for uneven profiles of cognitive
strength across domains.

45. A school-age child says, "I forgot my assignment because I didn't write it down in my
notebook." This statement most clearly reflects growth in:

   A. object permanence
   B. metamemory
   C. sensorimotor coordination

 D. animism
       Answer: B. metamemory
   Rationale: The child shows awareness of memory processes and strategies by identifying
why forgetting happened.

46. Which child is showing a mastery-oriented pattern?
   A. one who avoids difficult tasks to protect self-worth
   B. one who persists after errors and treats them as part of learning
   C. one who attributes all outcomes to luck

 D. one who refuses feedback from teachers
       Answer: B. one who persists after errors and treats them as part of learning
   Rationale: A mastery orientation involves persistence, effort, and viewing difficulty as part of
skill growth.

47. A school introduces inclusive education for children with disabilities. The primary rationale is
that:

   A. children with disabilities should always be separated
   B. many children benefit from access to the general education environment with support
   C. academic standards should be removed entirely

 D. learning problems are caused only by teachers
       Answer: B. many children benefit from access to the general education environment with
support
   Rationale: Inclusive education aims to provide appropriate support while allowing many
children with disabilities to learn in regular educational contexts.

48. Which statement about bullying in middle childhood is most accurate?
   A. Bullying always involves physical aggression only.
   B. Bullying can include physical, verbal, relational, and now digital forms.
   C. Bullying has no relation to adjustment.

 D. Bullying is best explained by one single cause.
       Answer: B. Bullying can include physical, verbal, relational, and now digital forms.
   Rationale: Bullying is multidimensional and may involve direct aggression, social exclusion,
verbal attacks, or online harassment.

49. A child who adapts flexibly and effectively under stress is showing:
   A. fixation
   B. resilience
   C. egocentrism

 D. role confusion
       Answer: B. resilience
   Rationale: Resilience refers to positive adaptation despite stress or adversity.

50. Which family factor is most likely to support positive adjustment in middle childhood?
   A. chronic unresolved family conflict
   B. inconsistent caregiving and harsh rejection
   C. warm structure and predictable routines
 D. total absence of parental monitoring
       Answer: C. warm structure and predictable routines
   Rationale: Children in middle childhood generally benefit from warmth, stability, and
reasonable structure in family life.

51. Which situation best illustrates the influence of pubertal timing?
   A. A child learns to conserve number at age 7.
   B. An adolescent girl who matures earlier than peers faces unique social pressures.
   C. A toddler begins to use two-word utterances.

 D. An older adult experiences presbyopia.
       Answer: B. An adolescent girl who matures earlier than peers faces unique social
pressures.
   Rationale: Pubertal timing matters because early or late maturation can affect social
expectations, self-image, and adjustment.

52. Which statement best reflects current knowledge of the adolescent brain?
   A. Brain development is complete by puberty.
   B. Development of reward and control systems contributes to heightened risk-taking in some

contexts.
   C. The adolescent brain cannot support logical thinking.

 D. Brain maturation has no relation to emotion.
       Answer: B. Development of reward and control systems contributes to heightened
risk-taking in some contexts.
   Rationale: Adolescent risk-taking is partly linked to asynchronous brain development
involving motivational and regulatory systems.

53. Which adolescent belief best illustrates the personal fable?
   A. "My parents sometimes make mistakes."
   B. "My feelings are unique, and bad things won't happen to me."
   C. "People have different political views."

 D. "Teachers use grades to evaluate performance."
       Answer: B. "My feelings are unique, and bad things won't happen to me."
   Rationale: The personal fable includes a sense of uniqueness and invulnerability common in
adolescent egocentrism.

54. Which behavior is the clearest sign of formal operational reasoning?
   A. sorting objects only by visible characteristics
   B. solving a pendulum problem by systematically varying one factor at a time
   C. assuming taller containers always hold more

 D. using trial and error without planning
       Answer: B. solving a pendulum problem by systematically varying one factor at a time
   Rationale: Formal operational thought supports systematic hypothesis testing and control of
variables.
55. An adolescent argues that stealing medicine may be justified to save a life because human
welfare outweighs strict rule obedience. This reasoning is best classified as:

   A. preconventional only
   B. conventional rule conformity only
   C. postconventional moral reasoning

 D. premoral impulsivity
       Answer: C. postconventional moral reasoning
   Rationale: Postconventional reasoning evaluates rules in light of broader ethical principles
such as human welfare and justice.

56. Which statement about adolescent schooling is most accurate?
   A. Academic achievement is unrelated to self-efficacy.
   B. School engagement is influenced by family, peers, expectations, and opportunity

structures.
   C. Dropping out is caused only by low intelligence.

 D. Vocational planning is irrelevant during adolescence.
       Answer: B. School engagement is influenced by family, peers, expectations, and
opportunity structures.
   Rationale: Adolescent academic adjustment is shaped by multiple contextual and
motivational factors, not by ability alone.

57. A teenager repeatedly sends sexually explicit messages and images through a phone. This
behavior is best termed:

   A. individuation
   B. sexting
   C. foreclosure

 D. parallel play
       Answer: B. sexting
   Rationale: Sexting refers to sending sexually explicit messages or images electronically.

58. Which adolescent is showing identity achievement?
   A. one who avoids exploration and commitment
   B. one who adopts parental choices automatically
   C. one who has explored alternatives and made commitments

 D. one who is still actively undecided after extensive exploration
       Answer: C. one who has explored alternatives and made commitments
   Rationale: Identity achievement combines prior exploration with subsequent commitment.

59. A clinician notes that an adolescent's sense of self is strongly shaped by ethnic background,
migration experience, and peer acceptance. This observation is most directly relevant to:

   A. object permanence
   B. identity development in context
   C. operant conditioning only
   D. neonatal adjustment
  Answer: B. identity development in context

   Rationale: Adolescent identity is shaped by social location, cultural background, migration,
and peer dynamics.

60. Which statement about peer influence in adolescence is most accurate?
   A. Peer influence is uniformly harmful.
   B. Peer relationships can support both risk behavior and positive development.
   C. Family influence disappears once peers become important.

 D. Adolescents cannot resist peer norms.
       Answer: B. Peer relationships can support both risk behavior and positive development.
   Rationale: Peers can encourage delinquency or risky behavior, but they can also support
belonging, identity, and prosocial growth.

61. The idea that emerging adults often feel "in-between," neither fully adolescent nor fully adult,
is most closely associated with:

   A. industry versus inferiority
   B. Arnett's concept of emerging adulthood
   C. disengagement theory

 D. behavior genetics
       Answer: B. Arnett's concept of emerging adulthood
   Rationale: Arnett described emerging adulthood as a distinct period marked by exploration,
instability, and feeling in-between.

62. Which situation best illustrates reflective thinking in early adulthood?
   A. A person insists that every problem has one absolute answer.
   B. A person weighs evidence, context, and competing values before making a decision.
   C. A person can only solve problems with concrete materials present.

 D. A person relies purely on authority without evaluation.
       Answer: B. A person weighs evidence, context, and competing values before making a
decision.
   Rationale: Reflective thinking involves evaluating uncertainty, context, evidence, and multiple
perspectives rather than accepting simple absolutes.

63. Sternberg's concept of practical intelligence is best illustrated by:
   A. quickly memorizing a poem word for word
   B. knowing how to handle real-life work demands effectively
   C. scoring perfectly on a vocabulary quiz only

 D. repeating an expert's instructions without understanding
       Answer: B. knowing how to handle real-life work demands effectively
   Rationale: Practical intelligence refers to adaptive know-how in everyday or occupational
settings.

64. Which statement about health in emerging adulthood is most accurate?
   A. Health is determined only by genes.
   B. Lifestyle choices and social conditions strongly influence health outcomes.
   C. Mental health problems rarely emerge in this period.

 D. Preventive behavior has little long-term value.
       Answer: B. Lifestyle choices and social conditions strongly influence health outcomes.
   Rationale: Health in emerging adulthood is shaped by behavior, access to care, relationships,
stress, and broader social conditions as well as genetics.

65. A young adult who is legally married but still depends heavily on parents for daily decisions
may be described as having achieved adult status in:

   A. biological terms only
   B. social role terms but not full psychological independence
   C. neither social nor psychological terms

 D. cognitive terms only
       Answer: B. social role terms but not full psychological independence
   Rationale: Adult status can be uneven; a person may meet some social markers of adulthood
while remaining dependent in decision making.

66. According to the triangular theory of love, consummate love includes:
   A. intimacy only
   B. passion only
   C. commitment only

 D. intimacy, passion, and commitment
       Answer: D. intimacy, passion, and commitment
   Rationale: Consummate love, in Sternberg's model, includes all three components: intimacy,
passion, and commitment.

67. Which statement about cohabitation is most accurate?
   A. It has identical meaning across cultures and individuals.
   B. It may function as a trial marriage, an alternative to marriage, or a pragmatic arrangement.
   C. It is always unrelated to later relationship quality.

 D. It is legally and psychologically identical to marriage in all respects.
       Answer: B. It may function as a trial marriage, an alternative to marriage, or a pragmatic
arrangement.
   Rationale: Cohabitation serves varied functions depending on values, goals, economics, and
social context.

68. Which factor most strongly supports adaptation to parenthood?
   A. rigid expectations and poor communication
   B. adequate support, shared roles, and realistic expectations
   C. total isolation from kin

 D. avoiding all routine structure
       Answer: B. adequate support, shared roles, and realistic expectations
   Rationale: Parenthood is easier to navigate when adults have social support, flexible role
sharing, and realistic views of demands.
69. Which statement best reflects cognitive development in middle adulthood?
   A. All abilities decline uniformly beginning at age 40.
   B. Many adults show stability or gains in knowledge-based performance despite slower

processing in some tasks.
   C. Creativity disappears by midlife.

 D. Expertise has no role in adult cognition.
       Answer: B. Many adults show stability or gains in knowledge-based performance despite
slower processing in some tasks.
   Rationale: Midlife cognition often reflects a mixed pattern, with slower speed in some
domains but maintained or strengthened expertise and knowledge.

70. Which example best illustrates integrative thought?
   A. viewing issues in rigid either-or categories
   B. recognizing that multiple truths can coexist and must be balanced
   C. relying only on rapid processing speed

 D. rejecting emotional information in reasoning
       Answer: B. recognizing that multiple truths can coexist and must be balanced
   Rationale: Integrative thought involves synthesizing contradictions, context, and competing
perspectives.

71. A 48-year-old adult begins mentoring younger coworkers and finds this deeply meaningful.
This most strongly reflects:

   A. stagnation
   B. generativity
   C. despair

 D. diffusion
       Answer: B. generativity
   Rationale: Mentoring younger adults and contributing to future generations are core
expressions of generativity in middle adulthood.

72. Which statement about menopause is most accurate?
   A. It is best understood only as pathology.
   B. Its meaning and experience are shaped partly by biological, cultural, and personal factors.
   C. It occurs identically in all women.

 D. It eliminates all sexual interest permanently.
       Answer: B. Its meaning and experience are shaped partly by biological, cultural, and
personal factors.
   Rationale: Menopause is a biological transition, but symptoms, meaning, and adjustment vary
with culture, expectations, and personal context.

73. Which situation best illustrates the timing-of-events model in adult development?
   A. A toddler learns to walk at 13 months.
   B. A 52-year-old experiences stress after becoming a first-time parent much later than peers.
   C. A child develops object permanence.

 D. A fetus responds to sound.
       Answer: B. A 52-year-old experiences stress after becoming a first-time parent much later
than peers.
   Rationale: The timing-of-events model emphasizes how the timing of major life events relative
to social norms affects adaptation.

74. A midlife adult who balances work, adolescent children, and care for an aging parent is most
likely dealing with:

   A. identity diffusion
   B. the social convoy only
   C. overlapping family role demands

 D. neonatal transition
       Answer: C. overlapping family role demands
   Rationale: Midlife adults often face simultaneous responsibilities to children and aging
parents, creating overlapping role demands.

75. Which statement best reflects a strength of trait models in adulthood?
   A. They explain all life events completely.
   B. They help describe patterns of personality continuity and gradual change.
   C. They show that personality stops changing after adolescence.

 D. They deny any role for context.
       Answer: B. They help describe patterns of personality continuity and gradual change.
   Rationale: Trait models are useful for describing how stable personality tendencies can
persist while still changing gradually across adulthood.

76. Which factor is most associated with positive adaptation in later adulthood?
   A. complete social withdrawal
   B. maintenance of meaningful activity and supportive relationships
   C. exclusive dependence on others for all decisions

 D. rejection of continuity with past identity
       Answer: B. maintenance of meaningful activity and supportive relationships
   Rationale: Later-life adaptation is often promoted by engagement, purpose, and emotionally
supportive social ties.

77. Which statement about life expectancy is most accurate?
   A. It is determined solely by biological aging.
   B. It is influenced by genetics, health behavior, environment, and access to care.
   C. It is identical across all social groups.

 D. It is unrelated to public health conditions.
       Answer: B. It is influenced by genetics, health behavior, environment, and access to care.
   Rationale: Life expectancy reflects multiple interacting influences including biology, lifestyle,
public health, and medical access.
78. A healthy older adult who uses calendars, lists, and structured routines to compensate for
mild memory decline is demonstrating:

   A. tertiary circular reactions
   B. compensation in adaptation to aging
   C. identity foreclosure

 D. animistic thought
       Answer: B. compensation in adaptation to aging
   Rationale: Using external aids such as lists and calendars is a compensatory strategy that
supports functioning despite mild decline.

79. Which cognitive change is most typical of normal late adulthood?
   A. total loss of semantic memory
   B. some slowing in processing speed with relative preservation of accumulated knowledge
   C. disappearance of language comprehension

 D. inability to learn anything new
       Answer: B. some slowing in processing speed with relative preservation of accumulated
knowledge
   Rationale: Normal aging often involves slower processing while semantic knowledge and
many learned abilities remain comparatively strong.

80. Which statement best reflects socioemotional selectivity in later life?
   A. Older adults always enlarge their social networks.
   B. Older adults may prioritize emotionally meaningful relationships over numerous casual ties.
   C. Emotional goals become less important with age.

 D. Relationship quality matters less than quantity.
       Answer: B. Older adults may prioritize emotionally meaningful relationships over
numerous casual ties.
   Rationale: Socioemotional selectivity theory proposes that as time is perceived as limited,
emotionally rewarding relationships are prioritized.

81. Which situation best illustrates ego integrity?
   A. an older adult feels life was wasted and cannot accept past choices
   B. an older adult reviews life with acceptance, including regrets and accomplishments
   C. an older adult refuses all reflection on the past

 D. an older adult becomes dependent on magical thinking
       Answer: B. an older adult reviews life with acceptance, including regrets and
accomplishments
   Rationale: Ego integrity involves accepting one's life as meaningful and coherent, even while
acknowledging imperfections.

82. Which statement about retirement is most accurate?
   A. Retirement affects everyone the same way.
   B. Adjustment to retirement depends on health, finances, identity, and voluntariness of the

transition.
   C. Retirement always improves well-being immediately.

 D. Retirement automatically causes depression.
       Answer: B. Adjustment to retirement depends on health, finances, identity, and
voluntariness of the transition.
   Rationale: Retirement is not one uniform experience; its effects depend on resources,
meaning, and whether it is chosen or forced.

83. A family discusses whether to continue aggressive treatment for a dying relative with
irreversible illness. Which issue is most central?

   A. emergent literacy
   B. end-of-life decision making
   C. social referencing

 D. transitive inference
       Answer: B. end-of-life decision making
   Rationale: Decisions about continuing or stopping aggressive treatment in irreversible illness
are central end-of-life ethical issues.

84. Which statement about bereavement is most accurate?
   A. Grief responses are identical across all losses.
   B. Bereavement includes both emotional response and adjustment to loss over time.
   C. Mourning is unrelated to culture.

 D. Grief is abnormal if it lasts more than one month.
       Answer: B. Bereavement includes both emotional response and adjustment to loss over
time.
   Rationale: Bereavement refers broadly to the condition of having lost someone and the longer
process of adapting, whereas grief is the emotional response.

85. Which loss is especially likely to involve disenfranchised grief because others may minimize
it?

   A. failing an exam
   B. miscarriage
   C. graduating from school

 D. changing jobs voluntarily
       Answer: B. miscarriage
   Rationale: Miscarriage is often socially minimized, which can make the grief less recognized
and therefore disenfranchised.

86. Which statement about near-death experiences is most accurate?
   A. They prove a single religious interpretation.
   B. They are reported by some people close to death, but interpretation remains debated.
   C. They occur in every dying person.

 D. They have no psychological significance.
       Answer: B. They are reported by some people close to death, but interpretation remains
debated.
   Rationale: Near-death experiences are reported by some individuals, but their meaning and
causes remain open to differing interpretations.

87. A psychologist is asked by a school to release a student's raw test responses and notes
directly to a teacher for classroom curiosity. Under ethical standards, the best response is to:

   A. release all materials because the teacher works with the child
   B. release raw data only if the teacher promises confidentiality
   C. refuse release because raw test data should not be given to unauthorized persons without
proper basis

 D. post a summary in the faculty group chat instead
       Answer: C. refuse release because raw test data should not be given to unauthorized
persons without proper basis
   Rationale: Ethical assessment standards protect raw test data from release to unauthorized
persons; teachers may receive explained results but not unrestricted raw materials or notes.

88. A psychometrician is assigned to administer an assessment in a language the examinee
barely understands. The most ethical action is to:

   A. proceed because standardized instructions must never be adjusted
   B. administer the tool anyway and omit concerns in the report
   C. use an assessment appropriate to the client's language and characteristics or recommend
proper referral

 D. ask a relative to translate sensitive items without safeguards
       Answer: C. use an assessment appropriate to the client's language and characteristics or
recommend proper referral
   Rationale: Assessment tools must be appropriate to the client's language and relevant
characteristics; otherwise validity and fairness are compromised.

89. A supervising psychologist delegates testing tasks to a psychometrician. Which condition is
ethically required?

   A. Delegated work may exceed the subordinate's competence if the clinic is busy.
   B. Clients must be informed that delegated tasks are being performed and may choose to
continue or reschedule.
   C. Supervision is optional when standardized tests are used.

 D. The psychometrician may independently practice psychotherapy if rapport is established.
       Answer: B. Clients must be informed that delegated tasks are being performed and may
choose to continue or reschedule.
   Rationale: Ethical delegation requires competence, adequate supervision, and informing
clients that tasks are delegated, including giving them a choice.

90. During teleassessment, an examinee repeatedly loses internet connection in a timed test.
The most ethical response is to:

   A. ignore the issue because technology problems are the client's responsibility
   B. interpret the scores as fully valid without qualification
   C. explain the implications of poor connectivity and consider its effect on performance and
interpretation

 D. advise the client to guess quickly to finish on time
       Answer: C. explain the implications of poor connectivity and consider its effect on
performance and interpretation
   Rationale: Teleassessment standards require informing test takers that unstable connectivity
can affect performance, especially on timed tests, and this must be considered in interpretation.

91. A psychometrician is asked to interpret obsolete test results from several years ago to make
a current placement recommendation. Ethical standards require the practitioner to:

   A. interpret the results as current if no better data exist
   B. avoid basing conclusions on outdated results
   C. rely on old results if the client agrees

 D. convert the old scores into percentile ranks manually
       Answer: B. avoid basing conclusions on outdated results
   Rationale: Ethical standards state that interpretations, conclusions, and recommendations
should not be based on outdated test results.

92. A practitioner wants to use photocopied answer sheets and test plates from a copyrighted
instrument to save money. The most ethical action is to:

   A. proceed if the copies are clear
   B. use only original test materials
   C. use photocopies only for high-IQ clients

 D. post scans online for peer consultation
       Answer: B. use only original test materials
   Rationale: The ethics code requires using only original copies of test materials, not
photocopies, to protect legality, standardization, and security.

93. Under RA 10029-linked boundaries, which task is most appropriate for a psychometrician?
   A. independently conducting psychotherapy
   B. prescribing psychotropic medication
   C. administering and scoring psychological tests within lawful scope and supervision

requirements

 D. issuing medical diagnoses
       Answer: C. administering and scoring psychological tests within lawful scope and
supervision requirements
   Rationale: RA 10029-linked practice boundaries allow psychometricians to perform
psychometric functions within legal scope, unlike psychotherapy, prescribing, or medical
diagnosis.

94. A psychologist learns that an organization wants to use an assessment report for a purpose
different from the original referral. Ethically, the psychologist should first consider:

   A. whether the new use is authorized and within the limits originally clarified
   B. whether the organization is influential
   C. whether the report can be made more dramatic

 D. whether the client will probably never know
       Answer: A. whether the new use is authorized and within the limits originally clarified
   Rationale: When report use changes, the practitioner must revisit who the client is, intended
uses, access, and limits of confidentiality before permitting a different use.

95. A practitioner starts dating the sibling of a current therapy client. Which ethical concern is
most directly raised?

   A. random assignment
   B. multiple relationship risk
   C. sensory adaptation

 D. natural selection
       Answer: B. multiple relationship risk
   Rationale: A romantic relationship with someone closely associated with a current client can
create a multiple relationship that risks impaired objectivity or harm.

96. A practitioner who is exhausted, irritable, and unable to focus begins making errors in case
work. Which ethical principle is most directly implicated?

   A. duty to ignore personal issues and continue working
   B. obligation to monitor personal problems and seek help if competence is affected
   C. requirement to avoid all CPD activities

 D. rule that emotions should never be acknowledged
       Answer: B. obligation to monitor personal problems and seek help if competence is
affected
   Rationale: The code requires practitioners to monitor personal problems and take action such
as consultation, assistance, or limiting duties if competence is impaired.

97. A researcher studying adolescents obtains assent from participants but does not seek
parental permission even though the study involves more than minimal risk and the participants
are minors. The main ethical problem is failure to:

   A. use a longitudinal design
   B. secure appropriate informed consent protections
   C. randomize participants equally

 D. standardize the interview questions
       Answer: B. secure appropriate informed consent protections
   Rationale: Research with minors, especially beyond minimal risk, requires proper informed
consent procedures, including parental permission and child assent when appropriate.

98. Which public statement by a psychology practitioner is most ethical?
   A. "Guaranteed cure for depression in three sessions."
   B. "Licensed practitioner offering assessment and consultation within stated competencies."
   C. "Best psychologist in the city, with perfect success rate."
   D. "Expert in every area of psychology."
  Answer: B. "Licensed practitioner offering assessment and consultation within stated

competencies."
   Rationale: Ethical public statements must be accurate, nondeceptive, and limited to genuine

qualifications and services.

99. A practitioner becomes aware of a colleague's serious ethical violation likely to cause
substantial harm. Which response is most consistent with the code?

   A. remain silent because reporting is disloyal
   B. report the violation to appropriate authorities if informal resolution is insufficient and
confidentiality is not improperly breached
   C. post anonymous accusations online

 D. confront the colleague violently to stop the behavior
       Answer: B. report the violation to appropriate authorities if informal resolution is insufficient
and confidentiality is not improperly breached
   Rationale: When a likely serious ethical violation may cause substantial harm, the code
supports further reporting to appropriate authorities if informal action is not enough and
confidentiality is respected.

100. A PRC-level board item in developmental psychology is strongest when it:
    A. depends mainly on trivial memorization of isolated facts
    B. contains multiple equally correct answers
    C. integrates developmental concepts with applied reasoning and ethical judgment

 D. uses implausible distractors to make the item easy
        Answer: C. integrates developmental concepts with applied reasoning and ethical
judgment
    Rationale: High-quality licensure items assess not only knowledge of developmental
concepts but also application, analysis, and professional judgment.
